# alpha.15 → beta.1 gap adjudication

Date: 2026-07-05 · Status: **complete** — machine adjudication plus
owner-position re-examination (both 2026-07-05). Final scope calls rest with
the owner: each re-examined position carries open questions only the owner can
close (§Owner-position re-examination, end of report). No design edits have
been applied.

Adjudicates every entry of the consolidated
[gap report](../../0.1.0-beta.1-alpha15-gap-report.md) — 126 gaps in 16
sections — into one of three dispositions, with the
[design history](../../../design-history/memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md)
as precedent evidence and the
[requirements charter](../../0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md) as the spec.

**Method.** 18 adjudicator agents (one per section, large sections split), each
verifying recording-status claims against the governing corpus and grepping the
design history for the failure that earned each alpha position. Ground rule set
by the owner: **ADRs are reference, never a justification** — an ADR number is
a search key into the reasoning; only the underlying documented failure,
mechanism, or charter requirement can justify a disposition. Every disposition
was then adversarially verified: a 3-lens skeptic panel (already-recorded /
precedent / charter-fit) on each needs-change finding with majority-refute
downgrade; an evidence-only skeptic on each record finding; a citation audit on
every leave finding (a citation passes only if it *adjudicates* the delta —
decision plus rationale — not merely mentions it). 9 dispositions were
overturned by verification; 1 survived contested.

**How to read a disposition:**

- **LEAVE — deliberate and recorded**: the delta is adjudicated in an
  authoritative record (design §11/§13/§15–§18 or body decision-with-rationale,
  regression-review resolution, docs-history borrow/adapt/reject, or a charter
  Deliberate Exclusion), citation verified.
- **RECORD — sound but unrecorded**: defensible on the merits but no
  authoritative record adjudicates it; the entry carries paste-ready recording
  text and a target location (usually the design §11 divergence list).
  *Applying these 38 recordings to the design doc is a follow-up task, not
  performed by this report.*
- **CHANGE — needs design change**: the delta re-opens a documented alpha-line
  failure unaddressed, drops a load-bearing invariant without replacement, or
  contradicts the charter; the entry carries the minimal concrete change.

## Headline

| Disposition | Count |
|---|---|
| LEAVE — deliberate and recorded | 87 |
| RECORD — sound but unrecorded | 38 |
| CHANGE — needs design change | 1 |
| **Total** | **126** |

Verification: 9 overturned (8 leave→record on failed citation audits, 1
change→record), 1 contested, 0 unverified.

**The one machine-confirmed CHANGE — S3.5 (identity):** restore a stable
machine identity (ULID/`work_id`-class) as the primary key for works and all
internal references, with `citekey` demoted to a pinned human-facing alias; a
citekey correction updates the alias and may rename the directory as
presentation, but never changes identity. Contested 1-of-3 skeptics — but the
question is closed regardless: **owner ruling R-1 (2026-07-05, hard ruling)**
decides it on the same grounds, with a concrete failure case (Zotero re-exports
the same work under a new citekey when metadata changes; beta.1's own
`zotero_key` idempotency store concedes the primary key is mutable).

## After re-examination — recommended dispositions

The re-examination pass (12 position agents, each verdict attacked by an
opposite-side skeptic; all 12 survived) amends the machine dispositions **as
recommendations**:

| Disposition | Machine | Recommended after re-exam |
|---|---|---|
| LEAVE | 87 | 85 |
| RECORD | 38 | 33 |
| CHANGE | 1 | 8 |

The eight recommended CHANGE entries: **S3.5** (stable identity — ruled, R-1);
**S3.2 + S2.3 + S10.2** (hub returns as a minimal researcher-created editorial
concept with a machine-candidates block — R-2/R-5, the hard "every digest→hub"
mandate not upheld); **S5.4** (foreign-change detection + graph-integrity
sweep restored; universal withhold-quarantine not upheld — R-3); **S3.1**
(normative per-class contract table in §3, including the project.md Concept
contract the export gate already presupposes — R-6/R-12); **S2.1**
(Memoria-born vault, never nested in an existing one — R-8, upheld outright);
**S13.3** (footprint-limited rollback + explicit interrupted-run recovery —
R-19, whose premise the history corrected: the alpha line had cross-store 2PC,
not 2PL). Five-plus RECORD entries get amended recording text (S2.5 .bib
never-local-only; S3.7 with a pre-registered revive trigger; S6.3/S9.2/S9.11
under the two-stage enrichment frame; S6.4/S9.14 Semantic Scholar wording +
deferred allowlist entry).

## Coherence notes

The automated coherence agent could not run (session limits); this check was
performed manually over the full disposition map, targeting the
duplicate-substance clusters:

1. **Identity (S3.5 × S7.2)** — the one real tension: S3.5's CHANGE (restore
   stable identity) and S7.2's RECORD (book citekey-as-primary-key as a sound
   divergence) cannot both be applied. Resolved by ruling R-1: S3.5 governs;
   do **not** apply S7.2's recording text as written.
2. **Hub (S2.3, S3.2, S10.2)** — consistent (all RECORD); the citation audit
   independently confirmed the hub drop is *silent* in the design corpus —
   every claimed adjudication was a passing mention, not a decision.
3. **Steering/Librarian (S8.3, S11.2, S15.3)** — consistent; owner-endorsed.
4. **Enrichment/providers (S6.3, S6.4, S9.1, S9.2, S9.9, S9.11, S9.14)** —
   consistent (all RECORD); all governed by R-15/R-17 re-exam.
5. **Argument graph (S3.3, S3.4, S3.6, S8.1)** — no contradiction: the graph
   *deferral* is recorded (LEAVE entries), while two of its substrate drops
   (claim mode, typed links) are individually silent (RECORD entries).
6. Per-section counts match the gap report exactly; no missing ids.

## Caveats

- Two runs were required (session limits); the second run re-verified live and
  flipped two entries relative to the first (S3.5 record→change,
  S10.5 change→record) — the report reflects the second, fully-verified run,
  and S10.5's recording action still corrects the §11 convergence misfiling.
- Proposed recording texts are drafts for the design owner, not applied edits.
- Re-examination verdicts are recommendations, not applied edits: each carries
  open questions only the owner can close, and several proposed changes merge
  on the same design location (S3.1 via R-6 and R-12; S2.3 via R-2 and R-5).

---
## 1. Host / runtime / distribution

10 gaps — leave 9 · record 1 · change 0

### S1.1 — Obsidian plugin returns as the required researcher UI

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The delta is adjudicated in two authoritative records I verified: design §16's first bullet ('ADR obligation, named') states the host decision amends ADR-125/ADR-130, requires that ADR before implementation begins, and keeps docs/reference/obsidian-plugins.md unchanged so the proposal is 'not product truth'; design §11 item (10) records the host decision as new alpha.16 scope. The alpha.14 removal was scope discipline plus the keep-test, not a plugin-failure incident, and beta.1 preserves the keep-test substance: charter Success Claim 4, no-plugin floors on every surface except Ask (§1/§16), mobile as keep-test mode, and the plugin inheriting ADR-121's enqueue-only rule (§2: 'nothing in the plugin writes machine content').

- **Recorded:** design.md §16 'ADR obligation, named' (L1152-1158) + §11 item (10) (L987-991); regression review buckets it as recorded (L78-81)
- **History:** Alpha.14 cut the .obsidian tree because 'the product must remain fully operable if the editor is only vim, nano, or a file browser' (history L1930, PR #1124) and alpha.15's Scope Boundary plus PR #1203 fenced editor adapters behind their own ADR (history L2216) — scope and keep-test reasons, not a documented plugin failure. Beta.1 addresses both: the keep-test survives as charter Claim 4 with per-surface no-plugin floors, and the ADR fence is honored by §16's named ADR obligation.

### S1.2 — On-demand serve promoted to plugin-supervised resident two-process daemon with in-daemon scheduling

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Residency, plugin supervision, and the supervisor/worker split are explicit decisions-with-rationale in the design body: §1 L51-65 (compute out of Electron for crash isolation and one network choke point; parent-death watch; crash-loop give-up), §16 'LSP lifecycle, verbatim' with its evidence base (Smart Connections' in-Electron 500MB index/hangs as the failure archetype), and §11 item (10) naming 'plugin + local daemon' as the recorded host decision under the §16 ADR obligation. The scheduling move is governed too: §2's operational contract is the docs-history 'memoriad job contract' borrow (an adjudicated recorded decision), and the always-on citation monitor rides §17 item 4 plus the charter's amended discovery exclusion (2026-07-03). Beta.1 addresses each reason alpha held the no-daemon line: the daemon is session-scoped (dies with Obsidian), the consumption-guard family is intact per the regression sweep, and heartbeat-on-success plus bounded retries directly answer the silent-cron-failure risk.

- **Recorded:** design.md §1 (L51-65), §2 operational contract (L170-186), §16 LSP bullet (L1172-1177), §11 item (10) (L987-991), §17 item 4 (L1253-1257); requirements.md Deliberate Exclusions amendment (L84); docs-history Borrow 'memoriad job contract' (L34)
- **History:** The no-daemon stance was earned by shedding Hermes weight — ADR-125's goal 'one install command, no external runtime, no always-on process' (history L2190, L2304) — plus ADR-127 rejecting the watcher-as-required-daemon while keeping 'guard never retired' (L2186), and ADR-95's unattended loop rejected as 'conflicts with no-daemon arch' (L2233) with silent cron failure and inbox flooding the named risks (L547). Beta.1 addresses all three: one artifact with no separate always-on install unit, the guard family verified intact, heartbeat rows as the silent-non-execution detector, and review-queue back-pressure bounding flood.

### S1.3 — CLI demoted from product surface to survival floor; mem ask dropped

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The drop is explicitly ruled with rationale in the design body: §1 L89-93 ('No mem ask — Ask is a judgment surface with no survival role, and the keep-test answer is stock-Obsidian navigability, not a CLI') and §16's 'Two rich panes, floors everywhere' bullet restating that Ask alone has no floor 'by §1's own ruling'; the demotion itself rides the recorded §11 item (10) host decision. ADR-72's underlying failure — routine actions reachable only through an LLM round-trip with the Co-PI — is not re-opened: the plugin panes are direct, non-agent-mediated PI surfaces, so PI-direct-access is honored by a different mechanism. ADR-130's 'no-daemon recovery surface' role is kept in substance by the mem survival floor (serve/capture/export/rebuild/backup/restore/migrate/revert-run), installed by construction wherever the daemon runs (§16 'One artifact').

- **Recorded:** design.md §1 (L89-93) + §16 'Two rich panes, floors everywhere' (L1178-1183), riding §11 item (10) (L987-991)
- **History:** ADR-72 was earned by 'some actions were reachable only by asking the Co-PI... making routine actions depend on an LLM round-trip' (history L779) — an anti-agent-mediation principle, not a pro-CLI one; ADR-122 had already held 'CLI is inspect/verify/administer only, not a PI action surface' when Obsidian was the UI (L1896); alpha.14/15 made the CLI the direct-access product surface only because Obsidian was dropped (L2188). Beta.1 restores the direct-access surface to the plugin, so the reason the CLI was promoted no longer applies, and ADR-72's principle is honored by the plugin.

### S1.4 — Plugin distribution + consented binary acquisition story added (catalog-clean, code-signed)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The mechanics are adjudicated in design §16 itself, an authoritative record: 'Acquisition is consented, never bundled' with the named evidence base (rust-analyzer's explicit-consent download, vscode-ripgrep's retreat from postinstall downloads, the community catalog's three-asset limit and May-2026 scanning regime), the catalog-clean/desktop-only plugin bullet, Windows code-signing with its SmartScreen rationale, and recorded flip conditions (package-manager-only if consented downloads get banned; signing-untenable fallback). The alpha installers' 'install no Obsidian plugin' stance was a consequence of the alpha.14 host cut, not an acquisition-failure incident, so re-introducing a distribution story under the recorded host decision re-opens nothing.

- **Recorded:** design.md §16 'Acquisition is consented, never bundled' (L1163-1171), catalog-clean bullet (L1184-1191), flip conditions (L1222-1232)
- **History:** Alpha.14/15's installer requirement 'Install no Obsidian plugin. Install no Hermes profiles. Require no Zotero setup' (history L2022) followed from dropping Obsidian as a required surface (PR #1124, L1930), not from any distribution failure; code-signing has no alpha-line precedent at all. Beta.1's mechanics are new evidence-based design constrained by the re-homed packaging discipline (checksum pinning echoes ADR-76's SHA256-pinned wheel), with the removal reason (host cut) superseded by the recorded host decision.

### S1.5 — Distribution artifact changes class: Python package + per-vault venv to self-contained static binary with bundled models

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The delta is sound on the merits: the charter's ≤30-minute clean-machine install bar and hash-pinned bundled-model supply-chain row, plus §16's acquisition story (winget/brew and the rust-analyzer consented-download model presuppose a self-contained artifact), all require it, and removing Node/qmd completes what alpha.15 itself earmarked (§11 records FTS5+sqlite-vec as convergence). But no record adjudicates the reversal of ADR-125's pinned Python 3.12 + uv-tool + per-vault-venv stack as such — §11's divergence list omits it, §16's recorded rationale covers plugin+daemon+acquisition rather than the stack class, and the only design-body traces are presuppositions (§7's pdfium bullet 'matching the single-static-binary install; PyMuPDF's AGPL + Python contradicted it'). Per the calibration rule, 'amends ADR-125' without the recorded rationale covering this half is not a leave.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (fragments at design §7 L633-636 and §16 L1159-1171 presuppose the binary but never adjudicate the stack-class change)
- **History:** The alpha line was Python-shaped by stack pragmatics, never failure-earned against binaries: ADR-76's wheel was recast because a wheel 'cannot carry SOUL.md/plugin.yaml/crons' (history L989) — a problem that dissolved when ADR-125 made operations product code — and ADR-125 then pinned Python 3.12 + uv tool install as the runtime (L2096, L2190). Beta.1 keeps the surviving disciplines (checksum pinning, one artifact, one-command install) while changing the artifact class, so no documented failure is re-opened; only the recording is missing.
- **Action:** Add to design §11's divergence list (after item (10)): "(11) the distribution artifact — beta.1 ships mem as a single self-contained static binary with installer-bundled hash-pinned ONNX models, superseding ADR-125's Python 3.12 + uv-tool + per-vault-venv stack pin. Forced by the §16 acquisition story (winget/brew and the rust-analyzer consented-download model presuppose a self-contained artifact), the charter's ≤30-minute clean-machine install and bundled-model supply-chain rows, and FTS5+sqlite-vec completing alpha.15's own earmarked removal of the qmd/Node dependency. The §16 host ADR must cover this stack amendment explicitly, not only the plugin+daemon shape."

### S1.6 — Beta.1 fills the host-decision slot alpha.15 explicitly reserved for a later version

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is the most directly recorded delta in the section: design §11 item (10) names the host decision as new alpha.16 scope that alpha.15 'anticipates but does not yet center', and §16's 'ADR obligation, named' bullet honors alpha's fence in its own terms — the decision amends ADR-125/ADR-130, requires its ADR before implementation begins, and remains 'a proposal, not product truth' until that ADR lands. The framing tension the gap report notes ('back-pressure' vs 're-introduction') is wording, not governance: the fence alpha.15 erected (adapters need their own ADR) is precisely the obligation §16 carries forward, so the reserved slot is filled by the sanctioned mechanism rather than around it.

- **Recorded:** design.md §11 item (10) (L987-991) + §16 'ADR obligation, named' (L1152-1158)
- **History:** PR #1203 made future editor adapters 'require their own ADR rather than inheriting an alpha.15 commitment' and the Scope Boundary ruled 'alpha.15 cannot close with Obsidian plugin implementation counted as release scope' (history L2216); the daemon half was fenced by ADR-127's watcher-as-required-daemon rejection (L2186). Beta.1 addresses the fence's purpose — decision authority before implementation — by naming the ADR obligation and keeping the current-state docs unchanged until it lands.

### S1.7 — Write-event push channel + lockstep plugin/daemon/CLI version handshake replace FS polling and the free-schema stance

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both halves are explicit decisions-with-rationale in the design body: the push channel in §1 L56-60 and §16 'Write-event push, not watcher faith' (Obsidian's watcher provably misses external writes; a stale check badge is an honesty-contract violation, not cosmetic), and the handshake in §2 L183-186 ('stale boundary code waves through what a newer runtime treats as mutating') reinforced by §15 (the lockstep handshake is load-bearing in the authored-chrome ruling) and standing negative deny-tests proving boundaries fire on the installed build. The handshake is additionally an adjudicated docs-history borrow ('Guard liveness + fail-closed contract'). Alpha's free-schema/no-handshake stance was not failure-earned — a single artifact made version skew structurally impossible — so making skew refusable when three components ship is the same invariant extended, not a reversal of an earned position.

- **Recorded:** design.md §1 (L56-61), §2 (L183-186), §16 'Write-event push, not watcher faith' (L1192-1195), §15 (L1080-1084); docs-history Borrow 'Guard liveness + fail-closed contract' (L35)
- **History:** serve --watch was stdlib polling kept deliberately on-demand so 'the worker remains the correctness boundary' and the guard is 'never retired' (ADR-127 Alternatives, history L2186); --json was transport 0 of the read-API with no second component to skew against (ADR-130, L2176). Beta.1 keeps the guard family intact (regression sweep) and adds push/handshake against two documented failure classes: Obsidian's watcher missing external writes (§16 evidence base) and the enforcement-theater pattern where deployed boundary code silently diverged from source (docs-history L144).

### S1.8 — VS Code second-client / host-portability design added (Appendix A)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Appendix A is itself the record: it opens 'Not scheduled work — recorded to show the §16 shape pays its M×N dividend', keeps binary acquisition to the single §16 story, and explicitly triggers §15's recorded flip condition — strict view-spec versioning plus capability negotiation before any second client ships, so a dropped badge cannot become a silent honesty violation (the Adaptive Cards lesson). It introduces no new write path, no second dialect, and no second distribution story, so nothing load-bearing is touched. Alpha's lack of a second client was an artifact of having no plugin host at all, not an earned position against one.

- **Recorded:** design.md Appendix A (L1314-1353) + §15 flip conditions (L1126-1130)
- **History:** ADR-130 established the view-spec contract ('clients render known kinds only', declarative verdict-carrying specs) with only CLI/MCP/HTTP marshalling clients (history L2176, L2182); no failure or decision ever weighed against a second client — it simply had no host. Appendix A extends the same ADR-130 contract and strengthens it with the capability-negotiation obligation §15 records as mandatory before launch.

### S1.9 — Binary renamed mem; daemon folded into mem serve with no separate memoriad executable

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §16's 'One artifact' bullet is an explicit decision-with-rationale: no separate memoriad means 'one distribution story, one version, and the CLI survival floor is by construction installed wherever the daemon runs', which Appendix A reinforces ('two distribution stories for one binary is how version skew starts'). The docs-history 'memoriad job contract' borrow is honored in substance, not dropped: its full content (idempotency keys, bounded retries, heartbeat-on-success, logs-only scheduled jobs) lands verbatim as §2's operational contract under the mem serve supervisor. The memoria name and a separate daemon executable were never failure-earned positions — alpha had no daemon executable at all.

- **Recorded:** design.md §16 'One artifact' (L1159-1162) + §2 operational contract (L170-186); docs-history Borrow 'memoriad job contract' (L34)
- **History:** Alpha's binary was memoria with serve as an on-demand subcommand (ADR-127 Alternatives, history L2186) and distribution as one uv-installed package (L2190); the name and single-artifact shape carried no incident history. The one risk a folded artifact could raise — component version skew — is the exact failure the §2 handshake and one-artifact rule close, consistent with the enforcement-theater lesson in the docs-history patterns (L144).

### S1.10 — Formal offline operating contract added (local surfaces work; LLM jobs queue and fail cleanly, never half-writing)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This addition is charter-mandated, not an ungoverned delta: the Required Product Scope 'Offline' row demands exactly this contract ('Reading, writing, catalog browsing, and local search work offline; paid engines queue or fail cleanly'), and design §1 L66-69 specifies it with its mechanism — the DB-persistent job queue and the §6 staged-write spine that makes never-half-writing structural. A15's silence was the absence of a requirement, not a position; the charter is the spec and an addition satisfying a required-scope row is governed by that row. The never-half-write property rests on the staging spine the regression review verified intact.

- **Recorded:** requirements.md Required Product Scope 'Offline' row (L35) + design.md §1 (L66-69, staged writes §6)
- **History:** None found as an earned alpha position — A15 simply ran local operations directly and let LLM-dependent operations fail offline, with no documented failure or decision behind the absence of a contract. The nearest precedent, cross-store recoverability and observable atomicity (ADR-127, history L2128), is the machinery beta.1's staged-write offline guarantee generalizes, so the alpha lineage is honored rather than reversed.
## 2. Vault structure / bundle layout

5 gaps — leave 2 · record 3 · change 0

### S2.1 — Memoria/ subfolder beside existing notes; catalog/spaces/journal shells removed; engine-private state relocated to per-device data dir

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The core delta is governed: the charter's Knowledge-format row itself names 'the Memoria/ tree' as the OKF bundle, design §3 (L191-262) states the zero-migration/bundle-boundary rationale, §11 item (10) and §16 record the host decision that dissolves the workspace-as-install model, §5 (L361-363) and §16 relocate engine-private state out of the synced vault with a stated reason (Sync ignores hidden folders; per-device DB), and the regression review's fourteen recorded divergences cover kanban/spaces while §3's log.md projection replaces journal/. Two residues the gap report names are genuinely silent: the retirement of the folders.yaml categories/transient-prefix machine map, and what install does when the user already has a Memoria/ folder. Owner ruling R-8 (Memoria is a new vault, never added into an existing one) contests the nesting premise; on the merits beta.1's shape holds — Obsidian wikilinks do not cross vault boundaries, so a Memoria-born vault would sever linking between the researcher's real notes and works, undercutting the charter's note-writing-parity and retention claims — but the disagreement gets its mandated re-examination pass. Human-text protection is location-independent (absence of mem-* markers = human), so the collision silence is bounded harm, not a lost invariant.

- **Recorded:** Core delta: charter Required Product Scope 'Knowledge format' row; design §3 L191-262; §11 item (10); §16 ('ADR obligation' bullet amending ADR-125, 'No dot-folder' bullet); §5 L361-363; §17.6. Residues (folders.yaml categories retirement; Memoria/-name collision policy): nowhere - silent.
- **History:** Whole-tree ownership was earned by install/repair machinery, not a failure of nesting: ADR-26/55 made the repo the install unit with a hash-manifested golden copy that turned the Linter 'from a detector into a repairer', and folders.yaml was 'the single source for the Linter, the policy gate, the installer skeleton, and the tests' after the four-hand-synced-places drift ADR-119's context documents. The alpha line itself dissolved the ownership reason at alpha.15 (golden_restore.py removed, PR #1206; 'package reinstall is the restore path', ADR-125), so beta.1 extends an already-made move; the single-source anti-drift concern is addressed by making the layout product code with a closed type enum (one encoding, no user-editable schema). Nesting beside foreign notes has no alpha precedent in either direction — no earned failure is re-opened.
- **Action:** Add after design §3's zero-migration paragraph (L262): "Recorded divergence: alpha's folders.yaml categories/homes/transient-prefixes map is retired — the layout above is product code and the closed type enum is its only schema, preserving the single-source contract with one encoding instead of four hand-synced ones. If <vault>/Memoria/ already exists at install and does not carry the bundle-root index.md (okf_version: '0.1'), the installer stops and asks the researcher to choose another bundle-root name; pre-existing notes are never silently adopted into the bundle. Owner ruling R-8 (Memoria-born vault) is under re-examination and would supersede this nesting model if upheld."
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Two fixes to the proposed recording, disposition unchanged. (1) Material — the collision remedy: "the installer stops and asks the researcher to choose another bundle-root name" contradicts the governing texts the recording itself cites. The charter's Knowledge-format row hard-names "The Memoria/ tree" as the OKF v0.1 bundle, and design §3 states "the bundle boundary is Memoria/, not the researcher's vault"; a renamable bundle root parameterizes every Memoria/… path in the design (system/, bibliography.bib, local-only/, plugin/daemon surfaces) and silently falsifies the charter row — new machinery introduced via a recording sentence. Replace the remedy clause with: "If <vault>/Memoria/ already exists at install and does not carry the bundle-root index.md (okf_version: '0.1'), the installer stops and asks the researcher to move or rename the pre-existing folder before install proceeds; a folder that does carry it is recognized as an existing Memoria bundle and reconnected, never re-minted. Pre-existing notes are never silently adopted into the bundle." (2) Minor — placement: inserting after L262 severs the frontmatter paragraph (L260-262) from its illustrating YAML block (L264-284); insert after the OKF-bundle paragraph (after L258) or after the YAML block instead. The folders.yaml-retirement sentence and the R-8 re-examination sentence are accurate as proposed.

### S2.2 — works/<citekey>/ co-locates record.md (full CSL-JSON authority), fulltext.md, digest.md, source.pdf; anchor scheme W3C selector → ^pNNNN

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

The delta is adjudicated in the design body and the docs-history record: §3 states the decision with its rationale verbatim ('Full CSL-JSON is serialized into record.md... the derived DB is rebuildable, so bibliographic fidelity and the Zotero re-import key cannot live only in the DB'), §11 records the convergence frame (SQLite authority + markdown keep-set + blobs), docs-history Reject #123 records 'beta.1 deliberately reversed to works/<citekey>/source.pdf for the keep-test' plus the .bib-as-interface staleness rejection, and Reject #125 already directed CSL-JSON and W3C selectors to be boundary subsets, never the internal model — the ^pNNNN switch carries its own survival rationale at §3 L286-292 ('plain text, so they survive reopen, sync, and the death of the tool'). Every motivation of the alpha SQLite arc is honored by a different beta.1 mechanism: worker state, jobs, checks, and raw payloads stay DB-side (§5, §18.3), entities stay DB-side per §17.5 against the sprawl reject, and there is exactly one authority per record (file, DB derived) so the dual-authority drift that killed catalog-frontmatter-as-SSOT cannot recur. Owner rulings R-4/R-9 contest this (relational catalog, .bib as the survival artifact); on the merits the alpha line's own alpha.12 record — 'references.bib is portable but lossy relative to the catalog DB' — is the decisive counter, since only full CSL-JSON in a keep-test file satisfies the charter's Survival and Rebuild bars; the mandated re-examination pass is noted. Citekey-as-primary-key (owner hard ruling R-1) is owned by the §7 adjudicator, not this entry.

- **Recorded:** Design §3 L224-226 (CSL-JSON-in-record.md decision with rationale) and L286-292 (anchor rationale); design §11 L965 (convergence: SQLite authority + markdown keep-set + blobs); docs-history Reject #123 (source.pdf co-location for keep-test) and Reject #125 (CSL-JSON/W3C selectors as boundary subsets); §17.1 (fulltext.md as evidence substrate).
- **History:** Alpha.12-14 moved catalog authority to SQLite for stated operational reasons: the worker 'needs indexed catalog rows for materialization, idempotency, bibliography rendering, and later provider provenance' (ADR-122 context), staging markdown 'leaves an unchecked source-shaped file for tools to accidentally consume' (ADR-123), and a frontmatter-only catalog could not carry 'durable worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates' (ADR-124) — while SQLite-as-canonical-Concept-store was itself rejected as 'opaque to Obsidian/Git'. Beta.1 addresses each: operational state stays in the per-device DB, record.md is a VaultWriter-minted fenced block (not editable frontmatter fields) from which the DB derives, consumers read via the DB/read-API, and entities never become files. The alpha.12 catalog-recovery spike failure (periodic export loses DB-only catalog changes) argues for beta.1's file-canonical records, and alpha's own '.bib is lossy relative to the catalog' finding is the reason record.md carries full CSL-JSON.

### S2.3 — No hubs/ folder (hub type dropped); projects split into project/evidence/gaps/draft/ruled-out files; per-work digest.md restored

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

Two of three sub-deltas are governed: the project multi-file split and ruled-out.md are recorded re-homings (docs-history Adapt #77/#78/#88 put thesis/question/accepted-gaps into project.md and gaps.md; Borrow #59 places the ruled-out log beside gaps.md, never auto-promoted) and the digest.md restore is presumed and endorsed by recorded decisions (Adapt #97 fixed digest.md headings, Adapt #92 takeaway inputs, Borrow #59 processing-debt signal), with alpha.15's fold reason addressed — the old digest type 'conflated the human-authored subjective take with the machine-owned bibliographic record', and beta.1's digest.md is purely machine-class (untrusted, opt-in) while the human take lives in notes/, which owner R-10 explicitly endorses as the wiki concept. The hub drop, however, is not actually recorded: the regression review classes 'hub/tag graph' as a recorded divergence in §11-§17, but no §11-§17 item adjudicates it — the design's only mention is the §7 parenthetical 'hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers' (L623), and docs-history even carries hub-presuming borrows (Borrow #49 hub-due/hub-staleness detectors). The drop is defensible under the charter (no required-scope row needs hubs; OKF parity is about format, not the type roster), but owner rulings R-2/R-5/R-10 contest it as the wiki-LLM/ZK bridge and the flow's missing digest-to-hub link, so the silence must be closed with an explicit record pending that re-examination.

- **Recorded:** Project split + ruled-out.md: docs-history Adapt #77/#78/#88 + Borrow #59; design §3 L202-207, §8. Digest restore: docs-history Adapt #97/#92 + design §3 L199, §7 DigestEngine. Hub drop: nowhere - silent (design §7 L623 is a deferral parenthetical, not an adjudication; the regression-review sweep's '§11-§17 recorded' claim does not verify against the design).
- **History:** Hub survived every alpha consolidation on re-derived value, not an incident: MOC→hub (ADR-50) kept the threshold-alert mechanism under a plainer name, and the alpha.15 four-type cut (ADR-126) kept hub while deleting nine schemas, giving it an owned controlled-vocab tag precisely to fix documented membership rot ('every relevant new note requires a hub edit') and ADR-19's hazard of 'a generated list that looks curated but isn't'. Beta.1 partially honors the function via generated navigation-only index.md projections and human-authored notes, but ships neither the hub type nor the vocabulary substrate its alpha.15 mechanism required. Digest fold: alpha.15 moved digest onto work because the type conflated human take with machine record (ADR-126) — beta.1's machine-only digest.md resolves that conflation, so no earned position is re-opened there.
- **Action:** Add design §18 item 7: "Hub — deferred, not carried: beta.1 ships no hub type or hubs/ tree; navigation rides generated index.md projections and researcher-authored notes, and hubs/mapping views are named post-beta.1 consumers (§7). The alpha-line hub survived every consolidation (ADR-50; ADR-126's owned-vocab-tag fixing membership rot), and owner rulings R-2/R-5/R-10 place its restoration — including the digest→hub flow link — under re-examination; if restored it returns with the controlled-vocabulary substrate it requires. The per-work digest.md restore and the project multi-file split stand as recorded borrows/adaptations (docs-history Adapt #77/#78/#88/#97, Borrow #59)."

### S2.4 — inbox/ repurposed to import staging; system/ slimmed to manifest/incidents/metrics; new reports/ tree

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

All three sub-deltas trace to authoritative records I verified. inbox-as-visible-staging is an explicit §17 resolution ('the inbox becomes visible staging, never silent minting', item 6) with §3 scoping it outside the OKF bundle and minting only via the awaiting-import chip; the attention-projection function alpha's inbox served is re-homed by recorded mechanisms (dead-letter triage stubs in the works tree per §7 and docs-history Borrow #41; attention routing per Borrow #37). The system/ slimming is governed by docs-history Reject #116 (vault-resident prompts/patterns/templates stay dead — operations are product code, which the alpha line itself decided), the charter's Support-org-machinery exclusion (dashboards/eval/observability), out-of-vault logs (Borrow #62), and §16's recorded reason the remainder is visible ('Obsidian Sync ignores hidden folders, and audit copies must survive device loss'). reports/ is a design-body decision with rationale and structural enforcement — §3: report-class notes are 'never indexed for Ask and never citable as compose evidence' — and it is the container the charter's amended discovery exclusion requires ('output never enters Ask or gap denominators'). No owner ruling contests this entry.

Beta.1 keeps both underlying guarantees by other recorded means: pollution control via the bundle boundary (staging is outside OKF conformance, stubs mint only via the chip) and blocked-capture visibility via always-succeeds catalog stubs plus visible dead-letter triage stubs, so no captured source is silently lost. The rich system/ tree's members were already being dissolved by the alpha line itself (ADR-125 'operations are product code'; capabilities relocated out of the workspace at alpha.15), and reports/'s closest ancestors (dashboards, _views) died with the surfaces the charter now excludes.

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The purely nominal rename is silent — no record adjudicates dropping the name that was stable alpha.11→15 as the keep-test takeout — and owner ruling R-9 adds a constraint the design nowhere states: bibliography.bib is the catalog's survival artifact and must never fall under any local-only mechanism. Both are sound on the merits (no production vault exists, so the rename breaks nothing; the bib is generated at the bundle root outside local-only/), but per the project's own name-every-divergence discipline they need one recorded sentence. Catalog-authority questions raised by R-4/R-9 are owned by S2.2 and the §7 entries, not re-adjudicated here.

- **History:** references.bib was the name of the keep-test bibliography takeout continuously from alpha.11 (moved to the workspace root from .memoria/memoria.bib as a generated tracked projection) through alpha.15, and its atomicity rule was earned by a documented failure: the alpha.12 catalog-recovery spike FAILED ('periodic export loses Memoria-owned catalog changes made after the last export'), forcing render-in-the-same-commit. (2) Replace "the catalog's survival artifact" with "a keep-test survival artifact (the portable bibliography takeout)" — the definite-article phrasing is R-4/R-9's SQLite-authority framing and collides with §3 L224-226 (record.md's full CSL-JSON is the fidelity/Zotero-re-import authority in the governing design); catalog authority is owned by S2.2 and must not be pre-judged here. Suggested wording: "references.bib continues as Memoria/bibliography.bib — a rename only: still the generated, complete keep-test bibliography takeout. The alpha.12 same-commit atomicity rule's earned reason (catalog changes lost after the last export) no longer applies: catalog records are themselves keep-test files, so the .bib is regenerable and its freshness is not survival-critical. bibliography.bib is a keep-test survival artifact and is never subject to any local-only mechanism — frontmatter flag, local-only/ residence, or marked ancestor (owner ruling R-9). The per-project export/references.bib (cited works only, emitted at export time) is a second, export-scoped artifact serving the charter's Compose bar, not a replacement." Location as proposed (§3 under the layout block, or a §11 clause) is fine.
## 3. Concept / type model

7 gaps — leave 2 · record 4 · change 1

### S3.1 — Four typed-concept schemas replaced by flat file-class enum; per-type schema files dropped

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

The enum replacement is stated as an explicit decision in the design body (§3: every Memoria-created file carries a `type` from the closed class enum, grounded in OKF §9.2 typed frontmatter), and the load-bearing half of the delta — losing the reject-undeclared per-type validator — is adjudicated with rationale in §18(6): OKF-permissive toleration is deliberate, machine writes stay conformant by construction because VaultWriter serializes from typed fields in product code, which is where the per-type contract now lives. The alpha position was earned by type-zoo accretion ('the multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion'), a failure that cannot recur in a regime with no per-type schema files to accrete lifecycle fields and per-type rules into. The un-named residue — the schema files as artifacts — is plainly covered by §18(6), since validation was the files' function; the charter's knowledge-format bar (required typed frontmatter, OKF v0.1 conformance, no exchange-format regression) is met. Owner position R-6 (every md file a Concept with defined OKF frontmatter+body contracts; this drop a 'first sign beta.1 was sloppy') disagrees and is flagged for the dedicated re-examination pass, but it names no re-opened failure, lost safety invariant, or charter contradiction.

- **Recorded:** design.md §3 (L232-267: class enum stated with OKF §9.2 rationale) + §18(6) (L1303-1312: strict-reject validator declined, conformance-by-construction mechanism named); regression-review R6 + Resolution 2026-07-04 (L99-101)
- **History:** Per-type schemas ran continuously from the pre-alpha.1 Old Skeleton; the alpha.15 collapse to four types (ADR-126 as pointer) was earned by accretion damage — '12+ types across three bundles... each with folder homes, lifecycle fields, and per-type rules. The multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion' (design-history L2074, L2284-2286) — and closed validation guarded the meaning layer against undeclared-field drift. Beta.1 addresses the accretion failure structurally (no schema surface to accrete into; typed contracts live in VaultWriter's serialization code) and trades the strictness half deliberately per §18(6), so the motivating failure is addressed by different machinery, not left open.

### S3.2 — Hub type dropped — no hub concept anywhere in beta.1

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: medium

The design body itself defers hubs deliberately: §7 (L622-624) names 'hubs and mapping views' as post-beta.1 consumers of the entity layer, and the regression review's verified sweep (L78-81) classifies the hub/tag graph among the fourteen recorded divergences, not silent drops; machine-spawned topical pages are additionally a standing reject (§17(5); docs-history reject 'Entity note types'). The alpha hub's documented failures — hand-curated membership rots, and ADR-19's 'generated list that looks curated but isn't' — were failures of hub maintenance mechanics that the alpha.15 owned-tag design fixed; omitting hubs re-opens neither, and no charter bar (capture, reading, Ask, compose, knowledge format) requires hubs. Conflicts flagged for the re-examination pass: owner R-2 ('hub cannot be dropped' — the wiki/Zettelkasten bridge), R-5/R-10 (digest→hub is the missing terminal step of the basic flow), info-flow-research's adopted editorial-hubs verdict, and the docs-history beta1 sample-corpus borrow that presupposes a 'starter hub set'. Under this adjudication's criteria the deferral is a recorded scope decision, not an unaddressed failure.

- **Recorded:** design.md §7 L622-624 ('hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers') + regression-review checked-and-intact sweep L78-81 ('hub/tag graph' verified as recorded divergence); reinforced by design §17(5) L1258-1260 and docs-history reject 'Entity note types' (L111)
- **History:** Hub descends continuously from the Old Skeleton MOC (renamed hub at ADR-50, design-history L149, L268); its alpha.15 owned-checked-tag form was earned by 'hand-curated hub membership rots (every relevant new note requires a hub edit)' and ADR-19's curated-looking-generated-list hazard (design-history L2078). Both are failures of how hubs were maintained, not evidence that hub absence fails; beta.1 does not re-open them by omitting hubs, though the alpha basic flow's digest→hub step (owner R-5) is genuinely gone and unserved until post-beta.1.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Citations are tangential, not adjudication of the hub drop. §7 L622-624 is a passing parenthetical inside the entity-resolution policy ('hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers') — a deferral mention with no decision or rationale about dropping the hub type. §17(5) L1258-1260 and docs-history reject 'Entity note types' (L111) adjudicate person/venue entity pages, not the hub/MOC concept — and the reject's rationale 'Four concept types are deliberate' presupposes hub (one of the four), cutting against the drop. The regression-review sweep (L78-81) claims hub/tag graph is recorded in §11-§17/charter, but 'hub' appears nowhere in design §11-§17 (only §7 L623) and no charter exclusion covers it — the sweep's pointer does not check out.
- **Verifier notes:** Citations are tangential, not adjudication of the hub drop. §7 L622-624 is a passing parenthetical inside the entity-resolution policy ('hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers') — a deferral mention with no decision or rationale about dropping the hub type. §17(5) L1258-1260 and docs-history reject 'Entity note types' (L111) adjudicate person/venue entity pages, not the hub/MOC concept — and the reject's rationale 'Four concept types are deliberate' presupposes hub (one of the four), cutting against the drop. The regression-review sweep (L78-81) claims hub/tag graph is recorded in §11-§17/charter, but 'hub' appears nowhere in design §11-§17 (only §7 L623) and no charter exclusion covers it — the sweep's pointer does not check out.

### S3.3 — Note claim/question mode, question_status, and claim-context/claim-substrate fields dropped

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The claimed record fails verification: the regression review's sweep (L79) lists 'claim-context fields' as a recorded divergence 'in §11-§17 or the charter's exclusions,' but no such passage exists — grep of the design finds no mode, question_status, or claim-substrate text anywhere, and no charter exclusion covers it. On the merits the drop is sound: the mode existed to create gap-engine obligations ('a claim without evidence is an under-warranted gap; an open question is a compose lead'), and that consumer — argument-graph gap analysis — is recorded alpha.16 writing-module scope in the docs-history dossier, so carrying the mode in beta.1 would be exactly the mechanism-without-a-consumer decay the docs-history patterns warn about; the destructive question→claim type-transition failure the mode fixed cannot recur when neither claims nor questions are distinguished at all, and fleeting capture is served by mode-less notes plus inbox/ staging (the docs-history 'Fleeting capture' adapt permits either realization). Owner R-10 concurs the substrate belongs to R-7's argument-graph scope, not a separable drop — if R-7's overrule of the alpha.16 deferral is upheld, this substrate returns with it.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (regression-review L79 claims it is recorded, but no locating §11-§17 passage or charter exclusion exists; verified by grep over the design)
- **History:** ADR-126 (as pointer) made claim/question a mode, not a type, because 'separate types make the question→claim transition destructive' and 'field-derived typing could not tell a plain thought from a claim missing its evidence' — the mode fed the gap engine with under-warranted gaps and compose leads (design-history L2074-2076, L2286). Beta.1 defers the consumer to alpha.16 and drops the substrate with it; the destructive-transition hazard cannot recur with no claim/question distinction at all, so the alpha reason is honored by the deferral rather than left unaddressed.
- **Action:** Add to design §11 divergence list: "Dropped from alpha.15: note `mode: claim|question`, `question_status`, and the claim-context/claim-substrate fields. Their consumer — argument-graph gap obligations (a claim without evidence = an under-warranted gap; an open question = a compose lead) — is alpha.16 writing-module scope, and the substrate returns with it. Fleeting capture folds into mode-less `note` plus `inbox/` staging."

### S3.4 — Argument-graph project concept dropped; project becomes a folder of files and gap analysis becomes retrieval-coverage

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

This is the most thoroughly recorded deferral in the corpus: the docs-history adjudication targets the entire cluster — argument-graph-vs-knowledge-map with outline derivation, the gap taxonomy, saturation-with-refutation-floor-and-researcher-stamp, counter-outlines with CHOSEN, the draft claim-trace loop, thesis-as-project-anchor, the export decision model — at alpha16 (borrow table L50-57, adapt L77-78), and recommended action 10 (L157) seeds the alpha.16 writing module with the dossier as its starting spec, standing rejects included. The saturation-meter face additionally collides with the charter's Deliberate Exclusion of aggregate evidence scores (the 'Consensus Meter — seductive and wrong'), which is decisive against demanding that part back. The verify-added drops (deliverable target types outline/section/figure/code, project frame-paper, export --ready-only) are faces of the same deferred writing module, plainly covered by the broader record. Owner R-7 explicitly overrules the alpha.16 deferral ('argument graph is beta.1 scope') — flagged for the dedicated re-examination pass; under this adjudication's criteria the deferral re-opens no documented failure and contradicts no charter bar (the compose bar requires gather/gaps/draft/export, not an argument graph), so the recorded decision stands.

- **Recorded:** docs-history borrow/adapt/reject: argument-graph cluster all Target alpha16 (L50-54, L56-57, L77-78) + recommended action 10 (L157); charter Deliberate Exclusion 'Aggregate evidence scores' (requirements L85) for the saturation-meter face
- **History:** ADR-77/78/79 (accepted 2026-06-16, design-history L987) built the project gate, thesis type, and argument graph; alpha.15 absorbed them into the typed project concept (thesis a role not a type, saturation floor folded into the gap engine — design-history L2080, L2160), motivated by gap analysis over argument structure ('a project can have zero missing notes and still be intellectually bankrupt') and outline-derives-from-argument-else-survey (docs-history L50-51). Beta.1 re-sequences rather than abandons that reason: the whole kit is recorded alpha.16 scope with the recovered dossier as starting spec, and the charter excludes the saturation-meter flavor outright.

### S3.5 — ULID identity dropped; identity re-derived from citekey + file path

**CHANGE — needs design change (severity: medium)** · verification: contested (1/3 skeptics dissent) · confidence: high

Disposition decided by owner hard ruling R-1 (owner-rulings 2026-07-05, L16-37): a mutable key cannot be identity, and the concrete failure case is native to beta.1's own design — BBT-derived citekeys change on metadata correction, so re-import of the same work either mints a duplicate works row/directory or defeats the idempotent upsert, which is why §7 already stores the Zotero item key as a second, stable key: two identity systems with the mutable one primary. The machine adjudication, preserved as a footnote per the ruling, would have been 'record': the drop is fully silent (not in R1-R6, the fourteen divergences, or §11), but §7's pin-at-import plus the revertible rename run do implement the docs-history citekey-stability borrow that documented the drift failure. The ruling's point stands on the merits regardless: pinning mitigates but does not address the alpha.14/15 reason (identity decoupled from mutable keys and paths so corrections never change identity), and beta.1 reverses 'citekey change no longer renames the Work' — a correction now cascades through every citekey-keyed table (works, chunks, anchors, edges, annotations, checks) and every vault path in one rename blast radius.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (only embodied in design §5 L374 `works(citekey PK)` and §7 L569-577 rename-run; the drop itself is adjudicated in no authoritative record). Owner hard ruling: gap-analysis/owner-rulings-2026-07-05.md R-1 (L16-37)
- **History:** ADR-124 (alpha.14, design-history L2042) made stable Work IDs primary with citekeys as aliases because a standalone engine cannot hang identity on a desktop reference manager's mutable keys; ADR-126 added ULID id — 'identity ≠ filename ≠ title... so renames/moves don't break references' (design-history L2088). The documented failure behind pinning: 'unpinned keys drift on metadata correction and orphan the works/<citekey>/ folder, every wikilink, and the BibTeX keep-test output' (docs-history L40). Beta.1 adopts the pinning fix but re-mounts identity on the mutable key, so the decoupling reason is mitigated, not addressed — the owner's re-import case shows the residue is live.
- **Action:** Restore a stable machine identity (ULID/work_id-class) as the primary key for works and all internal references — the DB tables (works, chunks, anchors, edges, annotations, checks), the manifest, and anchor/citation resolution — with `citekey` demoted to a pinned human-facing alias; a citekey correction updates the alias and may rename the directory as presentation, but never changes identity, and re-import idempotency keys on the stable ID (zotero_key becomes a provider alias, not a second identity system). Record the decision in design §5/§7 and name the reversal in the §11 divergence list.
- **Verifier notes:** No charter row demands a stable machine ID: the owner's concrete failure case is mitigated inside required scope (pin-at-import, zotero_key idempotent upsert, exact-identifier auto-merge with needs_metadata on conflict — design §7 L554-579), the DB-side cascade lands entirely in the derived store the charter's Rebuild row (requirements L63) declares regenerable, and the vault-side rename cost persists under ULIDs anyway since the proposal keeps directory renames as presentation. An architecture-wide re-keying of seven tables, anchor resolution, and the manifest (which is path-keyed over non-work human files that have no work_id) is over-machinery for a one-researcher retention experiment (requirements L9-11), and the Upgrade row (L61, exercised lossless migrations) keeps a post-beta.1 work_id migration open at no risk. What the charter's own discipline does require is that the reversal stop being silent — the drop is recorded nowhere, violating the name-every-divergence practice the regression review enforces (alpha-regression-review L88-90), and the preserved machine adjudication itself reached 'record'. Owner hard ruling R-1 forces 'change' procedurally, but R-1 is a design-quality judgment outside the charter, and the charter is the spec.

### S3.6 — Relation-typed frontmatter links map dropped for body wikilinks + DB links table

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

No authoritative record adjudicates this delta: §18(6) covers only validator strictness (R6's 'nested-link invariants' were the validation path, not the typed-links model), the fourteen recorded divergences omit it, and §11/§17 are silent. On the merits it is defensible: every consumer of authored supports/contradicts/extends edges — argument-graph gap analysis, the contradiction surface, outline derivation — is recorded alpha.16 scope in the docs-history dossier, and the one relation live in beta.1, supersession, is honored in substance by the scalar `superseded-by:` successor key (satisfying the docs-history 'successor pointer, not a bare boolean' borrow) plus the DB links backlink table. The alpha line's reason for keeping typed edges in the core against OKF's prose-conveyed links — untyped links cannot power the argument layer — travels with the deferred consumer, so it does not bite inside beta.1; the representation question must reopen when the argument graph returns. Conflicts flagged: owner R-7 pulls typed links into beta.1 scope, and info-flow-research's 'denominator-honest gap analysis' argument is the same conflict — but neither converts a consumer-less field drop into a lost safety invariant or charter contradiction today.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-52 (alpha.1, design-history L196) split authored typed links from mechanical relationships because one field 'conflated two different things... [that] differ in nature, owner, and gating'; the alpha line refused prose-typed relationships as the internal representation with recorded rationale — 'Memoria deliberately rejected prose-typed relationships in favor of typed edges... OKF is therefore a fit for the boundary, not the core' (ADR-107 as pointer, design-history L2296) — because typed edges powered the argument layer (contradictions dashboard, claim supersession). Beta.1 defers that layer to alpha.16 and carries supersession via the scalar key, so the motivating consumers are re-sequenced, not ignored; the representation decision itself went unrecorded.
- **Action:** Add to design §11 divergence list: "Dropped from alpha.15: the relation-typed frontmatter `links:` map ({supports, contradicts, extends}). Its consumers (argument-graph gap analysis, the contradiction surface, outline derivation) are alpha.16 scope and the typed-edge representation question reopens with them; beta.1's link substrate is body wikilinks plus the DB `links` table, and the one live typed relation — supersession — is carried by the `superseded-by:` successor key."

### S3.7 — Controlled-vocabulary / faceting substrate dropped entirely (vocabulary.md, research_area/methodology, vocab, classify)

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

Only the doctrine half is recorded: machine-materialized frontmatter facets are a standing reject (design §5 'stage state stays DB-side', §17(2) meaning-only holds, docs-history reject 'Machine-written frontmatter' L110), which forecloses the alpha classify-into-frontmatter path. But the total absence of any topical substrate — the curated vocabulary.md SSOT, the research_area/methodology facets, the vocab and classify operations — is adjudicated only in lens documents (the if-design's 'enrichment-only (unverified)' charting tier, addendum §3 bullet 7) that were never folded into the design body: the design contains no mention of topics, facets, or vocabulary at all, and per the gap report's verified correction not even a tags field. On the merits the drop is defensible for beta.1: retrieval is FTS+vectors and discovery is citation-graph (recorded at §17(4)), so the documented alpha failure the vocabulary guarded against — facet drift making facet queries silently incomplete — has no beta.1 query surface to bite. Owner R-13 (topics are a discovery precondition, 'the system cannot help the user find information about X') is flagged for re-examination; it argues future discovery value, not a re-opened failure or charter contradiction, since the charter's Ask bar is met by corpus retrieval and its discovery amendment is deliberately citation-graph-scoped. The drop should be named so it reads as a decision, not an omission.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent for the substrate drop itself (partial coverage: the machine-facet write path is rejected at design §5 L418-427 + §17(2) L1245-1248 + docs-history reject L110; the enrichment-only-tier framing lives only in lens docs — gap-analysis addendum §3 bullet 7 citing if-design L180/L197)
- **History:** Continuous from the Old Skeleton; alpha.1's vocabulary-discipline doc records the motivating failure: facet drift like 'receptivity-detection vs opportune-moments... produces no error... queries return incomplete results; the PI infers thin coverage when coverage is adequate' (design-history L218); classify was automated because a human gate on high-volume verifiable metadata 'is a guaranteed rubber stamp' (ADR-54 as pointer, L244); ADR-04's surviving half kept topics in frontmatter facets, never folders (L272). Beta.1 moots rather than re-opens the failure — with no facet query surface the silent-incomplete-query mode cannot occur, and the facet write path is doctrinally rejected — but no beta.1 record says so, and OpenAlex topic data survives only incidentally in the payloads store.
- **Action:** Add to design §11 divergence list (or an §18-style recorded decision): "Dropped from alpha.15: the controlled-vocabulary/faceting substrate (`system/vocabulary.md`, `research_area`/`methodology` facets, the `vocab` and `classify` operations). Beta.1 retrieval is FTS+vector and discovery is citation-graph (§17(4)), so no facet query surface exists, and machine-materialized frontmatter facets remain a standing reject (§5, §17(2)). OpenAlex topic payloads are preserved in the content-addressed `payloads` store, so a post-beta.1 enrichment-only topics tier can be built without re-fetching."
## 4. Frontmatter discipline

9 gaps — leave 6 · record 3 · change 0

### S4.1 — Universal frontmatter re-scoped from every-Concept to every-Memoria-created-file at the Memoria/ bundle boundary

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The beta.1 charter itself sets the bar at exactly this scope: the Knowledge-format row requires 'required typed frontmatter on every Memoria-created file' with OKF v0.1 bundle conformance and 'no regression of the exchange format' — the re-scope is charter-defined, not silent. Design §3 records the two scoping rules explicitly ('the bundle boundary is Memoria/, not the researcher's vault'; 'the conformance guarantee is every Memoria-created file, always; freehand files converge via proposals') and states the absence-of-mem-*-markers = human rule with its zero-migration rationale. The alpha reason for universality (consumers need guaranteed fields for standing filtering and links traversal) is served DB-side in beta.1, and the regression review verified OKF bundle conformance held. Vault-wide universality is structurally incompatible with beta.1's zero-migration commitment to the user's pre-existing notes.

- **Recorded:** Requirements charter, Required Product Scope 'Knowledge format' row (0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md L36); design §3 L232-262 (bundle-boundary scoping rules and absence-of-markers rule with zero-migration rationale)
- **History:** Universality arrived at alpha.14 (PR #1157, commit 88b7f0f5): id/standing/links enforcement on every Concept because OKF Knowledge Bundle contracts, standing-based supersession filtering, and links traversal 'have no guaranteed field to read' without it (history L1916-1922). Alpha.15 retired #1157's field set the same day while keeping universality with meaning-only fields (L2086, L2290-2292). Beta.1 addresses the motivating need differently: filtering/traversal consumers are DB-side, OKF conformance holds at the bundle boundary, and the human-span manifest carries authorship safety — the regression review's sweep confirms the exchange format did not regress.

### S4.2 — Closed reject-undeclared-fields validator and x.* extension namespace dropped for OKF-permissive toleration

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is adjudicated verbatim in design §18(6): 'Frontmatter strict-reject validator — declined; OKF-permissive is deliberate,' with the machine-write-conformant-by-construction argument (VaultWriter serializes from typed fields, closed type enum), the freehand-converges-via-proposals path, and the x.* confinement explicitly deferred with a named revisit trigger (if mem-* keys crowd the meaning layer). The regression review's Resolution of 2026-07-04 records the same verdict (R6 declined, x.* deferred) after flagging it Low-borderline and noting beta.1's stance is more OKF-idiomatic, not less. The alpha closure was a principle-completion, not a failure response, so declining it re-opens nothing.

- **Recorded:** Design §18(6) L1303-1312; regression review Resolution 2026-07-04 (R6 declined) and R6 borderline analysis L48-57
- **History:** Closed validation landed only in alpha.15 (PR-AC #1197): validate_frontmatter rejects undeclared fields with an x: map escape hatch, closing the field-closure half of ADR-119's schema-as-single-declarative-contract (history L2090) — it reversed the alpha.1-14 permissive posture and was motivated by design principle (meaning-layer cleanliness), not a documented incident. Beta.1 keeps the property that mattered (machine writes cannot emit undeclared junk, by construction) and defers the x.* cleanliness gain with a recorded revisit condition.

### S4.3 — Universal fields id, tags, links, aliases, archived dropped from the Memoria frontmatter contract

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

Each dropped field's function is either honored by a different beta.1 mechanism or legitimately out of charter scope, but no authoritative record adjudicates the field-set change itself. Rename-safe identity (the ULID's purpose) is re-earned via citekeys pinned at import with correction as a first-class revertible rename run — design §7 even labels citekey drift 'a documented historical failure'; the typed link layer moves to DB links/edges with wikilinks as the in-vault form; citekey serves as the human alias; researcher-set superseded plus ruled-out files carry the meaning-bearing archived cases. Tags served the hub membership system, which beta.1 has no equivalent of, and the charter requires none of these fields (OKF requires only type plus recommended keys). The keep-test and exchange-format invariants were verified intact by the regression sweep, so the drop is sound — it is just silent.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (fragments exist: citekey and superseded semantics detailed in design §3/§4, citekey pinning in §7; but no record names the universal-field-set drop)
- **History:** Alpha.15's universal contract (PR #1164/#1179, history L2086) carried ULID id ('identity ≠ filename ≠ title' — renames must not break references, L2088), tags (hub-owned controlled-vocabulary membership, L2078), typed links (ADR-52's human argument layer distinct from engine relationships, L2092), aliases, and archived (with superseded, 'the meaning-bearing survivors' of the lifecycle-ladder cut). Beta.1 addresses the rename-fragility motive via pinned citekeys + revertible rename runs (§7 L569-577); the hub/tag system the tags field served is dropped wholesale; the typed authored-link layer has no beta.1 successor but no documented failure earned it and the charter does not require it.
- **Action:** Add to design §11's divergence list: "Diverges from alpha.15's universal Concept field set: id/tags/links/aliases/archived are dropped from Memoria frontmatter. Identity and rename-safety move to citekeys pinned at import with correction as a revertible rename run (§7); the link graph lives in DB links/edges with wikilinks as the in-vault form (§3, §5); citekey serves as the human alias; researcher-set superseded plus ruled-out files replace archived (§4). The hub/tag membership system those fields served is outside beta.1 scope."
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Recording text fix (disposition stands; location §11 is fine as a new third "Diverges from alpha.15" paragraph beside Converges/Back-pressures, or as a §18 Recorded-decisions entry per the R5/R6 pattern — there is no existing §11 "divergence list"). Replace the proposed text with: "Diverges from alpha.15's universal Concept field set: id/tags/links/aliases/archived are dropped from Memoria frontmatter (§3). Rename-safe identity (the ULID's motive) is re-earned by citekeys pinned at import with correction as a first-class revertible rename run (§7); in-vault connectivity is Obsidian wikilinks backed by the DB links backlink table and the machine citation-graph edges table (§5) — the human-authored typed relation layer (supports/contradicts/extends, ADR-52) has no beta.1 successor and is deferred with its argument-graph consumer to alpha.16; citekey serves as the human alias; researcher-set superseded (§4) plus ruled-out files (§3, §8) carry the meaning-bearing archived cases. The hub/tag membership system the tags field served is post-beta.1 scope (§7), and the charter requires none of these fields." Key changes from the draft: (1) do not claim the typed link layer "moves to DB links/edges" — DB links is untyped backlinks and DB edges is the machine citation graph, so the typed authored layer is a drop-without-successor and must be named as such; (2) cite superseded to §4 but ruled-out to §3/§8, not §4; (3) attribute the hub/tag system to the tags field specifically, not to "those fields" collectively.

### S4.4 — Researcher-set superseded/superseded-by returned to frontmatter after alpha.15 moved supersession standing to the DB

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The design body adjudicates this delta explicitly and with rationale in two places: §4's invalidation paragraph designs the researcher-set flag end-to-end (Ask default-exclusion counted in the denominator, per-Ask override with visible labels, export refusal, Crossref audit) and quotes the docs-history lesson that the flag previously shipped without a retrieval consumer and was a live bug for months; §5 states 'the only pipeline-adjacent frontmatter is researcher-set, meaning-bearing decisions (reading, superseded), which meaning-only doctrine permits.' The alpha failure that exiled standing to the DB was machine-verdict state being forgeable and churning — beta.1 keeps machine verdicts DB-side (§18(1) checks table) and returns only the human-authored judgment to the file, which is consistent with ADR-125's own split ('files own meaning, the DB owns verdicts'): a researcher's supersession decision is meaning. The export-refusal half is separately recorded in §18(2), and the docs-history borrow entry ('Supersession + retraction consumption') is a recorded decision demanding exactly these consumers.

- **Recorded:** Design §4 L339-353 (decision with rationale incl. the no-consumer failure lesson); §5 L424-427; §18(2) L1287-1289; docs-history borrow-adapt-reject, Borrow table 'Supersession + retraction consumption' entry (L31)
- **History:** Alpha.15 (#1163/#1179, ADR-125/126, history L2086/L2225/L2292) moved standing/check_status DB-side because frontmatter verdict state meant 'checking a note rewrote it, hand-edits forged status, and every consumer had to distrust the file' — a failure about machine-written, mutable verdict state. The researcher-set flag maps to alpha.1's superseded_by (human meaning, set once, fail-safe direction: forging it only restricts retrieval and blocks export, never mints green). The documented failure that actually bit — the flag shipping with no retrieval consumer (alpha.9 audit: drafts citing retired claims for months) — is directly addressed by beta.1's wired consumers.

### S4.5 — New researcher-set reading: skip|cite-only|read disposition key with no alpha frontmatter precedent

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17(2) records this precisely: 'Meaning-only frontmatter holds — machine stage state stays DB-side...; researcher-set decisions (reading) are the only new frontmatter,' explicitly re-rejecting the clean-slate pass's machine-owned stage frontmatter in the same breath. §5 repeats the governing principle (researcher-set, meaning-bearing decisions are the permitted class) and §7 specifies the mechanism ('meaning-bearing frontmatter, never machine state,' set via Zotero tag/color or the work page). A pass-1 reading disposition is a human judgment that survives the keep-test, so the addition is squarely inside the recorded doctrine rather than an erosion of it.

- **Recorded:** Design §17(2) L1245-1248; §5 L424-427; §7 L705-708
- **History:** No alpha-line frontmatter precedent — the nearest relatives were machine capture-stage states and source lifecycle fields, which alpha.15 kept DB-side under meaning-only doctrine (ADR-126) precisely because machine stage state in frontmatter churns and forges. Beta.1 preserves that reason intact: the new key is researcher-set and stage state stays DB-side with a reconciliation pass (§5); nothing the alpha position protected is re-exposed.

### S4.6 — Intake-origin (source:) and resource identity (resource:) surfaced as work frontmatter keys where alpha.15 kept them DB-side

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The two keys split: resource: is recorded — design §3 names it the OKF-recommended key for the underlying asset (DOI URL or pinned repo URL) as part of the charter-required OKF conformance decision — but source: appears only in the §3 YAML example with no adjudication anywhere. The delta is sound: source: is a set-once birth fact, not the mutable machine pipeline state §5's standing reject targets ('works.status, jobs, edges, entity status... never materialized into frontmatter'), so it cannot churn or forge; it survives the keep-test, OKF consumers tolerate producer keys, and the intake provenance of record still rides capture events DB-side (§5). Since alpha's DB-side position was an authority-split principle rather than a response to a frontmatter failure, nothing is re-opened — but the source: half deserves a sentence so the machine-writes-frontmatter boundary stays sharp.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent for source:; resource: recorded in design §3 L238-240 (OKF-recommended key on works, with rationale)
- **History:** Alpha.14/15 kept catalog/intake facts DB-side under ADR-124/125 split-authority: a frontmatter-only catalog was explicitly rejected because 'durable worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates, and generated projections [are] better represented in SQLite' (history L2042), and the machine-frontmatter pattern has 'three documented generations of decay' (design §5) — but that decay record concerns mutable derived scalars, not set-once origin facts. Beta.1 keeps mutable state DB-side, so the documented failure mode is not re-exposed.
- **Action:** Add to the design §3 frontmatter paragraph (or §11 list): "Divergence from alpha.15, recorded: works carry a set-once source: zotero|inbox|doi|bibtex|url|repo origin key stamped at mint. It is a birth fact, not mutable pipeline state, so the §5 machine-frontmatter standing reject does not apply; it survives the keep-test and OKF consumers tolerate it as a producer key. Intake provenance of record still rides capture events (§5)."

### S4.7 — Optional in-frontmatter citations: list dropped; citation relationships live as DB edges

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The alpha citations: field existed for one reason — keep-set self-sufficiency after the catalog moved to SQLite — and beta.1 honors that reason through different machinery: full CSL-JSON is fenced into record.md precisely because 'bibliographic fidelity and the Zotero re-import key cannot live only in the DB' (§3), in-body wikilink citations resolve by citekey to those records, and bibliography.bib is the regenerated portable artifact; the regression sweep verified the keep-test (markdown + BibTeX survive the tool) intact. The DB edges table is the machine citation graph (provider reference lists), a different object from alpha's per-note survival copy. The substance is preserved but the field drop itself is adjudicated nowhere, so it should be named once.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (the survival-copy successor mechanism is recorded in design §3 L224-226, but the citations: drop is not named)
- **History:** Alpha.12 added citations: to digest/hub/note as 'the load-bearing consequence of moving the catalog into SQLite': a note holding only a source_id handle 'becomes meaningless the moment SQLite is dropped,' so the cross-store reference rule demanded a denormalized survival copy in the file, corroborated by the cross-store spike's FAIL result (history L1776, L1804). Beta.1 addresses the identical self-sufficiency requirement at the work level (CSL-JSON in record.md + citekey wikilinks + bibliography.bib) instead of per-note denormalization, and the charter's Survival claim is met.
- **Action:** Add to design §11's divergence list: "Divergence from alpha.15, recorded: the optional in-frontmatter citations: survival-copy list is dropped. Its keep-test purpose is served by full CSL-JSON fenced in record.md, wikilink citations resolving by citekey, and the regenerated bibliography.bib; the machine citation graph lives in DB edges (§5). No per-note denormalized citation copy is required for the survival claim."

### S4.8 — New per-file local-only: true frontmatter key enforced in prompt assembly

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §11 item (8) explicitly records 'the fail-closed local-only marker' as one of the requirements beta.1 back-pressures the alpha plans with — the addition is named in the design's own alpha-relationship record, not silent. The mechanism is fully specified with fail-closed semantics in §8 (frontmatter flag, local-only/ folder residence, or any marked ancestor excludes; unparseable frontmatter is treated as local-only; transitive), and drafts default to local-only (§3, §8). The docs-history borrow table separately records the per-work privacy knob ('excluded works never leave the machine') as an adopted decision, so this is a governed, deliberately-added invariant rather than an ungoverned drift.

- **Recorded:** Design §11 item (8) L984-985; §3 L211/L280; §8 L942-944 (fail-closed exclusion semantics); docs-history borrow-adapt-reject, Borrow 'LLM context-assembly contract' entry (L43, per-work excluded level)
- **History:** Alpha.15 had no per-file local-only marker — the capability simply did not exist at file granularity, so there is no alpha position earned by failure to re-open; the deleted-docs record carried the per-work excluded/privacy knob that beta.1's key realizes. Beta.1 strengthens rather than weakens the alpha line: the marker fails closed (unparseable frontmatter excludes), which is the direction every beta.1 honesty mechanism takes.
