### S4.9 — In-file provenance/verdict layer (mem-prov/mem-taint/mem-flags/mem-run + %%prov%% block markers) re-added after alpha.15 eliminated all in-file verdict state

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The delta is doubly recorded: §4 designs the in-file marker layer with explicit rationale (sidecars rot under stock-Obsidian edits; in-file markers travel with the text; the hash manifest backstops), and §18(1) adjudicates the exact ADR-126 hazard — 'in-file mc is a claim, not authority': the verdict of record is the DB checks row bound to block_sha256, green requires marker + current hash + row to agree, and mem rebuild/restore fails closed to amber and re-earns via the local Checker. Both documented reasons ADR-126 rejected an in-file projection are answered: the forged-status foot-gun is neutralized because a hand-written or restored marker cannot render green without a matching DB row and current hash, and the hash-churn/rewrite hazard on human notes is structurally absent because markers exist only on machine-created content (absence of markers = human) so checking never rewrites a human file — a human edit under a marker demotes to amber and enqueues re-check. Taint stays monotone and never-green (§4), and mem-flags mirrors a DB column (works.distrust_flags) rather than replacing it.

- **Recorded:** Design §18(1) L1282-1286 (regression R1 resolution) + §4 L294-338 (no-sidecar rationale; marker-is-claim/DB-is-authority; fail-closed rebuild); §5 L384-385 (checks table as mc-authority)
- **History:** ADR-126 rejected even a generated-but-ignored in-file check_status projection as 'hash churn plus a forged-status foot-gun,' rooted in the deeper failure that 'check_status lived in frontmatter, so checking a note rewrote it, hand-edits forged status, and every consumer had to distrust the file it was reading' (history L2086, L2292). Beta.1 initially re-opened exactly this (regression review R1, HIGH: ProvenanceRenderer painted green straight from the file marker, contradicting §11) and then closed it with the checks-row + block-hash + fail-closed-to-amber mechanism — the failure is addressed, not merely tolerated.
## 5. Integrity / review / gate model

7 gaps — leave 5 · record 2 · change 0

### S5.1 — First-class Review surface (Obsidian main-pane view + ribbon badge, one-click revert, cognition-bound throttle) vs alpha.15's consequence-routed attention worklist

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The substance A15 kept when it removed the approval surface — honesty cards (arguments not verdicts), batch worklists, graded loudness, dispositions at the review action — is carried verbatim in design §1 'Review discipline' (L112-134), and §11 files the Elicit-style span-first review surface plus 'no approval dialogs' under Converges (L970-972). The surface-form delta (main-pane view + ribbon count) follows from §11 item (10), the recorded host decision that beta.1 is an Obsidian plugin; one-click revert and the no-catch-up-queue property are charter Review-row requirements ('reversible by run, reviewable without creating a catch-up queue'). The cognition-bound throttle is a recorded docs-history borrow ('Attention back-pressure', target beta1). Nothing restores approval-confers-correctness: proposals carry no verdict line, no 'approved' machine state exists, and the graduated pre-write approval gate is a docs-history keep-dead reject.

- **Recorded:** design.md §11 L970-972 (converges: Elicit-style span-first review surface; no approval dialogs) and L987-989 (item 10, host decision); design.md §1 L112-134 (Review discipline); docs-history borrow rows 'Attention back-pressure' (L30) and 'Batch worklists' (L28); charter Required Product Scope, Review row
- **History:** ADR-128 removed the review queue's approval semantics because per-write approval measurably bought no correctness — Jacobs 2021 (N=220): clinician+ML 0.356 ≈ clinician-alone 0.357, and a wrong recommendation dragged the human below baseline; Feng & Liu verification asymmetry degrades the gate to a cursory nod under load (history L2110, L2116). ADR-51/ADR-121 honesty-card and enqueue-only obligations were carried, and the inbox-as-category died as collateral of the inbox retirement, not on merits (docs-history 'Patterns' L134). Beta.1 keeps the failure fixed: the Review surface dispositions and reverts already-applied runs, it never gates writes, so the rubber-stamp failure mode ADR-128 documented is not re-opened.

### S5.2 — Rejection→regression-fixture ratchet momentarily lost (R4), now restored

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This delta was found as regression R4 (Med, calibration debt) by the alpha-regression review and fixed in the design body on 2026-07-04: §18 'Fixed in the body' item 4 records the resolution, and §1 L125-130 carries the mechanism verbatim — 'a rejected engine output is not just telemetry: it is auto-added as a candidate case to that operation's regression fixture,' mirroring the security-fixture ratchet (§10). The current design converges with alpha.15; there is no residual delta to adjudicate.

- **Recorded:** design.md §18 item 4 (L1293-1294); design.md §1 L125-130; alpha-regression-review Resolution of 2026-07-04 (L92-98, R4)
- **History:** Alpha.15 made every human-rejected engine output a candidate case in that operation's regression fixture, part of ADR-128's calibration bargain — dispositions are what make 'calibrated' falsifiable, and the fixture ratchet turns the sharpest review signal into a permanent guard (history L2114 disposition telemetry; fixture-ratchet practice in docs-history borrow L68). Beta.1's clean-slate draft fed rejections only to tuning; the regression review caught it and the §18 fix restores the alpha mechanism exactly.

### S5.3 — Synchronous pre==post human-span manifest gate + block-level byte-immutability + auto-rollback (stronger than alpha.15's asynchronous read-path guard)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is a beta.1 strengthening explicitly adjudicated in §11 back-pressure item (4): 'the block-level human-content read-only rule + span-hash manifest with pre==post gate and auto-rollback (stronger than alpha.15's propagation-only demotion)' (L978-981), with the mechanism specified in §6 steps 2-3 (per-file recompute under the write lock, mismatch ⇒ git reset --hard + incident + run failed). It directly serves the charter's hardest trust bar — 'Machines never overwrite or delete human-authored text; a violation stops the beta immediately' — and the Overreliance row's demand for vigilance-independent mechanisms. The per-human-span granularity having no exact alpha precedent is fine: the gap report itself grades it survivor-grade, not a regression.

- **Recorded:** design.md §11 item (4) L978-981; design.md §6 L463-476 (apply/verify steps); charter Required Trust Scope, 'Human text' and 'Overreliance' rows
- **History:** Alpha's lineage ran vault-hash-drift (alpha.1, whole-file) → quarantine-on-scan (alpha.14) → ADR-127's deliberately asynchronous read-path consumption guard; the synchronous form was rejected there only for the READ path — 'a write on the read path races the workspace lock; refusal alone is already fail-closed' (history L2124). Beta.1 applies the synchronous gate on its own WRITE path, per file, under the per-file lock immediately before/after its own write (§6 step 3), so the race that motivated alpha's rejection structurally cannot occur where beta.1 put the gate. The alpha reason is respected, not re-opened.

### S5.4 — Universal quarantine-until-verified narrowed: human content trusted-by-default, no workspace foreign-edit scan, no read-path refuse-to-serve

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The narrowing is nowhere adjudicated: §11 claims convergence on 'the consumption-guard / hash-manifest family' (L967-969) without naming the dropped scan or refuse-to-serve, the §18 resolutions cover only R1-R6, and no docs-history entry or charter exclusion touches it. On the merits it is sound: the charter attributes trust defenses only to vigilance-independent mechanisms (taint, manifest gate, revert, export gate) and never requires universal quarantine, and beta.1 enforces consumption integrity at point of use instead — green requires marker + current block hash + checks-row agreement, an edited block demotes to amber and re-checks, export refuses on unwarranted or superseded citations (§8 L828-836), and the periodic reconciliation pass flags artifact divergence into Review (§5 L421-427). The alpha scan's objects largely do not exist in beta.1's substrate: there is no overrides.jsonl, bibliography.bib is generated from stored CSL-JSON rather than consumed, and human notes are not embedded in retrieval (§5 L414-416). Serving foreign-edited content amber-with-framing rather than withholding it mirrors alpha.15's own stale-served-with-framing posture for non-correctness-bearing consumers, while the refuse behavior survives where it is load-bearing (the export gate).

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (§11 L967-969 claims family-level convergence; regression-review sweep L66-68 verified 'quarantine-and-verify realized as staging + the human-span manifest gate' but the Resolution adjudicates only R1-R6)
- **History:** ADR-127's universal invariant — every mutation non-consumable until verified, one shared check suite with a workspace-scan ingress covering all tracked paths incl. references.bib/overrides.jsonl, hash-mismatch refuses to serve and enqueues a scan — existed to make ADR-128's no-write-gate epistemics safe: 'errors become detectable, attributable, and reversible instead of gated at creation' (history L2122, L2124). It was a designed belt for the epistemic reversal, not the residue of a specific foreign-edit incident. Beta.1 addresses that reason by moving detection to point-of-use hash agreement plus export-time refusal and run-scoped revert, and by removing the consumption paths the scan guarded — but never says so.
- **Action:** Add a recorded divergence to design §11 (or an §18-style recorded decision): "Beta.1 narrows alpha.15's universal quarantine-until-verified: there is no workspace foreign-edit scan and no read-path refuse-to-serve. Consumption integrity is enforced at point of use — green requires marker + current block hash + `checks` row agreement, an edited block serves amber and re-checks, and export refuses on unwarranted or superseded citations — with the periodic reconciliation pass flagging artifact divergence into Review. The alpha scan's objects (overrides.jsonl, a hand-consumed references.bib, human notes in the retrieval substrate) do not exist in beta.1."

### S5.5 — Non-authoritative in-file %%prov:mc%% marker (three-way agreement, 'citation-correct' semantics) vs alpha.15's DB-only no-marker end-state

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The marker-as-claim contract is the recorded §18 fix of regression R1 (design §18 item 1, L1282-1286: verdict of record is the DB checks row bound to block_sha256; green requires marker + current hash + row agreement; rebuild/restore fails closed to amber), and design §4 L325-338 states the same decision with rationale in the body. The 'citation-correct' relabel and the UI-copy rule ('verified against anchors,' never 'safe/approved') are an explicit decision-with-rationale at §4 L311-320, grounded in the Wallat post-rationalization evidence with the faithfulness gap documented rather than papered over, and the charter's Overreliance row independently forbids crediting the marker as a defense. Beta.1's terminology gate being narrower than alpha's (which also blocked 'verified') is inside that recorded decision, and the load-bearing safety is carried by the byte-substring quote guarantee and export gate, not the label.

- **Recorded:** design.md §18 item 1 (L1282-1286); design.md §4 L311-338 (marker-is-claim + citation-correct naming with rationale); charter Required Trust Scope, 'Overreliance' row
- **History:** Alpha.15 removed in-file verdict state (ADR-126, PR-L #1179) because frontmatter check_status meant 'checking a note rewrote it, hand-edits forged status, and every consumer had to distrust the file it was reading,' with DB-loss failing closed to unchecked and rebuild ignoring forged frontmatter (history L2086, L2110, L2132, L2290). Beta.1 addresses each documented failure: a forged or restored mc marker cannot render green (no matching checks row / hash), rebuild demotes every mc to amber and re-earns via the $0 local Checker, and markers are trailing comments on machine blocks only, so checking never rewrites human content. The alpha failure mode (authoritative-until-scanned in-file status) is structurally closed, not re-opened.

### S5.6 — Derivation graph + transitive two-tier stale/invalid demotion cascade dropped (first version since alpha.1 with no multi-hop propagation)

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

No record adjudicates the drop: §11 item (4) compares the manifest gate to 'propagation-only demotion' only for the human-content-protection function, §1 L118-119 mentions 'a demotion cascade' merely as a batch-worklist example, and the docs-history 'Authorship asymmetry in propagation' adapt row targets alpha15, not beta1. On the merits the drop is sound because beta.1's substrate structurally removes what the graph walked: only fulltext plus opt-in digest chunks (keyed by citekey) are retrievable, so supersession's citekey-scoped exclusion covers derived chunks of the same work; export re-verifies every mapped claim at the gate; and verdicts are lazily re-derived at consumption via marker + block-hash + checks agreement instead of eagerly propagated — no machine artifact feeds another at depth ≥ 2 in a correctness-bearing way. Retraction/supersession fallout keeps its recorded consumers (§4 superseded machinery + weekly Crossref sweep) and renders as one batch worklist, honoring both halves of the alpha lesson (never serve stale as current; never flood attention). The silent part is the trade itself, which deserves a named home so the cascade is not re-proposed or its absence mistaken for an oversight.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (§11 item (4) L978-981 covers only the human-protection comparison; §1 L118-119 presupposes a demotion-fallout worklist without a mechanism record)
- **History:** ADR-127/PR-C2 #1167: two-tier demotion (depth-1 demote, depth-≥2 stale-with-framing, retraction one level deeper) was motivated by the build-system stale-vs-invalid lesson — 'so one demoted foundational node cannot cascade a whole subgraph into an attention flood,' with hard exclusion rejected because it 'breaks cross-period queries' (history L2126); lineage runs to alpha.1's fama-exposure superseded_by walk. The mechanism presupposed alpha's multi-hop machine-consumes-machine artifact chains. Beta.1 moots that precondition rather than re-opening the failure: the retrieval substrate has no depth-≥2 machine consumption, and point-of-use verdict re-derivation replaces eager propagation.
- **Action:** Add an §18-style recorded decision (or §11 divergence entry): "Beta.1 carries no derivation graph and no transitive demotion cascade: verdicts are re-derived at consumption (marker + block-hash + `checks` agreement), supersession/retraction fallout routes through the `superseded` consumers (§4) and one batch worklist (§1), and no machine artifact consumes another's output at depth ≥ 2 in the retrieval substrate. Multi-hop propagation is re-earned the day machine outputs begin consuming each other (e.g. digests over digests)."

### S5.7 — Surface-wired apply-rate rubber-stamp detector dropped; capability moved to evaluation-protocol analytics

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

The honesty function survives intact in the charter-designated home: evaluation-protocol §3 reads the disposition stream through the same two-sided bands (sustained accept ≳90% = rubber-stamping, ≲20% = mistuned generator, n-stated with a sample floor) and §5 adds quarterly gate-efficacy sampling ('is review improving correctness or is it theater') that alpha.15 never had. This bands-plus-blind-re-review shape is a recorded decision — the docs-history borrow entry 'Disposition interpretation layer' adopts exactly it — and the charter's scope map assigns all evaluation-scope rows to the protocol, whose pre-registered cadence guarantees the stream is actually read. The docs-history failure pattern this area is prone to (enforcement half shipped, consumption half lost) is satisfied because the consumer is named in the governing documents; the non-backfillable inputs (accept-unedited vs accept-after-edit, decision time) are instrumented from day 1.

- **Recorded:** evaluation-protocol §3 L57-60 (two-sided bands) and §5 L82-85 (gate-efficacy sampling); docs-history borrow row 'Disposition interpretation layer' (L29); charter Scope Map (evaluation scope → evaluation-protocol) and Verdict-basis/Calibration rows
- **History:** ADR-128/PR-B3 #1165 made dispositions first-class non-backfillable telemetry with apply-rate bounds (>0.9 / <0.2) as the rubber-stamp detector because 'this is what makes calibrated falsifiable' — without recorded dispositions the theatre-check cannot be evaluated (history L2114). The motivating function was falsifiability of the review mechanism, an evaluation-time need, not a live-UI need; beta.1 preserves the recorded stream and its two-sided interpretation on the protocol's pre-registered cadence and strengthens it with gate-efficacy re-judging, so the reason alpha held the position is fully addressed in a different mechanism-form.
## 6. Machine judgment / LLM allocation

16 gaps — leave 10 · record 6 · change 0

### S6.1 — Tier-2 LLM tension/contradiction judge dropped; contradiction detection re-homed onto local deberta-NLI as proposer

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design section 13 is an explicit, exhaustive adjudication of which LLM calls the product carries (operation test, applied roster, 'New LLM features must pass the same test') and states the invariant the Tier-2 judge existed to protect: 'every LLM opinion is a proposer,' never a verdict-conferrer. The docs-bar Adapt entry 'Middle-band LLM adjudication' (target beta1) directly adjudicates LLM adjudication on this path: NLI-with-frozen-thresholds stays primary and an LLM survives only as optional paid escalation of the ambiguous 'mentions' band under price-before-click; the Reject table re-kills model-judges-model consensus. The alpha evidence (GBrain's failure, ~28% wrong belief-flips in ConCoRD-class systems) argued against LLM-judge-as-authority, and beta.1's stronger position — no LLM judge at all, per-quote stance chips never aggregated — moves further in the direction that evidence points, so no documented failure is re-opened.

- **Recorded:** design.md s13 L1021-1048 (operation test + roster + 'every LLM opinion is a proposer'); docs-history borrow/adapt/reject: Adapt 'Middle-band LLM adjudication' L79 (target beta1), Reject 'Second-model consensus pre-filter' L107
- **History:** The Tier-2 judge landed only at alpha.15 (PR-AF #1200, history L2170), already hedged as 'a proposer, never an authority,' admissible only on Tier-1 abstain, because LLM-judge-as-authority was rejected on GBrain's failure and ConCoRD-class ~28% wrong belief-flips. Beta.1 honors that motivating evidence a fortiori: it removes the LLM judge entirely, keeps local NLI as proposer with mentions-means-unknown framing (design s8), and records the middle-band paid escalation as the adapted survivor.

### S6.2 — Standalone corpus-wide surface-tensions operation removed; contradiction surfacing folded into Ask only

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The docs-bar Adapt entry 'Corpus contradiction surface' adjudicates exactly this function — point beta.1's existing deberta-NLI at topically-near claim pairs to propose human-confirmed contrasts links aggregated into one pre-draft surface — and targets it at alpha16, which is the recorded decision that beta.1 carries only the in-Ask projection; the companion Reject entry rules 'stance labels + human-confirmed proposals are the ceiling until real data shows missed contradictions costing the researcher.' The charter's Ask bar requires span citations, coverage denominators, and absence-as-absence, not corpus-wide tension detection, so the removal is charter-clean. The earned discipline behind the alpha contract — tri-class with first-class abstain, NLI silence never presented as no-contradiction — survives verbatim in s8's mentions-means-unknown and 'within the retrieved set' framing.

- **Recorded:** docs-history borrow/adapt/reject: Adapt 'Corpus contradiction surface' L81 (target alpha16, 'the full engine stays dead'); Reject 'Full NLI/MaxSAT contradiction engine + autonomous supersession' L128
- **History:** surface-tensions shipped in alpha.11 as an epistemic operation (history L1685) and was re-tiered at alpha.15 onto a pinned NLI comparator with first-class abstain and an FP budget (L2168) because NLI confidently fabricates contradictions on different-variable pairs at 0.94-1.00. Beta.1 carries those measured failure classes into its calibration set (design L676-679) and keeps abstain-first stance semantics; the corpus-wide scope is deferred with a recorded data-driven trigger, so the earned parts are preserved.

### S6.3 — Per-field best-source-wins authority merge (with coverage states and provenance tables) replaced by single-provider empty-field-fill

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The substitution is sound under the charter: beta.1 restores Zotero and citation.doi.org as the primary metadata record, so enrichment is supplementary blank-filling rather than canonical-record construction, and the spike's motivating concern — each provider is incomplete — is answered by surfacing incompleteness (three-valued fields present/absent-in-source/not-yet-fetched, provenance-and-as-of-stamped counts, cap-stamped edges) instead of union-merging it away. The load-bearing never-silent-overwrite invariant survives as per-field left/right diffs through Review, never auto-applied, and auditability survives via the content-addressed payloads store (s18.3). But no authoritative record names the departure from the day-one spike-grounded multi-provider merge: s7 states the JabRef rule without engaging why one provider now suffices where three were required, and s11/s17/s18 are silent on it.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (design s7 L589-613 states the replacement rule and s18.3 records the payloads store, but the merge-subsystem departure itself is unnamed)
- **History:** ADR-30 (alpha.1) chose per-field best-source-wins after two red-team rounds plus an 867-entry spike showing S2/OpenAlex/Crossref each incomplete (reference counts 151/129/146 for the same paper; ORCID in OpenAlex, ~0 in S2) — single-source was rejected on exactly that evidence (history L521-527); alpha.15 PR-F #1173 hardened it with provider_coverage=full|partial|degraded and conflict-raises-attention (L2138). Beta.1 addresses the reason structurally: providers no longer author the record, and their incompleteness is labeled rather than hidden.
- **Action:** Add to the design s11 divergence list (or an s18-style recorded decision): "Enrichment merge: beta.1 drops alpha's per-field multi-provider best-source-wins authority merge (ADR-30's 867-entry spike: every provider incomplete) for single-provider empty-field-fill, because Zotero and citation.doi.org now own the primary record and enrichment is supplementary. Incompleteness is surfaced via three-valued fields, provenance-stamped counts, and cap-stamped edges rather than merged away; conflicts still never silently overwrite (per-field Review diffs)."

### S6.4 — Provider roster narrows to OpenAlex+Crossref; Unpaywall/OA locator dropped; reference edges single-source instead of cross-provider union

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: high

Design s17.3 is the recorded adjudication of the beta.1 provider set: allowlist entries are requirement-driven and named (OpenAlex, GitHub API, pinned citation.doi.org), the Memoria-side OA-PDF fetcher explicitly stays out via the Zotero capture handoff, and further providers (SWH/NCBI) are explicitly deferred; s7 additionally records the fallback trigger (named OA hosts if the handoff measurably fails). Unpaywall's alpha role — OA full-text location as a required promotion input — loses both premises in beta.1: Zotero is the designated PDF capture surface and full text is never a gate (no_pdf is a legal resting state). Single-source reference edges are a direct consequence of the recorded provider-set decision, and the incompleteness they create is honestly labeled (cap-stamped cited-by lines, index-relative coverage wording 'within OpenAlex', discovery output never entering Ask or gap denominators).

- **Recorded:** design.md s17.3 L1249-1252 (tiered allowlist; OA fetcher stays out; SWH/NCBI deferred); s7 L561-567 (Zotero handoff + recorded OA-host fallback), L600-603 (cap-stamped edges), L737-739 (index-relative coverage wording)
- **History:** Unpaywall entered at alpha.4 because an OA copy may have a better text layer (history L1009) and became load-bearing when alpha.14 made acquired full text a hard precondition for checked promotion, requiring the ordered OA retry loop (L1976); the DOI-deduped reference union came from ADR-30's each-provider-incomplete spike (L518). Beta.1 removes the premises (Zotero-first PDFs, land-then-resolve, no checked gate) and re-homes the incompleteness concern as honest labeling.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Partial only. The Unpaywall/OA-locator drop IS adjudicated (design s17.3 L1249-1252 + s7 L561-567: Memoria-side OA-PDF fetcher stays out via the Zotero handoff, with allowlist-violation/zero-interaction-beacon rationale and named OA-host fallback). But the single-source reference-edge delta is not: L600-603 is cap-stamping of the capped cited-by backfill and L737-739 is index-relative coverage wording - consequence handling, not a decision with rationale on dropping A15's cross-provider DOI-deduped union (original ADR-30 rationale: each provider is incomplete). No cited location adjudicates that leg.
- **Verifier notes:** Partial only. The Unpaywall/OA-locator drop IS adjudicated (design s17.3 L1249-1252 + s7 L561-567: Memoria-side OA-PDF fetcher stays out via the Zotero handoff, with allowlist-violation/zero-interaction-beacon rationale and named OA-host fallback). But the single-source reference-edge delta is not: L600-603 is cap-stamping of the capped cited-by backfill and L737-739 is index-relative coverage wording - consequence handling, not a decision with rationale on dropping A15's cross-provider DOI-deduped union (original ADR-30 rationale: each provider is incomplete). No cited location adjudicates that leg.

### S6.5 — Required-provider DOI promotion gate removed; enrichment never gates promotion or bibliography eligibility

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The design body explicitly decides and justifies land-then-resolve ('phase 1 never fails'; failure is a triage stub, never data loss; partial states are legal resting states; flags never block), and the specific harms the alpha gate guarded are re-homed to recorded mechanisms: export refuses — never warns — on a cited superseded/retracted work ('export is the one place the flag must block', s8, recorded as s18.2); Ask excludes superseded works by default with the exclusion counted in the denominator; unverified metadata surfaces as three-valued fields and needs_metadata chips; and the weekly audit probes retraction status. The alpha gate is also charter-incompatible: capture must complete with one initiating action and no mandatory per-item decisions, and requiring three live providers (including Unpaywall) before bibliography eligibility would put provider flakiness between the researcher and the 30-minute first-Ask contract.

- **Recorded:** design.md s7 L524-527 and L514-522 (land-then-resolve, flags never block — explicit decision with rationale); s8 L829-837 (export gate blocks on retracted/superseded); s18.2 L1287-1289
- **History:** ADR-123 (alpha.13) split capture from promotion because 'checked retrieval and references.bib would expose sources before required provider and retraction evidence had been reconciled' (history L1848, L1898) — under the consumable-checked read barrier, promotion was the only place to stop a retracted work reaching bibliography. Beta.1 has no checked read barrier; it blocks the same harm at the point of harm (the export gate) and labels unverified state everywhere else, so the motivating failure is addressed by relocation, not dropped.

### S6.6 — Generalized shadow-first-until-grounded discipline replaced by pre-registered frozen calibration sets; no calibration.yaml floor framework

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The charter itself mandates beta.1's mechanism — 'Checker calibration: Stance/Checker NLI thresholds are tuned on a small pre-registered labeled set before day 1 and frozen; any change is a dated amendment', plus 'every numeric threshold is labeled as a pre-registered guess until beta.1 data calibrates it' — and the charter is the spec, so demanding the calibration.yaml shadow framework back would contradict it. Alpha.15's own recorded endpoint was 'the first grounded thresholds arrive with beta-era disposition data'; beta.1 is that moment, realized as pre-registered tuning (Sainz ~15-point swing evidence) plus a HANS/PAWS launch-blocking floor and dated-amendment discipline (design s7, eval s4). The shadow residue survives exactly where scores remain ungrounded: knobs are 'logged shadow knobs' (s7), disposition bands are placeholder values with sample-floor degradation (eval s3), and beta.1 deliberately carries almost no tunables ('nothing to tune' — the rejected digest-chunk rank boost, s8).

- **Recorded:** requirements charter, Required Evaluation Scope rows 'Calibration' (L50) and 'Checker calibration' (L51); design.md s7 L672-682; evaluation-protocol s4 L62-72
- **History:** ADR-66-to-ADR-129 shadow-first existed because no threshold in the prior corpus was ever validated — every era minted confident numbers from zero data (history L2172; docs-bar patterns section L142) — and alpha.15 explicitly deferred grounding to beta-era data. Beta.1 grounds the one routing-relevant threshold set on hand-labeled data before day 1 and freezes it inside a pre-registered experiment: the failure's addressed form, not its re-opening.

### S6.7 — HANS runtime loud-degraded routing mode dropped; HANS/PAWS survives only as a launch-blocking acceptance test

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The alpha runtime mode protected an architecture beta.1 does not have: in alpha.15 the NLI comparator could gate candidates, so a HANS-failing comparator had to route candidates loudly to ask rather than silently filtering them; in beta.1 the NLI never gates or filters anything — stance failure degrades to mentions-as-unknown, Checker failure rests the claim at m/amber, and s8 explicitly forbids presenting an empty contrasts list as absence of disagreement. The silent-runtime-degradation scenario is also structurally closed: weights are hash-pinned and verified at load (charter Model supply chain row) and any pin change re-triggers fixture validation as a dated amendment, so nothing can change the model between the launch gate and use. The drop is sound, but no record adjudicates it — the design carries HANS only as the launch floor and never names the runtime mode's removal.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (design L679-682 and evaluation-protocol s4 L69-70 record only the launch-gate form; the runtime-mode drop is unnamed in s11/s17/s18)
- **History:** ADR-129's Tier-1 contract (history L2168) made HANS-failure 'a loud degraded mode (cosine/BM25 -> ask, attention raised) — never a silent no-op' because 'NLI shares cosine's lexical-overlap blind spot' and NLI silence must never read as no-contradiction. Beta.1 preserves both underlying invariants (never-silence-as-absence via s8's framing; never-cosine-as-truth via mentions-as-unknown) while removing the candidate-gating role the mode existed to protect.
- **Action:** Add one sentence to the design s11 divergence list (or an s18-style recorded decision): "Alpha's HANS runtime loud-degraded routing mode is not carried: beta.1's NLI never gates or filters candidates (stance fails to mentions-as-unknown, Checker fails to m/amber), model weights are hash-pinned and verified at load, and any pin change re-triggers fixture validation — HANS/PAWS therefore remains a launch-blocking floor only."

### S6.8 — Beat-a-declared-cheap-baseline-or-disable discipline not carried into the s13 operation test

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The discipline's substance is honored: the charter's whole verdict design is a beat-the-cheap-baseline test at product level (parity/payoff against the Zotero+Obsidian+ChatGPT null workflow with same-day counterfactual arms), beta.1's shipped choices each embody it (RRF with no learned weights; the digest-chunk rank boost rejected as an unmeasured tuning knob; eval diagnostic-never-gating), and the docs-bar Borrow 'Feature-triage discipline' records 'every capability names its cheap baseline and must beat it; ship/defer/kill with recorded kills' as adopted process. But the design's own admission gate for future LLM features — the s13 operation test — carries pinned-fixture, seeded-error, deterministic-checkability, and worst-case-price clauses without the comparative beat-a-baseline-or-disable clause, and no record adjudicates that omission: a future operation could pass all four clauses while adding cost over a cheap deterministic equivalent.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (docs-bar Borrow 'Feature-triage discipline' L69 records the discipline at process level, but nothing adjudicates its absence from design s13's operation test, L1021-1031)
- **History:** The alpha rule did concrete work at alpha.15: the retrieval-substrate replacement had to beat a declared baseline on a committed fixture and did not, so qmd stayed (history L2152; ADR-129 'each tier must beat a declared cheap baseline or it is disabled'). Beta.1 addresses the purpose at product level (counterfactual arms) and in its shipped choices, but the standing per-capability gate survives only as a process-level borrow record.
- **Action:** Add a fifth clause to the design s13 operation test: "(5) it names a cheap deterministic baseline (BM25 / no-checks / unranked) and beats it on the operation's fixture, or it stays disabled" — one sentence, making the docs-bar Feature-triage borrow binding on future roster additions rather than process memory.

### S6.9 — Per-operation capability-manifest registry replaced by the prose operation test

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

Every enforcement dimension of the A15 manifest has a structural replacement in beta.1: allowed_tools/paths collapse into engines having no sockets, only two IPC operations, and a staging-plus-read-only-vault filesystem (design §2 L150-156); allowed_network into the compiled egress allowlist + Linux netns (§10 L882-913); untrusted-input sealing into nonce-delimited data blocks (§10 L930-935); io_schema/required_checks into per-engine deterministic validation, Checker NLI, and launch-blocking probe sets (§7 L659-682); prompt_version and model pins into per-run model_id+prompt_v with change-triggered fixture revalidation (§9 L857-861); fail-to-load into Guard failing closed on policy load and workers refusing to start unregistered (§2 L178-180). But no authoritative record adjudicates dropping the per-operation declarative registry itself (risk_class included): §11's converge list covers only the human-span hash-manifest family, §13 defines the operation test without naming the registry it replaces, and the docs-history reject entry on vault-resident prompts cites operations-as-product-code as still live. Sound on the merits, silent as a divergence — record it.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (partial network-dimension coverage only: design §11 back-pressure item 6, L982-983)
- **History:** History L2102/L2144 (ADR-129 as pointer): manifests existed because "no threshold in the prior corpus was ever validated" — the manifest was the hard ceiling, non-sandbox use licensed per (operation, model, mode) by seeded-error verdicts — and because untrusted-input sealing (Greshake/AgentDojo/InjecAgent pressure) needed a fail-to-load enforcement point; the lineage runs from ADR-57 (L663: LLM inference is not batch-invariant — 80 distinct outputs at temperature 0 — so rule-derivable writes are engine code) through alpha.11 operations-as-policy (L1603) to alpha.15's move of manifests into PR-reviewed product code. Beta.1 addresses each motivating reason at shared chokepoints (no sockets, compiled allowlist, nonce sealing, fixtures + pin-change revalidation, Guard fail-closed); only the per-operation declarative artifact is not carried.
- **Action:** Add to design §11: "Alpha.15's per-operation capability-manifest registry (allowed_tools/paths/network, risk_class, required_checks, io_schema, prompt_version; fail-to-load on manifest/sealing violation) is deliberately not carried: its enforcement substance is redistributed to structural chokepoints — engines hold no sockets and exactly two IPC operations over a staging-plus-read-only-vault filesystem (§2), the compiled egress allowlist + netns (§10), nonce-sealed prompt assembly (§10), per-engine schema/anchor validation with fixtures (§7), and per-run model/prompt pins with change-triggered revalidation (§9). Fail-to-load survives as Guard's fail-closed policy load and workers refusing to start unregistered (§2). A per-operation declarative manifest returns only if engine capabilities ever diverge per operation."

### S6.10 — Per-operation dual model pins / --mode / eval select-models / pydantic-ai / two-provider split collapsed into one host + one beta-wide pinned tier

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: medium

Design §9 (L856-861) is an explicit decision-with-rationale that plainly covers the whole collapse: one pinned model tier for the whole beta, a mid-beta tier change is a release marker never silent, every run records exact model_id + prompt_v, and any pin change re-triggers fixture validation against the affected engine before it runs on the real vault — with one tier there is no per-operation pin to hold, no --mode to select, and nothing for eval select-models to choose. The regression review's intact sweep explicitly checked the "per-operation model pins with test/live modes" invariant family and verified it present-or-strengthened in beta.1 substance (review L76). §13's flip conditions (L1056-1058) additionally record when a Memoria-owned pinned-model host would return. pydantic-ai and the Ollama-local/gateway split are implementation stack of the alpha runner, below design-invariant altitude in a clean slate that ships no local generative model at all.

- **Recorded:** design §9 L856-861 (single pinned tier as release marker + pin-change revalidation); regression review "Checked and intact" sweep L76 ("per-operation model pins with test/live modes" verified held); design §13 L1050-1058 (pinned-model-host flip condition)
- **History:** History L2102/L2104: dual runner.test/runner.live pins with --mode existed because "no threshold in the prior corpus was ever validated" — use was licensed only by the live model's seeded-error verdict per (operation, model, mode) — and eval select-models pinned the cheapest passing candidate as a permitted build-time act (an ADR-11 amendment); pydantic-ai became sole typed runner after the Hermes removal (L1940, L2096). Beta.1 keeps the licensing substance (per-run pins; pin/prompt change re-triggers fixture validation before real-vault use, §9) and meets the cost motive with ceilings/batch/caps instead of model shopping; a single frozen tier is additionally an experimental control §13 requires of a pre-registered retention experiment.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Design §9 L856-861 records the new single-tier mechanism (release-marker tier, pin-change revalidation) but never decides the drop of per-operation dual pins, --mode, eval select-models, pydantic-ai, or the local/gateway split — none appear anywhere in the design or §11's divergence list. §13 L1050-1058 is a future hosting flip, tangential. The regression-review sweep line cited actually lists 'per-operation model pins with test/live modes' as verified intact, i.e. it denies the delta rather than adjudicating it (and contradicts the gap entry). No citation adjudicates this collapse.
- **Verifier notes:** Design §9 L856-861 records the new single-tier mechanism (release-marker tier, pin-change revalidation) but never decides the drop of per-operation dual pins, --mode, eval select-models, pydantic-ai, or the local/gateway split — none appear anywhere in the design or §11's divergence list. §13 L1050-1058 is a future hosting flip, tangential. The regression-review sweep line cited actually lists 'per-operation model pins with test/live modes' as verified intact, i.e. it denies the delta rather than adjudicating it (and contradicts the gap entry). No citation adjudicates this collapse.

### S6.11 — B1 adds a unified in-product-vs-agent LLM allocation framework with named flip conditions (no A15 analog)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This delta is an addition whose record is the delta itself: design §13 is a dedicated authoritative section ("Recorded so it is not re-proposed") that states the boundary (Memoria is not an agent; any agent is a quarantined, read-scoped, envelope-writes-only client), the operation test for which LLM calls ship, the deliberate redundancy of paid synthesis, and four named flip conditions with the invariant that in every flip the loop gains standing as a client, never ownership of the write boundary. The gap report's own Appendix C (L316) confirms the agent-boundary substance is a convergence with A15's ADR-130 contract, so nothing alpha earned is contradicted — the framework and flip conditions are net-new governance on top of it.

- **Recorded:** design §13 L998-1058 (entire section; explicitly "Recorded so it is not re-proposed")
- **History:** A15 had no externalization framework because the control-surface-vs-standalone-agent review postdates ADR-129; the lesson §13 codifies is the documented Hermes failure (history L2096: "the framework owned state, workflow, and the write boundary; every integrity mechanism had to be threaded through it" — accepted as the cost of leaving agent frameworks) plus ADR-130's quarantined-client contract, which the gap report's Appendix C verifies beta.1 converges with rather than reverses. Beta.1 does not merely address the reason — it turns it into recorded, falsifiable flip conditions.

### S6.12 — Machine-work unit shifts from named operations to named engines; "operation" demoted to the LLM-call admission test

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

The demotion is itself the recorded decision: design §13 (L1021-1031) fixes the beta.1 meaning of "operation" — "Memoria runs an LLM call directly iff it can be an operation" — in a section marked recorded-so-not-re-proposed, and §2 (L150-156) names the engine roster as the organizing unit. The invariant that made the old vocabulary load-bearing survives verbatim: §13's "Neither side, ever... performs a rule-derivable write (engines write)" (L1046-1048), and the properties the operation unit carried (pinned prompts, fixtures, prices, seeded-error checks) attach per engine call site (§7 digest_prompt_v1, §9 per-run pins + fixture revalidation). Nothing safety-bearing rides on the noun; the shift is organizational and covered by the recorded broader framework.

- **Recorded:** design §13 L1021-1031 (operation test) + L1046-1048 (engines write); design §2 L150-156 (engine roster)
- **History:** ADR-69 (alpha.4, history L2253) named the deterministic layer "operations"; the earned core was ADR-57 (L663): production LLM inference is not batch-invariant (one prompt at temperature 0 produced 80 distinct outputs), so any rule-derivable write must be deterministic engine code, never an LLM; alpha.15 then made operations manifest-pinned product code (L2102). Beta.1 preserves the earned rule word-for-word ("engines write") and keeps pins/fixtures per call site — the motivating failure stays addressed under the new vocabulary.

### S6.13 — Deterministic 6-kind work_aspects read-model replaced by an LLM-extracted, NLI-checked, anchored 5-kind digest

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

The beta.1 side is a fully recorded decision-with-rationale: design §7's DigestEngine (L648-682) specifies the pinned prompt, the MASSW-aligned kind set with the projected_impact exclusion reasoned ("speculation, not extraction"), verbatim-anchor validation with the anchor_hallucination fail state, per-claim NLI checking against concatenated anchors, distrust inheritance, and calibration-set-tuned frozen thresholds with a launch-blocking HANS/PAWS probe; §13 (L1033-1035) admits the digest through the recorded operation test. The docs-history adapt entry "MASSW aspect structure" (L97, target beta1) is a recorded adjudication that aspect structure lives as fixed digest.md headings — no schema, no fields — so section-scoped search survives. The move to LLM extraction does not re-open an earned failure: A15's own digest lineage was already LLM work under output contracts (alpha.11 wp5, docs-history borrow L48), and beta.1 guards it with exactly the check machinery alpha earned.

- **Recorded:** design §7 L648-682 (DigestEngine decision with rationale) + §13 L1033-1035 (LLM-call roster); docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L97 (adapt: MASSW aspect structure → fixed digest.md headings, target beta1)
- **History:** History L2148: the work_aspects read model was ADR-99/MASSW aspects accepted "via the DB work_aspects read model... Keep files simple" — motivated by structure-for-search without author-facing YAML and by the cheap deterministic path, not by a documented failure of LLM extraction; A15 concurrently ran LLM digests under engine output contracts (alpha.11 wp5-operation-digest, docs-history L48). Beta.1 keeps the MASSW structure and answers the LLM-consistency concern (ADR-57's non-batch-invariance evidence) with deterministic validation, verbatim-anchor checks, NLI promotion, and frozen calibrated thresholds rather than with determinism of extraction.

### S6.14 — Seeding relevance prefilter moves from deterministic (steering.md) to a paid LLM call

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The call site is individually named in an authoritative record: design §13's applied roster (L1033-1035) lists "the seeding relevance prefilter (§7)" as one of exactly three product LLM calls, "now with the rule stated" — i.e., adjudicated against the recorded operation test (pinned, deterministically checkable, arithmetic worst-case price, per-item corpus-scale). §7 (L684-687) records its shape and rationale: an optional cheap yes/no filter over the seeding batch to skip irrelevant works before digest spend, inside the ≤30-minute first-Ask contract. The A15 mechanism it nominally replaces served a different job (deterministic steering.md ranking of discovery candidates), and steering.md's removal is separately grounded in the gap report's verified corrections (Appendix C, L317).

- **Recorded:** design §13 L1033-1035 (applied LLM-call roster naming the prefilter) + §7 L684-687 (mechanism and purpose)
- **History:** History L2162 (ADR-92 as pointer): A15's relevance scoring was deterministic because "the cheap deterministic path clears the bar; ML deferred until data exists" — a cost/data judgment about ranking provider-discovered candidates against steering.md, not an earned failure of LLM prefilters. Beta.1's call is a different, bounded job (yes/no relevance of the researcher's own seeding batch against a live question, before paid digesting), optional and priced, and it is admitted through the operation test that beta.1 requires of every product LLM call — the alpha reason (don't spend ML where cheap suffices) is honored by making the spend optional, tiny, and previewed.

### S6.15 — Local machine-judgment models fixed to exact installer-bundled, hash-gated int8 ONNX pins

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is a pure strengthening mandated by the charter: the Required Trust Scope "Model supply chain" row (requirements L78) demands that bundled local model weights (embeddings, NLI) be hash-pinned and verified at load so a poisoned checker cannot silently pass claims. Design §8 (L751-756) realizes it exactly — bge-small-en-v1.5 int8 ONNX and deberta-v3-base-mnli-fever-anli int8 ONNX, installer-bundled and never downloaded at runtime, pins in `meta`, mismatch refusing with `mem rebuild --embeddings`. Nothing alpha earned is dropped; the per-operation-pin posture is narrowed to exact pins plus supply-chain verification, which is the stronger form of the same discipline.

- **Recorded:** requirements charter, Required Trust Scope "Model supply chain" row (L78); design §8 L751-756
- **History:** A15 pinned local models to bound drift and license use by seeded-error verdicts (ADR-129 runner policy, history L2102; the pinned local NLI comparator with HANS acceptance gate, L2168 — motivated by NLI's lexical-overlap blind spot). Beta.1 keeps the pin-and-gate posture (the same HANS-style probe set is launch-blocking in §7) and adds the supply-chain hash verification the charter newly requires; no motivating failure is re-opened.

### S6.16 — {0,1,2}-ordinal checked-input gap scoring + saturation band dropped; gap analysis becomes retrieval-coverage counting with a printed denominator

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Two authoritative records cover the drop. The charter's Deliberate Exclusion "Aggregate evidence scores" (requirements L85: vote-counting style meters mislead more than they help for beta.1) directly covers a summed 0..8 ordinal score with bands and a count-based saturation badge (≥1 support AND ≥1 counterpoint is a vote count), and the Calibration row (L50) forbids exactly the pre-registered fixed numbers such a band would need. The docs-history borrow table records the full kit — gap taxonomy with fill-or-scope-out disposition (L51) and "Saturation as an operational stop signal" with refutation floor and researcher stamp (L52) — as alpha.16 writing-module targets, restated in recommended action 10 (L157), matching the bullet's deferred-not-deleted reading. Beta.1 keeps what the charter does require (gaps with printed denominators, §8 L782-788) and carries the declining-yield reframe in §7's discovery continuation lines (per-run gain framing, "declining yield within OpenAlex as of <date>", L736-739).

- **Recorded:** requirements charter Deliberate Exclusions, "Aggregate evidence scores" (L85) + Calibration row (L50); docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L51-52 (gap-analysis mechanism kit; saturation as stop signal — target alpha16) + recommended action 10 (L157)
- **History:** History L2160: the ordinal scoring + saturation block absorbed ADR-79's saturation floor with checked-only inputs "so unverified content can't drive the compose-flow phase signal"; the earned core (L969-971, ADR-77/79 as pointers) was that below a maturity floor structural confidence is the automation-bias failure, saturation needs a refutation floor (Popper) plus a PI stamp, and "lowering this threshold is a safety change, not a preference" — and the whole thing was advisory, never gating. Beta.1 does not re-open that failure: it ships no phase-confidence meter at all rather than a weakened one, and the checked-inputs guard has no unchecked signal left to protect since the compose-phase signal is deferred wholesale to alpha.16 where the recorded kit preserves the refutation floor and stamp.
## 7. Catalog / bibliographic authority

7 gaps — leave 5 · record 2 · change 0

### S7.1 — Bibliographic fidelity authority moves to full CSL-JSON in record.md

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §3 states the decision with its rationale in the body: 'Full CSL-JSON is serialized into record.md as a fenced code block (the derived DB is rebuildable, so bibliographic fidelity and the Zotero re-import key cannot live only in the DB)', and §11 books the overall storage shape under Converges ('SQLite authority + markdown keep-set + blobs'). This is not the 'frontmatter-only catalog' ADR-124 rejected: everything ADR-124 said belonged in SQLite — durable worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates, projections — stays DB-side in beta.1 (§5: works.status, jobs, the payloads store, checks), and works.csl_json remains a rebuildable projection. Expanding the alpha.12 compact survival copy to full CSL-JSON strengthens the very survival property the compact copy existed to serve (charter Success Claim 4), while the relational working state that 'fails the survival test' stays in the DB.

- **Recorded:** design.md §3 L224-226 (decision + rationale), §11 L965 (Converges: 'SQLite authority + markdown keep-set + blobs'), §5 L429-444 (two-DB-classes split)
- **History:** Alpha.12's keep-test flip (ADR-122; history L1896, L1800) moved the catalog to SQLite because the *relational catalog graph* was working state failing the survival test, while denormalizing a compact citation survival copy into keep-set files after the cross-store spike FAILED (L1776, L1804). ADR-124 (L2042) rejected a frontmatter-only catalog because 'alpha.14 needs durable worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates, and generated projections better represented in SQLite.' Beta.1 addresses both reasons: all of that machinery remains DB-side; only per-work bibliographic fidelity and the re-import key move to markdown.

### S7.2 — Citekey becomes the works primary key, pinned at import, with correction as a revertible rename run

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: high

Design §7's 'Import fragility rules (each a documented historical failure)' directly confronts the exact failure that motivated alpha.11's demotion: citekeys are pinned at import (inherited from BBT or minted collision-checked), correction is a first-class revertible rename run that fixes directory, links, anchors, and manifest atomically, and work paths use collision-safe encoding. The docs-history Borrow entry 'Citekey stability' (L40) is a recorded decision adopting precisely this shape, naming the drift-orphans-everything failure; §17.6 records the one-key-namespace resolution against the superseded IF-design's 'identity law', with the immutable Zotero key retained as csl_json.custom.zotero_key for idempotent upsert. The alpha failure (unpinned keys drift on metadata correction) is addressed head-on rather than re-opened.

- **Recorded:** design.md §7 L569-579 (import fragility rules), §17.6 L1261-1264 (BBT citekeys inherited); docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L40 ('Citekey stability')
- **History:** Alpha.11 §6.1 (history L1631) made the catalog path an immutable source_id because 'citekeys are metadata-derived and get corrected, so they are a generated display/export alias, never the path' — fixture-verified across a citekey correction. Beta.1 addresses that failure by removing the drift (pin-at-import; upstream regeneration cannot silently rename) and making the residual correction case a single atomic revertible run, while the immutable identity function survives as the Zotero key in csl_json.custom.zotero_key.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Partially adjudicated only. Pin-at-import and correction-as-revertible-rename ARE decided with rationale (design §7 L569-579 'each a documented historical failure'; docs-history L40 Citekey-stability borrow row). But the headline delta — citekey becoming the works PRIMARY KEY, reversing alpha.11's demotion of citekey to optional alias — is nowhere decided: §5 L374 is a bare schema line, §17.6 L1261-1264 adjudicates key-namespace inheritance (BBT keys, one collision-checked namespace), not the key's role as PK vs work_id/Zotero-item-key identity. The gap entry itself says this 'silently diverges' from the IF-design identity law; §18's recorded decisions do not cover it either. Citation is tangential to the core delta.
- **Verifier notes:** Partially adjudicated only. Pin-at-import and correction-as-revertible-rename ARE decided with rationale (design §7 L569-579 'each a documented historical failure'; docs-history L40 Citekey-stability borrow row). But the headline delta — citekey becoming the works PRIMARY KEY, reversing alpha.11's demotion of citekey to optional alias — is nowhere decided: §5 L374 is a bare schema line, §17.6 L1261-1264 adjudicates key-namespace inheritance (BBT keys, one collision-checked namespace), not the key's role as PK vs work_id/Zotero-item-key identity. The gap entry itself says this 'silently diverges' from the IF-design identity law; §18's recorded decisions do not cover it either. Citation is tangential to the core delta.

### S7.3 — Generated bibliography input flips SQLite → stored CSL-JSON; BBT auto-export demoted to optional cross-check

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

§17.6 records the resolution verbatim: 'bibliography.bib remains Memoria-generated and complete, the BBT export an optional cross-check', and §7 L584-587 states it in the body with the completeness rationale (non-Zotero works must appear). The docs-history Reject entry 'Zotero anti-patterns' (L123) is the recorded adjudication of the BBT .bib-ingest alternative ('a second source of truth with built-in staleness and sync races — beta.1 chose the local API for this reason'). Alpha's generated-projection invariant (references.bib never capture-time or user-maintained) is preserved unchanged; only the projection's input moved with the authority re-scoping adjudicated in S7.1, and alpha.12's crash-consistency reason for SQLite-first rendering is covered by beta.1's run/snapshot cross-store recoverability contract (§6, booked in §11 Converges).

- **Recorded:** design.md §17.6 L1261-1264, §7 L584-587; docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L123 ('Zotero anti-patterns')
- **History:** Alpha.12 rendered references.bib from checked SQLite rows behind a crash-recovery barrier — 'citation metadata and the expected references.bib payload/hash are committed to SQLite first' (history L1862), and ADR-124's consequence kept it 'a generated projection from checked catalog rows, not a capture-time or user-maintained file' (L1972). Beta.1 keeps the generated-never-user-maintained invariant and covers crash consistency with the one-writer + staging + run-scoped-snapshot contract instead of the SQLite-first barrier.

### S7.4 — Single root references.bib splits into vault-level Memoria/bibliography.bib plus per-export cited-only references.bib

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: medium

Each half of the split is individually mandated by an authoritative record, so the conjunction is governed even though no single sentence names 'the split': the complete vault-level bibliography.bib realizes charter Success Claim 4 ('standard bibliography files' surviving the tool) and is recorded with rationale in §7 L584-587 and §17.6; the per-export cited-only references.bib realizes the charter Compose row ('export markdown plus BibTeX with resolving citations') and is specified in §8's export run. The relocation from vault root into Memoria/ follows from §3's ruling zero-migration boundary ('the user's existing vault, untouched' — Memoria writes only inside Memoria/). Alpha's single-root layout was never earned by a failure, and both artifacts derive from the same stored CSL-JSON, so no second-source-of-truth race is introduced.

- **Recorded:** requirements charter L22-23 (Success Claim 4) and L32 (Compose row); design.md §7 L584-587 + §17.6 L1261-1264 (complete generated bibliography), §8 L838-839 (per-export cited-only .bib), §3 L191 (vault untouched outside Memoria/)
- **History:** None found — the single root references.bib was layout convention, not a position earned by a documented failure; the invariant alpha did earn (the .bib is a generated projection, never user-maintained; history L1972) is preserved by both beta.1 artifacts.

### S7.5 — Zotero-owned citation-facing fields corrected at source, not locked vault-side

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §7 L606-610 is an explicit decision-with-rationale in the body, naming the rejected alternative: fields the researcher's Zotero owns 'are corrected at source (deep link to the Zotero item; the next sync confirms) rather than locked vault-side — a vault fork of bibliographic truth would diverge from the keep-test bibliography.' The alpha position it partially reverses was driven by the alpha.14 standalone-CLI premise, which the beta.1 charter itself supersedes: Zotero is a required Capture input and the null-workflow baseline, and beta.1 is a plugin+daemon (§11 item 10), not a standalone CLI. The delta does not reintroduce live-on-demand external truth (ADR-124's other rejected alternative): the correction propagates via sync into a durable vault copy (full CSL-JSON in record.md), non-Zotero works stay wholly vault-owned, and re-import never clobbers a diverged record.md (§7 L558-559).

- **Recorded:** design.md §7 L606-610 (explicit 'rather than locked vault-side' decision with rationale); charter L11 + Capture row L29 (Zotero as required input / null-workflow baseline)
- **History:** ADR-124 (history L2042) made the catalog THE citation authority because 'Alpha.14 makes Memoria a standalone CLI/engine. A required Zotero library or live Better BibTeX auto-export would violate that', and rejected live API-on-demand metadata for drift. Beta.1 removes the standalone premise by charter, and avoids the drift failure because the vault always retains its own durable CSL-JSON copy — corrections flow through sync into it rather than being read live.

### S7.6 — catalog/ + entities/ folder tree dropped for per-work co-location and DB-side entity queries

The nav-home function of catalog/index.md is preserved by a different recorded mechanism: §3's generated per-directory index.md projections, which the charter's Knowledge-format row requires at alpha.15 parity. The remaining folder-layout difference (works/<citekey>/ co-location instead of a catalog/ tree) is plainly covered by the §3 layout decision and continues, rather than reverses, the alpha.14 direction of removing markdown entity Concepts.

- **Recorded:** docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L111 ('Entity note types'); design.md §7 L615-631, §17.5 L1258-1260, §3 L242-246 (index.md projections); charter Knowledge-format row L36

Beta.1 extends the same position (entities DB-side, lazy point-of-use adjudication) rather than re-opening any failure; the only alpha artifact dropped is the projection folder shell, whose navigation function the OKF index projections replace.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Half adjudicated. But the other half — dropping the catalog/ + catalog/sources/ tree and catalog/index.md nav home for per-work co-location under works/<citekey>/ — has no decision or rationale at any cited location: it appears only as the §3 vault-layout listing (a design fact, not an adjudication), and §3 L242-246 / charter L36 concern index.md projection generation and OKF parity ('no regression of the exchange format'), which if anything cut against silently dropping the alpha.15 catalog projections rather than adjudicating the drop.

### S7.7 — Zotero re-centered: day-1 import, Zotero-first reading with annotation sync-back, PDFs copied into vault

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Every component is a recorded resolution: §17.1 records 'Reading is Zotero-first' (primary read in Zotero's reader, append-only annotation sync, exact-quote anchor bridge, fulltext.md demoted to evidence substrate and kept as the full path for non-Zotero works), §17.3 records the OA-fetcher exclusion via the capture-in-Zotero handoff, §11 back-pressure item 1 records Zotero import at fidelity as priority-1 scope, the docs-history Reject entry (L123) records copying PDFs into works/<citekey>/source.pdf because deep links 'make the corpus die with Zotero's install', and the charter names Zotero as a required Capture input and the null-workflow baseline. The alpha.14 demotion was driven by the standalone-CLI product boundary, which the beta.1 charter deliberately replaces, and Zotero is primary/default, not required — non-Zotero paths stay first-class. The alpha.11 §13 invariant that Memoria owns its own quote/span/hash selectors is honored in substance: Zotero annotations never become anchor authority — each is bridged by exact-quote match into Memoria's own fulltext.md ^pNNNN anchors (with DB text_sha256), and misses are counted as orphans, never silently dropped.

- **Recorded:** design.md §17.1 L1241-1244, §17.3 L1249-1252, §11 L974-976 (priority 1), §7 L554-567 + L697-720; charter L11 + Capture row L29; docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L123 (deep links rejected)
- **History:** Alpha.14 removed the Zotero import surface because 'Alpha.14 makes Memoria a standalone CLI/engine. A required Zotero library... would violate that' (history L1916, L1982, L2042) — a premise the beta.1 charter reverses by making Zotero the measured null workflow and a required import. Alpha.11 §13 held 'Zotero annotations are not an alpha.11 import path; Memoria-owned PDF capture stores canonical quote/span/hash selectors itself' (L1681) so spans resolve regardless of parser (W3C selector subset, L1633); beta.1 addresses that reason by keeping canonical anchors Memoria-owned (the exact-quote bridge earns anchors in Memoria's fulltext; orphans are counted), making the sync-back an input channel, not a selector authority.
## 8. Discovery / gap analysis

4 gaps — leave 3 · record 1 · change 0

### S8.1 — Argument-graph/saturation/note-mode gap analysis dropped; B1 gap analysis is retrieval-coverage only

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The entire dropped stack is adjudicated in the docs-history borrow/adapt/reject file: the Borrow rows 'Argument graph distinct from knowledge map', 'Gap-analysis mechanism kit' (which carries the under-warranted/fragility/conflict/structural/unstated-warrant/refutation taxonomy and structural-impact ranking), and 'Saturation as an operational stop signal' all target alpha16, and Recommended action 10 seeds the alpha.16 writing module with exactly this dossier — a deferral with a named home, not a silent drop. The saturation-score component is separately barred by the charter's 'Aggregate evidence scores' Deliberate Exclusion, which is decisive. The beta.1 charter's Compose bar requires only 'show gaps', which B1's printed-denominator coverage gaps meet, and the honesty core of the alpha machinery (never present machine confidence on sparse evidence) survives strengthened as the empty-contrasts refusal and denominator discipline in design §8.

- **Recorded:** docs-history B/A/R Borrow rows L50-52 (argument graph, gap-analysis kit, saturation — all Target alpha16) + Recommended action 10 (L157); requirements charter Deliberate Exclusions 'Aggregate evidence scores' (L85); design §8 L782-796 (coverage-gap mechanism of record)
- **History:** The alpha.5 Project gate (ADR-77/78/79, structural_impact.py; history L945-990) was built so a project 'knows when to stop': the maturity floor was 'the gate's trust switch… not a knob to tune', the ≥1-contradicts refutation floor encoded Popper against corroboration-only theses, and the taxonomy answered 'a project can have zero missing notes and still be intellectually bankrupt'; ADR-129 absorbed the saturation floor into alpha.15's native gap engine (history L2160), and ADR-126's note modes fed it (L2076). The position was earned by design reasoning — no production vault ever existed, so no incident backs it — and beta.1 addresses its motivating honesty concern by other means (empty-contrasts refusal, suspect-not-covered accounting) while deferring the argument machinery to its natural consumer, the alpha.16 writing module.

### S8.2 — Topic/concept-graph-driven discovery dropped; B1 discovery is bounded citation-graph only

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The delta is plainly covered by the amended charter Deliberate Exclusion, which admits only bounded citation-graph discovery and keeps 'open-ended search and recommender feeds' out — topic/concept co-occurrence candidate generation is a recommender leg outside the admitted bound — and by design §7's explicit heading decision 'Discovery (bounded citation-graph only)' with its recorded rationale (transparent occurrence counting, 'never a black-box recommender — that is the echo-chamber counter'), folded in via §17(4). The kept citation leg is positively grounded (Hirt et al. 2023; BibliZap occurrence-count scoring, info-flow verdict adopt) while the topic/concept leg was re-derived as out on evidence (VOSviewer/CiteSpace field-scale mapping non-transferable to a single-researcher corpus, verdict avoid), so the drop is a governed scoping decision, not an omission.

- **Recorded:** requirements charter Deliberate Exclusions, discovery row amended 2026-07-03 (L84); design §7 L722-739 ('bounded citation-graph only', occurrence-counting rationale); design §17(4) L1253-1257
- **History:** The topic/concept/keyword/authorship edge routing was a late alpha.13/14 build only weeks old at the clean slate: OpenAlex topics/concepts/keywords/mesh/SDG plus Crossref relation rows were imported into work_graph_edges so 'the graph feeds retrieval query expansion and gap analysis' and discovery candidates could be proposed from graph edges, ranked by ADR-92's deterministic relevance (history L1978, L1992, L2004-2006, L2162). It was an additive enhancement, not a position earned by a documented failure — no recorded incident shows concept-graph discovery fixing anything — so beta.1's reversion to the evidence-backed citation-graph leg leaves no unaddressed failure behind.

### S8.3 — steering.md program-memory file + Librarian persona + PI-priority discovery weighting removed

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The delta is sound on the merits but only partially governed: the Librarian persona removal is covered by design §13's recorded no-agent boundary ('Memoria is not an agent, and beta.1 adds none', with the Hermes-failure and unpriceable-worst-case rationale), the Librarian's external-API gap-driven discovery is an explicit docs-history Adapt decision ('alpha.16+ decision, never silent creep'), and priority-weighted ranking is displaced by §7's recorded transparent-occurrence-counting decision — but the steering.md program-memory function (standing open questions / priorities as the researcher's discovery lever, unbroken from alpha.1) has zero mentions anywhere in the beta.1 design and no record adjudicates its removal; the gap report itself concedes it is 'un-re-homed for beta.1'. On the merits the drop is defensible: beta.1 discovery is human-triggered with per-run ceilings, capped digest notes, human-signed continuation, and a seen/rejected ledger, so direction comes structurally from seed choice, and the program-memory substance disperses to project.md questions, gaps.md, and ruled-out.md. No safety/honesty invariant is lost and no charter requirement is contradicted, so this is silent-but-fine, needing a recorded divergence rather than a design change.

- **Recorded:** nowhere — silent for the steering.md/program-memory drop (the design body, §11 convergence list, and §18 never name steering.md or the Librarian); adjacent partial records: design §13 L1006-1019 (no-agent boundary), docs-history B/A/R Adapt 'Gap-driven discovery of unheld sources' (L99), design §7 L728-731 (transparent ranking)
- **History:** research-focus.md ships in alpha.1 as 'program memory — the PI's standing steering' that the Librarian (consolidated at ADR-48 from the Old Skeleton roster) reads at session start 'to weight discovery' (history L84, L237, L323-334); alpha.11 renames it steering.md as the Karpathy program.md-equivalent — 'Direction is authored as the program, not the content' (L1671); ADR-92 lands deterministic steering.md relevance ranking at alpha.15 (L2162). The risk it guarded — discovery volume overwhelming human triage without written direction (ADR-61's adoption conditions demanded a maintained research-focus.md precisely against inbox flooding, L547) — is addressed in beta.1 by structural caps and human-triggered rounds rather than relevance weighting; the standing priorities file itself is the one function beta.1 neither carries nor re-homes.
- **Action:** Append to design §18 'Recorded decisions' (or the §11 divergence list): "**Librarian + steering.md removed (recorded divergence).** Beta.1 ships no agent persona and no standing priorities file: §13's no-agent boundary retires the Librarian, discovery ranking is transparent occurrence-counting over researcher-chosen seeds (§7) so seed choice is the steering lever, and steering.md's program-memory function disperses to project.md questions, gaps.md, and ruled-out.md. The Librarian's external-API gap-driven discovery remains an alpha.16+ allowlist decision (docs-history B/A/R); if beta data shows snowball rounds surfacing low-relevance candidates despite seed choice, a researcher-authored priorities input to ranking is the recorded revive path."

### S8.4 — ADR-95's alpha.15 rejection (no always-on discovery loop) reversed by B1's daemon + scheduled citation monitor

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both halves of the reversal are deliberate, recorded decisions: the no-daemon premise is reversed by design §1's reasoned two-process daemon (crash isolation, one network choke point, plugin-supervised and resident only while Obsidian is open — not an unattended VPS), and the scheduled monitor is admitted by a dated charter amendment (Deliberate Exclusions, 2026-07-03) plus §17(4), scoped to identifiers-only egress, one capped machine note per schedule, and output excluded from Ask/gap denominators. The alpha.15 ADR-95 rejection rested solely on the ADR-125 no-daemon premise, which beta.1 removed on its own recorded grounds; the deeper reasons behind every earlier deferral — inbox flooding, silent cron failure, egress creep, experiment confounding — are each addressed (capped visible note through the exfiltration linter and loudness ladder, no auto-ingest: items enter only via human disposition through the normal import ladder, identifiers-only guard_log, intake provenance logged for payoff attribution). The docs-history Reject row keeps the *autonomous ingestion* form dead, and B1's propose-only monitor honors that substance.

- **Recorded:** requirements charter Deliberate Exclusions, discovery row 'Amended 2026-07-03' (L84); design §17(4) L1253-1257; design §7 L740-744 (citation monitor + T5 ingress); design §1 L51-65 (daemon decision with rationale)
- **History:** ADR-61 (alpha.1) deferred the nightly loop with named risks — 'silent cron failure' and 'inbox flooding' — and adoption conditions (written screening plan, maintained research-focus.md ≥4 weeks, always-on infrastructure; history L541-547); alpha.5 declined it again since gap-pull worked on demand and the conditions were unmet (L1059); the alpha.15 sweep rejected the unbundled ADR-95 purely on the ADR-125 no-daemon premise; docs-history Reject L108 keeps nightly *autonomous* discovery dead (triage bottleneck, allowlist, no agent-initiated ingestion, experiment confounding). Beta.1 removes the no-daemon premise deliberately and answers each underlying risk: the monitor is capped, visible, propose-only, identifiers-only, and out of coverage denominators — the unattended-ingestion core of every prior rejection stays unbuilt.
## 9. Ingest / enrichment graph

14 gaps — leave 9 · record 5 · change 0

### S9.1 — Graph import narrowed: alpha.14 topic/concept/keyword/MeSH/SDG/authorship + Crossref-relation wave, reference union, and research_area classification dropped; capped cited-by added

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

Parts of this delta are governed — authorship re-homing to DB entities is recorded in design s17 #5, and the capped cited-by edge is specified with rationale in s7 (L600-603) and licensed by the charter's amended discovery exclusion ('capped citation monitor') — but the headline narrowing is silent: nothing in design s11-s18, the docs-history tables, or the charter adjudicates dropping the alpha.14 topic/concept/keyword/MeSH/SDG and Crossref-relation edge wave, the DOI-deduped multi-provider reference union, or the research_area classification (grep of the design for topic/keyword/mesh/research_area returns nothing relevant; s11's convergence/back-pressure list omits it). The drop is sound on the merits: every alpha consumer of those edges (facet queries, retrieval query expansion, topic-coverage gap analysis) is absent from beta.1's architecture, and the deleted-docs synthesis itself warns that 'a mechanism without a named consumer decays into decoration'; the ADR-30 spike's provider-incompleteness finding is honored by index-relative, cap-stamped coverage wording instead of a union.
