The gap report's 'convergence, not a silent regression' claim rests on two beta documents agreeing with each other, which is not an authoritative record of the divergence from alpha.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (partial coverage only: design s17 #5 for authorship->entities; design s7 L600-603 + s17 #4 + charter amended discovery exclusion for capped cited-by)
- **History:** Alpha.14 built the wide graph because 'the graph feeds retrieval query expansion and gap analysis' (alpha.14 design s8/s10; history L1978) and gap analysis counted topic/keyword edge terms as coverage evidence (L2004); research_area was seeded mechanically from OpenAlex topics so the facet vocabulary stays drift-free, 'removing one whole class of drift at intake' (L217-218); the reference union was earned by ADR-30's 867-entry spike showing all three providers disagree and are each incomplete (151/129/146 reference counts; L518-521), hardened in alpha.15 ADR-129 (L2138). Beta.1 addresses these reasons by removing the consumers rather than the honesty: no facet layer exists (meaning-only frontmatter), retrieval is FTS5+sqlite-vec over fulltext, and discovery coverage wording is index-relative and cap-stamped ('declining yield within OpenAlex as of <date>'), so single-source incompleteness is disclosed, not misrepresented.
- **Action:** Add to design s11 (divergence list): 'Diverges from alpha.14/15 on enrichment-graph scope: the topic/concept/keyword/MeSH/SDG/authorship and Crossref-relation edge import (#1139-#1155) and the OpenAlex-topic-seeded research_area classification are deliberately not carried — their consumers (facet queries, retrieval query expansion, topic-coverage gap analysis) do not exist in beta.1, and an edge type without a named consumer is decoration. edges holds only outgoing references, capped cited-by, and paper<->repo links, all feeding discovery (s7). Reference edges are single-source (OpenAlex); the alpha.13-era spike finding that no provider's reference list is complete is honored by index-relative, cap-stamped coverage wording rather than a multi-provider union.'
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Two fixes to the proposed s11 text, keeping everything else: (1) replace "edges holds only outgoing references, capped cited-by, and paper<->repo links, all feeding discovery (s7)" with "edges holds only outgoing references, capped cited-by, and the paper<->repo typed edge (s5); the citation edges feed bounded discovery (s7), the repo edge joins paper and repo works"; (2) replace "the alpha.13-era spike finding that no provider's reference list is complete" with "the alpha.1-era ADR-30 spike finding (867-entry library; reference counts 151/129/146 for the same paper across S2/OpenAlex/Crossref), re-affirmed by alpha.15's ADR-129 ('no single provider is complete')". Location (s11) is sound — it is the design's alpha-relationship section and the natural home for a Diverges paragraph beside the existing Converges list.

### S9.2 — Enrichment-gates-promotion (three required providers) replaced by land-then-resolve; Unpaywall and required-provider orchestration dropped

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: high

The replacement is an explicit decision-with-rationale in the design body: s7 declares 'partial states are legal resting states' (L514-516) and 'Inputs — land, then resolve... phase 1 never fails; resolution is a separately visible, retryable step (failure is a triage stub, never data loss)' (L524-527), with enrichment explicitly reduced to merge policy ('fills empty fields only — the JabRef rule', L589-592). The Unpaywall drop is plainly covered by s17 #3 (requirement-driven named allowlist entries; the OA-PDF fetcher — Unpaywall's only beta.1 consumer — stays out). ADR-123's motivating failure (retraction and unverified metadata exposed through checked retrieval and references.bib) is re-homed rather than re-opened: registry-authored metadata with the >=0.95 title-match rule, the s18 #2 export refusal on cited superseded/retracted works, and the charter's own 'source-trust remains separate from check status' Provenance row, which dissolves the alpha 'checked source' promotion concept the gate protected.

- **Recorded:** design s7 L514-527 + L589-592 (land-then-resolve, merge-policy-only enrichment); s17 #3 L1249-1252 (Unpaywall/OA out, tiered allowlist); s18 #2 L1287-1289 (export refuses on retracted/superseded); charter Required Trust/Provenance rows
- **History:** The alpha gate was earned by a documented failure: alpha.12's capture-source 'could still promote a scholarly DOI to checked before any provider evidence had been fetched or reconciled — so bibliography output and retrieval could expose sources whose metadata, OA status, and retraction state were unverified' (ADR-123 Context; history L1842, L1848, L1858 — the retraction/conflict gate blocked promotion and never materialized references.bib). Beta.1 addresses that reason with different mechanisms: a trusted registry authors metadata (untrusted PDF text only nominates identifiers), identity conflicts flag as needs_metadata and never merge, the export gate refuses on retracted/superseded cited works (s18 #2), and the weekly citation audit probes superseded resurfacing — so the exposure the gate prevented is caught at the honesty surfaces instead of at import.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Half-adjudicated. Design s7 L524-527/L589-592 does decide land-then-resolve with rationale (phase 1 never fails; triage stub never data loss; JabRef empty-fields-only merge). But the Unpaywall + required-provider-orchestration drop is adjudicated nowhere cited: 'Unpaywall' has zero hits in the governing design; s17 #3 names only the OA-PDF fetcher, SWH/NCBI, and the three admitted hosts; s18 #2 is the export-gate widening (R2) — tangential to enrichment-gating-promotion; charter Trust/Provenance rows contain nothing about enrichment, promotion, or providers. The release's own verify-findings (gap-verify-findings L279-280) confirm the 'required-provider gate collapsed and Unpaywall dropped' delta is absent from the design.
- **Verifier notes:** Half-adjudicated. Design s7 L524-527/L589-592 does decide land-then-resolve with rationale (phase 1 never fails; triage stub never data loss; JabRef empty-fields-only merge). But the Unpaywall + required-provider-orchestration drop is adjudicated nowhere cited: 'Unpaywall' has zero hits in the governing design; s17 #3 names only the OA-PDF fetcher, SWH/NCBI, and the three admitted hosts; s18 #2 is the export-gate widening (R2) — tangential to enrichment-gating-promotion; charter Trust/Provenance rows contain nothing about enrichment, promotion, or providers. The release's own verify-findings (gap-verify-findings L279-280) confirm the 'required-provider gate collapsed and Unpaywall dropped' delta is absent from the design.

### S9.3 — Automatic OA-PDF / full-text acquisition (Unpaywall->OpenAlex->Crossref retry loop) removed; capture-in-Zotero handoff instead

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Fully adjudicated in two authoritative places: design s7 (L561-567) decides 'a Memoria-side OA-PDF fetcher stays out (an auto-fetch at import time is both an allowlist violation and a zero-interaction beacon)' with a recorded fallback (named OA hosts arXiv/Europe PMC if the handoff measurably fails), and s17 #3 records the same as an information-flow resolution 'so it is not re-litigated'. The alpha loop's reason for existing is dissolved rather than ignored: no_pdf is a legal resting state, indexed (not digested) is the payoff state, and digests are opt-in, so a dead OA URL can no longer block a work. The handoff also adds zero egress since Zotero is already the null workflow's capture surface.

- **Recorded:** design s7 L561-567 (fetcher stays out, rationale + recorded fallback); s17 #3 L1249-1252
- **History:** Alpha built the ordered OA retry loop (#1140-#1151) because 'full text is now a hard digest precondition, a single dead OA URL cannot be allowed to block an otherwise-acquirable Work' (history L1976); the Unpaywall-first tier ordering dates to alpha.4 #537 ('OA copy may have a better text layer than a scanned attachment', L1009). Beta.1 removes the hard precondition itself — partial states are legal resting states and Ask runs at $0 over whatever is indexed — so the failure mode the loop existed to prevent cannot occur, and the acquisition path moves to the researcher's existing Zotero capture surface.

### S9.4 — Extraction fixed to pdfium alone with no OCR, fail-closed coherence gate, dead-letter stub, deterministic distrust flags

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The single-extractor choice is an explicit decision-with-rationale in the design body (s7 L633-646): pdfium is BSD/native matching the single-static-binary install, PyMuPDF's AGPL+Python is named and rejected, and the dual-engine fallback is rejected because it 'doubled the test surface for no charter benefit'; scanned PDFs fail named (extract_failed:needs_ocr), never silently. 'No OCR' codifies a standing absence, not a regression — the gap report's own verification (review finding 14) corrected this, and the history shows OCR only ever appeared as an aspirational alpha.1 chain tier whose dependency 'literally currently fails to install' (ADR-30 Context). The alpha motive behind multi-path robustness — 'nothing captured is ever lost' — survives via the dead-letter triage stub, the fail-closed coherence gate, and deterministic distrust flags, themselves a recorded docs-history Borrow entry.

- **Recorded:** design s7 L633-646 (pdfium-alone decision with named rejections and named failure states); docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L41 ('Ingest dead-letter + extraction coherence gate' Borrow row)
- **History:** Alpha.1's full-text chain ended 'pymupdf4llm -> OCR' as robustness-by-redundancy under ADR-30's 'nothing captured is ever lost' (history L518-521), but the OCR dependency never worked ('ocr-and-documents literally currently fails to install', L521) and the ported alpha.14/15 extractors (PR #1117, L1942) never claim OCR — so there is no shipped capability to regress. The redundancy axis that mattered in practice was multiple OA text sources (L1009), which is the separately recorded S9.3/s17 #3 exclusion; the no-loss motive is met in beta.1 by the visible triage stub and fail-closed named failure states instead of extractor plurality.

### S9.5 — Explicit work-lifecycle state machine added (new->cataloged->...->indexed; distrust_flags; unsearchable as derived predicate)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is additive machinery fully specified with rationale in the governing design itself: s7 (L514-522) defines the machine, names indexed as the $0 payoff state, makes partial states legal resting states, and makes unsearchable a derived predicate honoring 'flags never block'. It stays inside alpha's earned constraints rather than re-opening them: machine stage state is DB-side only with a periodic artifact-reconciliation pass (s5 L418-427), which honors the standing reject of status/maturity ladders and machine-written frontmatter ('three documented generations of decay'). Alpha's implicit state was never an earned position — no documented failure argues for implicitness, and the alpha audit record repeatedly found implicit/undeclared state harmful (enforcement theater, silent non-execution).

- **Recorded:** design s7 L514-522 (the state machine, with rationale); s5 L418-427 (stage state stays DB-side, standing-reject honored); docs-history Reject rows 'Status/maturity ladders' and 'Machine-written frontmatter' (L109-110) as the bounding records
- **History:** No alpha position to defend — A15 work state was implicit in the pipeline ported by PR #1117 and 'unsearchable' was never a stated machine. The adjacent earned alpha position (lifecycle/maturity ladders in frontmatter are a write-time oracle and were killed across three doc generations — docs-history Reject L109) is addressed: beta.1's states are DB-side pipeline state rendered through read-only surfaces, never frontmatter meaning claims.

### S9.6 — Three-valued enrichable fields, mandatory provenance/as-of rendering, and content-addressed payloads store added

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The payloads half is the recorded fix for regression R3: the regression review's Resolution of 2026-07-04 and design s18 #3 record the content-addressed payloads store (sha256-named verbatim provider JSON, operational-ledger class) as restoring the auditability alpha.13/15 had and beta.1 had silently dropped; s5 (L386-387, L429-444) and s7 (L593-599) carry the mechanism with every enriched field/edge holding the hash. The trichotomy and as-of rendering are additive honesty machinery specified with rationale in the design body (s7 L603-606: counts 'never bare'), with no alpha counter-precedent — alpha's field_provenance/enrichment_runs is strictly weaker and beta.1 supersets it.

- **Recorded:** design s18 #3 L1290-1292 (R3 resolution); s5 L386-387 + L429-444 (payloads table + ledger class); s7 L593-606 (verbatim payload rule, three-valued fields, as-of rendering); regression review 'Resolution (2026-07-04)' L92-98
- **History:** Alpha.13 stored every provider response as a content-addressed blob with provider_payloads rows and api_call journal events (history L1854), and alpha.15's ADR-129 merge relied on 'deterministic blob replay' (L2138, L2314) — the position was earned by the need to audit and replay merges after providers mutate records. Beta.1 initially dropped this (R3, 'the drop is nowhere recorded'), the regression review caught it, and the 2026-07-04 resolution restored it — the motivating reason is now directly addressed, not bypassed.

### S9.7 — Entity resolution flips from never-auto-merge (flag only) to shared-ORCID/ISSN-L auto-merge with lazy point-of-use adjudication

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This exact delta is adjudicated in design s17 #5: 'the veto ladder, ORCID auto-merge, unresolved-by-default, and lazy point-of-use adjudication adopted as policy' — recorded precisely so it is not re-litigated — with the full mechanism and the week-3 abandonment arithmetic (a standing clerical queue at ~45 mentions/week plus a day-one backfill of thousands) in the body at s7 L615-631. Alpha's reasons for never-merge are addressed, not ignored: beta.1 merges only on an exact shared identifier with a name-incompatibility veto and a hard cannot-link on identifier conflict (no fuzzy thresholds), records provenance on every merge, and exports researcher same-as/not-same-as decisions to the vault so they are never overwritten and remain adjudicable at point of use. The docs-history Borrow row itself endorses the carve-out beta.1 uses ('auto-merge only on exact identifier match').

- **Recorded:** design s17 #5 L1258-1260; s7 L615-631 (veto ladder, unresolved-by-default, lazy adjudication); s5 L440-442 (decide events exported, decisions never DB-only); docs-history Borrow 'Silent auto-apply policy' L33
- **History:** Alpha's never-merge was precautionary, not incident-earned: ADR-94 record-linkage 'never merges records' because 'automatic merges are irreversible and unvalidated' and 'fuzzy thresholds stay out until real corpus misses justify them' (history L2166); ADR-129 bound work-ID merges to attention-never-auto-merge (L2140); the alpha.2-era 0.85 entity-resolution confidence floor routed uncertain merges to flag cards (L527). Beta.1 addresses both stated concerns — it uses no fuzzy or confidence-scored matching at all (exact ORCID/ISSN-L identifier match plus a name-compatibility veto), and recorded merge provenance plus vault-exported decide events make merges auditable and reversible at the point of use — while the never-merge rule survives intact for the ambiguous cases (everything else rests unresolved and counted honestly in denominators).

### S9.8 — DOI metadata channel: Crossref-API-primary field merge → citation.doi.org registry-agnostic content negotiation

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17 #3 records pinned citation.doi.org as a requirement-driven named allowlist entry resolved out of the information-flow pass, and the design body carries the rationale itself: registry-agnostic CSL-JSON across Crossref AND DataCite lets arXiv IDs resolve through their DataCite DOIs on the same channel with zero extra hosts (§7 L529-532), and §10 explains the security shape (pinned metadata endpoint, redirect-following disabled, general doi.org kept out because redirect-follow lands on arbitrary hosts). The substance of alpha's position — no single provider is complete, so merge per-field with provenance — survives in beta.1's enrichment: OpenAlex fills empty fields only under the JabRef rule, conflicts render as per-field diffs through Review, and raw provider payloads are preserved content-addressed (§7, §18 #3). The registry channel additionally serves DataCite-registered DOIs that a Crossref-primary client structurally cannot.

- **Recorded:** design §17 #3 (L1249-1252); design §7 L529-532 (channel + arXiv-via-DataCite rationale); design §10 L887-895 (pinned endpoint, redirects disabled, doi.org exclusion rationale)
- **History:** Alpha's Crossref-primary merge was earned by the ADR-30 empirical spike on the researcher's 867-entry library (reference counts 151/129/146 for one paper across S2/OpenAlex/Crossref; ORCID present in OpenAlex, ~0 in S2), hardened by ADR-129's static field-authority table ('no single provider is complete; provider output is claims, not ground truth'). Beta.1 addresses that reason with a different mechanism: registry record as canonical plus OpenAlex fill-blanks-only with per-field conflict diffs and replayable sha256 payloads, so the incompleteness and claims-not-truth lessons both hold.

### S9.9 — Peripheral provider set narrowed/deferred (arXiv via DataCite; PubMed/NCBI, SWH, ISBN deferred; ORCID/ROR resolvers removed)

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: medium

The narrowing is governed by two recorded broader decisions: §17 #3 resolves the information-flow allowlist question ('Allowlist expanded, tiered' — OpenAlex/GitHub/citation.doi.org admitted, OA-PDF fetcher out via the Zotero handoff, SWH/NCBI deferred), and §10's compiled-in requirement-driven allowlist explicitly names arxiv.org/europepmc.org, Software Heritage, and NCBI as deferred entries under the entry-plus-audit rule — anything unnamed is out by construction. ORCID/ROR resolver removal is covered because beta.1 needs no resolver egress: entity identity still keys on ORCID/ISSN-L from CSL-JSON payloads (§7 entities; §17 #5), preserving the identity-via-external-IDs lesson. The ISBN/book pipeline was never in the charter's required Capture scope (PDF, DOI/arXiv, BibTeX, Zotero, GitHub-repo), so its absence implements the spec rather than diverging from it.

- **Recorded:** design §17 #3 (L1249-1252); design §10 L887-903 (compiled allowlist + deferred named entries: arxiv.org/europepmc.org, Software Heritage, NCBI); design §7 L531-532 (arXiv via DataCite DOI, zero extra hosts) and L562-567 (Zotero capture handoff + named OA fallback); charter Required Product Scope, Capture row (requirements L29)
- **History:** Alpha accreted providers for coverage: the alpha.2 ADR-30 tiered chain, alpha.4 #537 Unpaywall/PMC ('OA copy may have a better text layer than a scanned attachment'), and alpha.14's identity-via-external-IDs (DOI/OpenAlex/ORCID/ROR/ISSN) fixing 'fragile local string matching' and preserving prior human merges on re-enrich. Beta.1 honors each earned reason by other means: OA text via the Zotero handoff with arXiv/Europe PMC as the recorded fallback, ORCID-keyed entity resolution from payload IDs without resolver calls, and SWH/NCBI kept revivable as deferred named entries rather than silently dropped.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Citations adjudicate arXiv-via-DataCite (§7 L531-532), the OA-host fallback deferral (§7 L562-567), and SWH/NCBI deferral (§17 #3; §10 L902-903 deferred named entries) — but NOT the ORCID/ROR resolver removal or the ISBN/book-pipeline deferral. ROR and ISBN appear nowhere in the design; ORCID appears only as entity auto-merge, not a resolver host. The charter Capture row (L29) merely omits them — omission from a required-scope row is neither a decision with rationale nor a Deliberate Exclusion; the 'info-flow-research avoid verdict' is uncited deeper-lens evidence, not a recorded adjudication.
- **Verifier notes:** Citations adjudicate arXiv-via-DataCite (§7 L531-532), the OA-host fallback deferral (§7 L562-567), and SWH/NCBI deferral (§17 #3; §10 L902-903 deferred named entries) — but NOT the ORCID/ROR resolver removal or the ISBN/book-pipeline deferral. ROR and ISBN appear nowhere in the design; ORCID appears only as entity auto-merge, not a resolver host. The charter Capture row (L29) merely omits them — omission from a required-scope row is neither a decision with rationale nor a Deliberate Exclusion; the 'info-flow-research avoid verdict' is uncited deeper-lens evidence, not a recorded adjudication.

### S9.10 — New GitHub-repo-as-work ingest subsystem (CITATION.cff chain, pinned SHA, typed paper↔repo edge)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is charter-required scope, not an ungoverned divergence: the Required Product Scope Capture row names GitHub-repo import as a beta.1 bar, and the design specifies the subsystem (§7: CITATION.cff → codemeta → Zenodo-DOI → GitHub-API chain with per-field level recording, pinned HEAD SHA, README as fulltext, paper and repo as two works joined by a typed edge, never merged). The api.github.com admission is recorded in §17 #3 under the requirement-driven allowlist rule. Code files staying inert honors the charter's 'Deep code intelligence' Deliberate Exclusion, so the addition does not smuggle in excluded scope.

- **Recorded:** charter Required Product Scope, Capture row (requirements L29) and Deliberate Exclusions, 'Deep code intelligence' (L86); design §7 L547-552; design §17 #3 (L1249-1252)
- **History:** None found as an earned alpha position — alpha never had a repo-as-work subsystem (alpha.1's catalog carried a 'repository' entity type that the alpha.15 four-type cut retired, and the docs-history 'Code provenance kit' borrow recommended linking a paper to its open-source repo as a typed link). Beta.1's typed paper↔repo edge realizes that recommendation; there is no alpha failure being re-opened.

### S9.11 — Calibrated background re-enrichment cadence + volatile-field TTL rejected in favor of attention-only refresh

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The design body states the rule ('No background metadata auto-refresh, ever; refresh follows attention', §7 L606-607) but nothing adjudicates the delta against alpha's calibrated cadence + TTL: it is absent from §11-§18, the regression-review resolution, the docs-history tables, and the charter exclusions — the verify pass grepped and confirmed the silence. The delta is sound on the merits: no charter row requires fresh volatile metadata; the honesty burden is carried by three-valued fields and as-of provenance stamps ('41 citations — OpenAlex, 2026-07-02', never bare); and the one safety-volatile field, retraction status, gets its own weekly corpus-scoped Crossref audit (§4), so no safety invariant depends on background refresh. It should still be named, because the docs-history borrow explicitly recommended a per-type re-check cadence (preprint→published) that this rule declines.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (the rule is stated at design §7 L606-607 but the divergence from alpha's cadence/TTL is not adjudicated in any authoritative record)
- **History:** No documented failure earned the alpha cadence: it appears as alpha.14's scheduled 'retraction/provider refresh' CLI wrappers and ADR-129's provider-drift policies ('providers drift, extractors upgrade'), motivated by drift-hygiene rather than an incident. Beta.1 addresses the drift concern differently — as-of staleness honesty plus attention-triggered refresh plus the weekly retraction audit for the field where drift is dangerous — so the alpha reason is honored in substance.
- **Action:** Add an §18-style recorded decision (or a §11 divergence bullet): "Background re-enrichment cadence + volatile-field TTL (alpha.15) — declined. Refresh follows attention (work-page open); every enriched count renders with provider and as-of date so staleness is visible rather than hidden, and the one safety-volatile field — retraction status — has its own weekly corpus-scoped Crossref audit (§4). Revisit if stale metadata misleads a real decision during the beta."
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Fix the recording text's alpha-side attribution and add the row-31 adjudication; location (§18-style recorded decision or §11 divergence bullet) is fine. Replace with: "Background re-enrichment cadence + volatile-field TTL — resolved by declining. The alpha line never decided a cadence: it was a standing open question (alpha.13 exec-plan D3 / design §11 → alpha.14 design §15 'still open, non-blocking' → carried forward at alpha.15), with alpha.13's cache-TTL note for volatile fields (cited_by_count, retraction status), alpha.14's scheduled retraction/provider-refresh CLI wrappers, and ADR-129's plan to calibrate a future cadence from journaled per-field drift. Beta.1 closes the question the other way: no background metadata auto-refresh, ever — refresh follows attention (work-page open); every enriched count renders with provider and as-of date so staleness is visible rather than hidden; and the one safety-volatile field, retraction status, has its own weekly corpus-scoped Crossref audit (§4). The docs-history borrow's preprint→published per-type re-check cadence (B/A/R row 31) is likewise declined for beta.1 under the same rule. Revisit if stale metadata misleads a real decision during the beta." Two load-bearing changes from the adjudicator's draft: (1) "resolved by declining [the open question]" not "(alpha.15) — declined", because alpha.15 carried the cadence as an unresolved open question (omnibus commit 09bf018f: alpha.15-design L2434; ADR-129 "calibrated from measured volatility" is a data plan, not a shipped cadence) — recording it as a decided-then-declined alpha.15 mechanism would falsify the precedent; (2) explicitly adjudicate docs-history B/A/R row 31's "Add preprint→published re-check as a per-type cadence" (an authoritative borrow recommendation that §7 L606-607's rule contradicts), otherwise the recorded-recommendation-vs-design-rule tension survives the recording.

### S9.12 — Retraction handling moves off the enrich-source promotion gate to a weekly corpus audit + export hard block

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The relocation is adjudicated across multiple authoritative records: design §4 specifies the weekly citation audit checking Crossref retraction/expression-of-concern status with human-only proposed dispositions plus the FAMA-style resurface probe, and explicitly cites the docs-history failure record ('last time the flag shipped without a retrieval consumer and was a live correctness bug for months'); §18 #2 records the export gate widened to refuse (not warn) on a cited superseded/retracted work, closing regression R2; the charter's Citation-audit row pre-registers the probe; and Crossref's narrowed role (retraction + title fallback) is its recorded §10 allowlist entry. The absence of a promotion gate is not a lost invariant but beta.1's recorded architecture — partial states are legal resting states and flags never block (§7) — with the retraction consequence moved to where alpha's documented failure actually was: consumption (Ask default-exclude counted in the denominator, superseded labels on override, export block).

- **Recorded:** design §4 L339-353 (weekly audit, human-only dispositions, FAMA probe, docs-history citation); design §18 #2 (L1287-1289, export refuses); design §10 L888-889 (Crossref = retraction + title fallback); docs-history Borrow 'Supersession + retraction consumption' (borrow/adapt/reject L31); charter Citation-audit row (requirements L52)
- **History:** Alpha.13's ADR-123 put retraction on the promotion gate because 'checked retrieval and references.bib would expose sources before required provider and retraction evidence had been reconciled' — an intake-side answer. But the documented alpha-line failure ran the other way: the superseded flag shipped with no retrieval consumer and drafts cited retired claims for months (docs-history headline + alpha.9 audit). Beta.1 addresses that actual failure with named consumers (Ask exclusion, export block, weekly audit, FAMA probe), trading at most a one-week detection window at intake for enforced consumption — the failure mode history documents is closed, not re-opened.

### S9.13 — Mandatory standalone work interview dropped; subjective layer via digest hook + Zotero annotation sync (reversing alpha.11's annotations-not-an-import-path)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both halves are recorded. The mandatory interview's drop is an explicit docs-history reject ('Mandatory ingest interview': violates no-mandatory-agent/PI-direct access, inflates exactly the per-source burden the retention experiment measures, duplicates annotations→notes), with the adapted survivor — the optional takeaway/interview-hook channel — recorded in the Adapt table and realized as beta.1's 2-3-question digest hook; the charter's Capture bar ('one initiating action and no mandatory per-item decisions') independently forbids the mandatory form. The annotation import path is the recorded §17 #1 information-flow resolution ('Reading is Zotero-first' — append-only sync, exact-quote anchor bridge, processing card), which plainly covers the reversal of the alpha.11 exclusion; and the promotion-laundering risk it introduces is guarded in §7 (promoted stubs keep m-class taint until the researcher edits; zero-human-typed-character promotions flagged in Review).

- **Recorded:** docs-history Reject 'Mandatory ingest interview' (borrow/adapt/reject L124) + Adapt 'Researcher takeaways as digest inputs' (L92); design §17 #1 (L1241-1244); design §7 L697-720 (annotation sync + taint guards); charter Capture row (requirements L29)
- **History:** Alpha.11 made the interview 'the hinge... not an optional side chat' and 'core — the Co-PI differentiator, not deferrable' on the conversation-turns-capture-into-knowledge premise, and alpha.14's digest failed without it — a founding belief, not a documented failure; the docs-history reject re-derives why the mandatory form is wrong for a retention experiment. Alpha.11 §13's annotation exclusion was scoped to that era's Memoria-owned PDF capture ('stores canonical quote/span/hash selectors itself'); beta.1's Zotero-first reading model changes the premise while honoring the underlying anchor-integrity lesson (ADR-129's 'Hypothes.is lesson': re-anchor, never silently rebind) via the exact-quote bridge with per-work orphan accounting.

### S9.14 — Semantic Scholar / scite.ai provider class dropped to deferred-with-revive-trigger, reversing the ADR-129 promotion

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The design body never mentions Semantic Scholar, scite, SPECTER, or TLDRs (grep: zero hits), the deferral is not among §17's seven folded resolutions, §10's deferred-named-entries line omits it, and no docs-history or charter record adjudicates it — the deferred-with-revive-trigger status lives only in the information-flow lens doc, which is not an authoritative record. The delta is sound on the merits: no charter row requires the S2 signal class, the recommendation-feed half brushes the charter's amended discovery exclusion ('recommender feeds remain out'), beta.1's NLI-only contradiction rework leaves no consumer for citation-intent candidates, and the compiled requirement-driven allowlist admits only entries with a requirement behind them. But reversing an explicit alpha.15 ADR promotion silently is exactly what the name-every-divergence discipline exists to prevent, and the revive trigger is worth a durable home so the deferral does not get re-litigated from scratch.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (only 0.1.0-beta.1-information-flow-design.md, a lens doc outside the authoritative record set; design body, §11-§18, docs-history, and charter are all silent)
- **History:** ADR-129 promoted Semantic Scholar to conditional default-on-when-keyed (reference union, free Tier-0 citation-intent contradiction candidates, TLDRs, SPECTER) with scite.ai opt-in, under 'like every provider and judge: proposers, never authorities' — a capability expansion from its alpha.13/14 deferred status, not a position earned by a documented failure. Beta.1 re-opens nothing: the contradiction pipeline is deliberately local-NLI-only (the docs-history Adapt row keeps the full engine dead), enrichment incompleteness is handled by OpenAlex fill-blanks, and the S2 value proposition (TLDRs/recommendations for triage) is precisely what the named revive trigger tests.
- **Action:** Append to design §10's deferred-named-entries line and add a §11 divergence bullet: "Semantic Scholar and scite.ai (alpha.15 ADR-129: conditional reference-union / citation-intent / TLDR / SPECTER providers) are deferred, not shipped — beta.1 enrichment is OpenAlex plus Crossref (retraction + title fallback). Revive as a named allowlist entry with its own audit — the first post-beta enrichment expansion — if discovery recall or reading triage measurably suffers without TLDRs/recommendations."
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Split the two providers in the recording; do not lump scite.ai into the deferral. §10 deferred-named-entries line: add only api.semanticscholar.org (not scite.ai). §11 divergence note, corrected text: "Semantic Scholar (alpha.15 ADR-129: conditional default-on-when-keyed — reference union, citation-intent contradiction candidates, TLDRs, SPECTER) is deferred, not shipped — beta.1 enrichment is OpenAlex plus Crossref (retraction + title fallback). Revive as a named allowlist entry with its own audit — the first post-beta enrichment expansion — if discovery recall or reading triage measurably suffers without TLDRs/recommendations. scite.ai (ADR-129: optional opt-in) is rejected, not deferred — link-out only, no revive trigger, on cost evidence (~12x budget; info-flow-design permanent-avoids list)." Basis: 0.1.0-beta.1-information-flow-design.md L110 ("Semantic Scholar is deferred — the first named post-beta expansion, revive-trigger: ... scite: link-out only, forever"), L276 ("Permanent avoids (no trigger, by evidence): ... scite API"), L288 ("scite ~= 12x budget -> link-out").
## 10. Surfaces / navigation / control

8 gaps — leave 5 · record 3 · change 0

### S10.1 — Obsidian 5-surface UI + ViewSpecRenderer + push-fed inspector replace A15's CLI/JSON-only surface model

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The delta is adjudicated in three authoritative places, all verified by opening them: design §11(10) records the host decision as deliberate new scope the alpha.15 plugin design 'anticipates but does not yet center'; §15 is a full recorded disposition of the control surface ('Recorded so it is not re-proposed' — block-not-pane generativity, ViewSpecRenderer over view-spec.v1, model-generated markup rejected on the missing-Obsidian-sandbox trifecta); §16 names the ADR obligation (amends ADR-125/130, requires its own ADR before implementation begins). The re-homed pieces are themselves recorded decisions: loudness ladder/ambient health (docs-history borrow row 37), empty-state honesty (row 38), the read-only inspector (row 46, lineage ADR-84), first-party-plugin-only (reject row 126), and §18(5) lands the R5 backup-status line on the inspector. Since the view-spec contract is alpha.15's own ADR-130 (review finding 4), only the renderer and host are new — exactly what these records adjudicate.

- **Recorded:** design.md §11(10) L987-991; §15 L1066-1133; §16 L1152-1158 (ADR obligation); §18(5) L1297-1302; docs-history borrow rows 37/38/46 + reject row 126
- **History:** ADR-130 (alpha.15 consolidation, PR #1158/#1159) already made the read-API the sole read path with a data-only 'render known kinds only' view-spec carrying ADR-102/116's one-definition rule; alpha.15 retired the dataviewjs dashboards to `status --json` + `knowledge/_views/` ('no board daemon survives', history L2012), and alpha.3's UI research (reject row 126) found community-plugin UI assembly defeated the write gate. Beta.1 addresses each reason: composition stays engine-side and single-definition, the UI is a first-party plugin only, the inspector is push-fed and strictly read-only, and owner ruling R-18 endorses CLI-first as a deliberately temporary phase.

### S10.2 — Hub concept dropped entirely (A15 kept hub as a first-class type; neither line ships hub navigation)

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The navigation half is continuity (no alpha version shipped more than the folded hubs.base view), but the concept drop is real and ungoverned: the §3 type enum carries no hub, the only design text is §7 L623-624's parenthetical 'hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers' (a rationale-free aside inside entity-resolution policy), and the regression review's claim that hub/tag graph is a recorded §11-§17 divergence does not verify — no hub row exists in §11-§18 or the charter. On the charter's merits the drop is defensible: no charter row requires hubs, mechanical membership survives as DB tag queries/Bases, and curated MOC-style notes remain writable as freehand human files. However the owner's 2026-07-05 reference rulings R-2/R-5/R-10 hold hub is the wiki-LLM/Zettelkasten bridge and the basic flow's terminus (digest→hub), governing the S3.2 re-examination — so this section's obligation is a named, verifiable record pointing at that adjudication instead of the current false 'recorded' claim.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (only §7 L623-624's parenthetical deferral, no rationale; the regression-review 'recorded in §11-§17' sweep claim does not check out)
- **History:** Hub survived every alpha reset — alpha.1's MOC, alpha.10's index-type removal, alpha.11's four-type collapse, and alpha.15's ADR-126 cut, which kept it as one of four types and redesigned it to own exactly one controlled-vocabulary tag because 'hand-curated hub membership rots', splitting mechanical membership from human salience (answering ADR-19's 'generated list that looks curated but isn't' hazard). Those records govern how to build hubs safely, not a documented failure from lacking them, and beta.1 honors the mechanical half via DB/tag queries — but four resets of survival is strong precedent the current silence never engages, and beta.1 offers no salience/organizing replacement beyond freehand notes.
- **Action:** Add a named divergence to design §11: 'beta.1 carries no hub type and no hubs/ tree; hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers (§7) — mechanical membership is DB tag queries/Bases, curated salience is a freehand researcher note.' Cross-reference owner rulings R-2/R-5 (digest→hub as the basic flow's terminus) so the S3.2 re-examination owns whether the hub concept returns.
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Keep the disposition (record) and the §11 location, but fix the divergence text: the clause "mechanical membership is DB tag queries/Bases" asserts a mechanism beta.1 does not carry. The §3 frontmatter contract declares no `tags` key, the §5 schema has no tags table or column, and the controlled-vocabulary substrate is dropped — the gap report's own verified correction (S3.7 entry, gap-report line 44, review §3 PLAUSIBLE) states "no primary B1 source defines a `tags` field ... a surviving degraded/freeform-tags field must not be asserted." Writing "DB tag queries" into §11 would repeat the exact failure class this gap fixes (an unverifiable recorded claim, like the regression review's "hub/tag graph" sweep line). Replace with what the design actually carries: mechanical grouping survives as DB `edges`/`links` queries and generated queue/index projections rendered via Bases over the declared meaning-only frontmatter keys (§5: "Bases-visible machine state renders through generated queue/index notes and the read-API, never per-work YAML"); curated salience as a freehand researcher note is accurate and stays. Two secondary fixes: (1) the divergence row should also dispose of docs-history Borrow row 42 — the beta1-targeted sample corpus includes "a worked-example starter hub set marked example-not-default," which under a no-hub-type design can only ship as freehand example notes; name that, or the recorded borrow dangles against the recorded drop. (2) Cite R-2/R-5/R-10, not just R-2/R-5 — R-10 is the ruling that pins "digest→hub connection" as the missing link (R-5 supplies the flow terminus "connected to a hub").

### S10.3 — Canvas/JSON-Canvas absent in both lines (ADR-103 proposed then rejected, never shipped) — continuity, not a delta

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This entry exists only to forestall mis-listing Canvas as a B1 removal: ADR-103 stayed proposed from alpha.8, gated on a stable-layout spike that never cleared, and was explicitly rejected at alpha.15 ('spatial-at-scale refuted; tabular/faceted is the validated default') — there was never a shipped surface to remove. The continued absence is governed by verified records: docs-history reject row 129 keeps the projected-argument-canvas engine dead (unbuilt substrates — reconcile semantics, stable incremental layout — and no measured demand), line 157 lists it among standing rejects, and adapt row 100 records the only admissible future form (derived views never the system of record, layout pins existing node positions, gated on a feasibility spike). Owner ruling R-11 (graphs render as JSON Canvas) is a prior on R-7's argument-graph restoration in sections S3/S6/S8; if upheld there it re-opens under row 100's recorded conditions, not silently here.

- **Recorded:** docs-history reject row 129 + standing-reject line 157 + adapt row 100 (keep-test-safe snapshot/spike conditions); alpha.15 ADR-103 rejection (design-history L2212)
- **History:** ADR-103 (alpha.8) proposed Canvas strictly as a projection of authored `links:`, never an authoritative edge store, gated on an unproven stable-layout spike; alpha.15 rejected it among the four consolidation-pass rejections (95/97/103/106). Beta.1 leaves the rejection standing and re-opens no failure; researcher-authored sketch canvases remain fine per row 129.

### S10.4 — Spaces tree + _nav Navigator + three-places model + Maintenance cadence dropped for interaction-mode surfaces

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

No authoritative record names this drop: the beta.1 design contains zero mention of spaces/, _nav, three-places, or a Maintenance cadence (grep-verified), §11 carries no row, and ADR-101 is left accepted with nothing to name; the regression review's 'kanban/spaces recorded in §11-§17' sweep claim holds for kanban (docs-history reject row 129's task-PM layer) but not for the spaces navigation layer. The drop is sound on the merits: the recorded surface model (§1 surface discipline, §15/§16 rulings) replaces place/queue pages with interaction modes plus Obsidian-native navigation, and every earned constituent of the alpha layer is honored by a recorded beta.1 mechanism — ambient health and the loudness ladder (§1, borrow row 37), queue-converges-to-empty via review back-pressure plus the weekly digest/sweep cadence (§1, borrow row 63), the one-definition rule via the single ViewSpecRenderer (§15). Only the naming of the divergence itself is missing.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-70 (alpha.3) rejected a Maintenance destination because unconditional surfacing causes alert fatigue — health must stay ambient; ADR-101 (alpha.8) was a lexical fix (gate ambiguity ~480:190); ADR-114 (alpha.10) added the _nav rail for ambient awareness and persistent orientation; ADR-116 split Queue/Maintenance by cadence to fix 'one queue mixing two cadences' and the five-drifted-Dataview/Bases-twins one-definition defect. Beta.1 addresses each earned reason with a different mechanism (status bar + ribbon pending badge, inspector, review throttling, single renderer, weekly digest) — none of these ADRs records a failure that interaction-mode navigation re-opens.
- **Action:** Add one divergence line to design §11: 'The alpha navigation layer — ADR-101 spaces/, ADR-114 _nav Navigator, the three-places framing, ADR-116 Queue/Maintenance cadence — does not return; interaction-mode surfaces plus Obsidian-native navigation replace place/queue pages (§1/§16). Its earned constituents are re-homed: ambient health and the loudness ladder in §1, review back-pressure and weekly cadence in §1, the one-definition rule in §15's single ViewSpecRenderer.'

### S10.5 — Retrieval substrate swap: qmd dropped for FTS5+sqlite-vec+bge-small, overturning the alpha.15 spike verdict; §11 misrecords it as convergence

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The swap is sound on the merits because beta.1 removes the exact blocker the spike recorded: alpha.15 kept qmd because 'the packaged product does not yet carry sqlite-vec plus a local embedding pipeline, so the semantic/hybrid replacement bar did not clear' — and beta.1 bundles precisely that pipeline (bge-small int8 ONNX + in-DB sqlite-vec, §8 L753-756), while dropping the external qmd/Node≥22 runtime serves the charter's 30-minute clean-machine install and the standalone arc. But no accurate record adjudicates it: qmd appears nowhere in the beta.1 design, and §11 L965-967's 'Converges … the alpha.15 §10 spike is exactly the Ask substrate' is affirmatively false — the spike kept qmd and declined this substrate (verify finding L483: 'mischaracterized as convergence'). An affirmative misstatement in the governing doc is the same zero-tolerated-contradiction class the regression review escalated for R1, and it suppresses the one open question the swap leaves — the never-run quality comparison against qmd's cross-encoder-reranked hybrid — so this silence is riskier than an ordinary unnamed divergence.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent; worse, design §11 L965-967 misrecords the swap as convergence (gap-analysis verify-findings L476/483)
- **History:** FTS5+sqlite-vec was on record since alpha.11 §6 as the zero-dependency fallback under qmd-as-backend; alpha.15's baseline-gated spike under ADR-129's 'beat a declared cheap baseline or be disabled' rule (PR-A #1162, verdict committed to tests/fixtures/retrieval-substrate-spike.json) kept qmd because the semantic pipeline did not exist in the package (design-history L2152). Beta.1 addresses that recorded reason head-on by shipping the pipeline; the unvalidated remainder (qmd's rerank edge, itself questioned at alpha.9 on reasoning-relevance — history L1375, Wei 2026) falls to the beta's pre-registered Ask instrumentation and weekly citation audit rather than a new spike.
- **Action:** Rewrite §11's retrieval clause out of the Converges list into a named divergence: 'Diverges from alpha.15 on the retrieval substrate: the §10 spike kept qmd because the package did not yet carry sqlite-vec plus a local embedding pipeline; beta.1 bundles that pipeline (bge-small int8 ONNX + sqlite-vec, §8) and drops the external qmd/Node runtime for the standalone-install bar. The swap's quality is not assumed from the spike — the pre-registered Ask instrumentation (empty/failed-Ask relegation clusters, weekly citation audit) is the measurement.'

### S10.6 — Daemon→plugin write-event push over loopback HTTP+WebSocket replaces A15's inbound FS-polling refresh

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Recorded with rationale in the design body twice: §1 states the daemon pushes write events after every applied run because 'Obsidian's file watcher provably misses external writes, and a stale check badge is an honesty bug, not a cosmetic one', and §16 carries a dedicated bullet ('Write-event push, not watcher faith'). The mechanism rides the recorded host decision (§11(10)) that dissolves the alpha constraint, and it is an addition in service of the charter's Review/Provenance honesty bars, not a dropped invariant. Docs-history borrow row 45 (derived-surface freshness honesty) records the same freshness discipline as a beta.1 target.

- **Recorded:** design.md §1 L56-62; §16 L1192-1195; host decision §11(10) L987-989; docs-history borrow row 45
- **History:** Alpha.15's `serve --watch` was stdlib FS-polling because a required watcher-daemon was rejected to preserve the no-daemon architecture — 'real-time when the on-demand process runs, scan + consumption guard otherwise, guard never retired' (ADR-127 Alternatives; PR-P #1184, design-history L2186). Beta.1's recorded host decision deliberately reverses no-daemon, so the alpha reason for polling no longer exists, and the push channel addresses the new staleness-honesty exposure the live plugin surfaces create.

### S10.7 — Versioned lockstep plugin/daemon/CLI handshake with refuse-on-mismatch replaces A15's free-schema `--json` stance

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The design body adjudicates this with explicit rationale: §2 mandates the version handshake with refuse-on-mismatch because 'stale boundary code waves through what a newer runtime treats as mutating'; §15 explains the lockstep choice (the handshake 'nullifies SDUI's ship-without-the-client payoff, so its versioning tax would be pure cost'); and Appendix A records the obligation to adopt strict view-spec versioning plus capability negotiation before any second first-class client ships. Docs-history borrow row 35 records the handshake as an adjudicated borrow from the alpha.9 hermes-clean-slate design. The free-schema spirit survives in substance — schemas stay unversioned behind a refuse-on-mismatch gate until a second client forces real versioning — so no alpha reason is discarded unexamined.

- **Recorded:** design.md §2 L183-186; §15 L1078-1084; Appendix A L1346-1353; docs-history borrow row 35
- **History:** A15's schema-free stance was not earned by a documented failure — ADR-130's CLI/FastMCP/loopback-HTTP skins shipped as one package in lockstep, so no skew existed to defend against. The motivating failure for the handshake sits on the alpha.9 record (hermes-clean-slate, docs-history row 35): stale boundary code waving through what a newer runtime treats as mutating. Beta.1 has three separately-running components where that failure becomes live, and the handshake closes it while keeping the schema free behind the gate.

### S10.8 — Host-free ViewSpecRenderer enabling a recorded VS Code client #2, plus a deferred agent-submitted view-spec instance path

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both halves are explicitly recorded. Appendix A exists precisely to record the second client ('Not scheduled work — recorded to show the §16 shape pays its M×N dividend'), including the shared host-free ViewSpecRenderer+DaemonClient package and the DocumentLinkProvider as the one genuinely new piece. §15's third bullet records the agent view-spec instance path as post-beta.1, requiring its own adapter ADR plus a deceptive-layout fixture family (SusBench/Unit-42 probes) before shipping, inside a mandatory proposed-view container with provenance banner, engine-clamped loudness, and enqueue-only vocabulary; §15's flip conditions and Appendix A both record the strict-versioning obligation any second client triggers. §13 keeps every agent a quarantined client under the ADR-130 contract, so the channel opens nothing the alpha boundary forbids.

- **Recorded:** design.md Appendix A L1314-1353; §15 L1098-1108 + flip conditions L1126-1133; §13 L1014-1019
- **History:** ADR-130 (alpha.15) made the view-spec engine-emitted data with no renderer because no UI host existed after ADR-125's standalone cut; the underlying lesson (the exited Hermes failure) was never to let a host own state, workflow, or the write boundary — not a prohibition on additional read clients. Beta.1 honors that reason: the second client is 'client #2 of the same daemon' with zero engine changes, and agent-submitted view-spec instances travel the existing quarantined request envelope as one-shot data through the queue, never a synchronized layer.
## 11. Agent / autonomy

9 gaps — leave 6 · record 3 · change 0

### S11.1 — Agent-as-quarantined-client boundary inherited from ADR-130 (convergence, not divergence)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The boundary is identical in substance on both sides and beta.1 records it explicitly: design s13 states 'Memoria is not an agent, and beta.1 adds none', defines any agent as a client under the ADR-130 contract (read-API + request envelope, quarantined, read-scoped, never file/terminal/exec/send, chat additive), and closes 'Recorded so it is not re-proposed.' The regression review independently classified agent/co-PI machinery among the 14 recorded divergences (none of R1-R6 touch the boundary), and the docs-history B/A/R rejects every resident-agent shape (agent-profile fleet, agent-executed code loops, mandatory ingest interview) while re-homing the Co-PI's takeaway-interview function onto a direct Obsidian affordance. The 'Co-PI' residue (ADR-130 filename, the retired record-copi-interview operation key) was verified by the gap-analysis review to name an operation/measurement, never a resident loop.

- **Recorded:** design.md s13 (L998-1019, 'Recorded so it is not re-proposed'); alpha-regression-review L78-81 ('agent/co-PI machinery' among 14 recorded divergences); docs-history B/A/R Reject rows L112/L113/L124 and Adapt L92
- **History:** The demotion arc was earned stepwise: seven Hermes profiles (ADR-02) -> five with a read-only co-PI front (ADR-48) -> alpha.11 binds policy to postures/operations not profiles -> ADR-125 deletes the profile system because 'the framework owned state, workflow, and the write boundary; every integrity mechanism had to be threaded through it' (the Hermes inversion), with the why-not-autonomous three-precondition analysis refusing resident loops. Beta.1 lands exactly this terminal posture and re-records the Hermes lesson verbatim in s13, so the earned position is preserved, not re-opened.

### S11.2 — Librarian persona, steering.md program memory, and eval rubrics deleted; discovery becomes deterministic occurrence-counting

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The functional replacements are sound and mostly recorded piecemeal: discovery ranking is deterministic occurrence counting in the design body (s7, L729), the Librarian's external-API gap-driven discovery is a recorded adapt ('alpha.16+ decision, never silent creep', B/A/R L99), topic-hint membership proposals are adapted at B/A/R L82, and a resident persona cannot survive s13's no-agent posture or the B/A/R reject of vault-resident prompts (L116). But no authoritative record names the deletion of the shipped Librarian persona, its system/eval rubrics, or steering.md itself, and the from-reports addendum (s8.3) confirms steering.md's program-memory function — the researcher's standing priorities — is unre-homed for beta.1 with no recorded decision. The delta is charter-clean (no charter row requires program memory; the amended discovery exclusion demands exactly the deterministic identifier-only shape beta.1 ships), so it needs a record, not a change.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (function-level partial records only: docs-history B/A/R Adapt L82 and L99; design s7 L729)
- **History:** steering.md descends from research-focus.md ('program memory — the PI's standing steering') and was elevated on the Karpathy program.md principle ('Direction is authored as the program, not the content'), with ADR-92 already choosing cheap deterministic steering-relevance scoring over ML; ADR-126 had already dissolved the steering type ('steering -> the instructions config'). The position was principle-earned, not failure-earned, and beta.1's deterministic occurrence-counting honors the ADR-92 determinism precedent; only the program-memory function is genuinely dropped, with no documented failure being re-opened.
- **Action:** Add to design s11's divergence list (or an s18-style recorded decision): 'The alpha.15 vault-template's Librarian persona, its system/eval rubrics, and steering.md are deleted, not ported: discovery ranking is deterministic occurrence counting (s7), external-API gap-driven discovery stays an alpha.16+ allowlist decision (docs-history adapt), and no resident persona survives s13. steering.md's program-memory function (standing researcher priorities) is deliberately dropped for beta.1; if discovery or seeding rankings prove misaligned with the researcher's priorities during the beta, revive it as a researcher-authored program note consumed deterministically, never as an agent prompt.'
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Amend the proposed recording's steering.md clause to carry the decided rationale: owner ruling R-14 (gap-analysis/owner-rulings-2026-07-05.md L158-161) endorses the steering.md/research-focus.md drop as "redundant with a project's research question," closing the entry in beta.1's favor. The record should therefore state that steering.md's program-memory function (standing researcher priorities) is re-homed onto the project's research question in project.md — not left homeless — and demote the revival clause to a secondary flip condition: if discovery or seeding rankings prove misaligned with the researcher's priorities during the beta, the owner-consistent first response is enriching the project's research question; only if that proves insufficient, revive a researcher-authored program note consumed deterministically, never as an agent prompt. The rest of the proposed text and the s11-divergence-list/s18-style location are verified correct (s7 L729 occurrence counting; B/A/R Adapt L82/L99 and Reject L116; s13 L1006 no-agent posture; charter exclusion L84; history: Karpathy program.md elevation at alpha.11, ADR-92 determinism, ADR-126 steering-type dissolution — principle-earned, no failure re-opened). Also update the adjudicator rationale's "no recorded decision" claim to "no authoritative design record; owner endorsement R-14 exists in gap-analysis reference notes."

### S11.3 — New explicit operation-test framework partitioning in-product vs agent LLM work

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is a new-in-beta framework whose authoritative record is the design body itself: s13 states the operation test (pinned prompt+model with fixture and seeded-error verdict; deterministically checkable output; arithmetic worst-case price; per-item unattended shape), applies it to the full beta.1 call-site roster, records the deliberate redundancy of product synthesis with frontier agents as 'the direct-access contract working, not waste', and grounds the boundary in the s9 cost ceiling, pre-registered-experiment integrity, and proposer-never-authority. That is an explicit decision-with-rationale in a governing section, so there is nothing silent to record and nothing to relitigate. It extends rather than contradicts the alpha position that operations are product code.

- **Recorded:** design.md s13 L1021-1048 ('The operation test', 'Applied to the beta.1 roster', 'Neither side, ever')
- **History:** Alpha held 'operations are product code' because vault-resident prompts proved untestable and unpinnable (B/A/R Reject L116; ADR-125 made pins/test-modes/calibration structural), and the Hermes exit taught that anything owning the write boundary must not change with each model generation. Beta.1's litmus test formalizes exactly that lesson and adds the printable-price criterion from the charter's cost-control bar — the earned position is sharpened, not re-opened.

### S11.4 — Four recorded flip conditions under which 'no resident agent' is revisable

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The conditionality is itself the record: design s13 enumerates the four flip conditions (synthesis losing to the ChatGPT counterfactual on integrative reasoning after section expansion; agent-host/MCP fragmentation; disposition telemetry showing conversation as de facto primary; scope leaving single-researcher/local-trusted territory), names the bounded response to each, and closes with the invariant that 'in every flip the loop gains standing as a client, never ownership of the write boundary.' The conditions are qualitative and observable through instrumentation beta.1 already ships (counterfactual archiving, disposition telemetry), unlike the retired numeric adoption triggers. Nothing here is silent or wrong.

- **Recorded:** design.md s13 L1050-1058 ('Flip conditions, recorded')
- **History:** Alpha recorded no revision conditions for the agent stance; its adjacent lesson (PR #406, B/A/R Reject L119) was that numeric adoption triggers written against imaginary usage 'can never meaningfully fire and rot unobserved', with assumes:-plus-cadence-review as the replacement. Beta.1's flip conditions are event-shaped and evidence-backed rather than numeric usage thresholds, so they honor that lesson, and the closing client-never-owner invariant preserves the Hermes-inversion lesson that motivated the no-agent posture.

### S11.5 — Post-beta agent-submitted view-spec instance path added

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The capability is recorded with its guardrails in design s15: an agent may submit a view-spec instance through the request envelope, validated like any write, landing unchecked, inside a mandatory proposed-view container with provenance banner, engine-clamped loudness, and an enqueue-only action vocabulary the producer cannot set — explicitly 'post-beta.1' and gated behind its own adapter ADR plus a deceptive-layout fixture family (SusBench/Unit-42 probe set) before shipping. The s15 flip conditions further bind it (restrict to engine-templated shapes or drop it if the fixtures fail against clamping). The alpha rejections it must not violate — agent-generated components, shared mutable agent-UI state, untrusted text as active content — are preserved by construction ('one-shot data through the queue, never a synchronized layer').

- **Recorded:** design.md s15 L1098-1108 ('Agent views land as data, not components') and s15 flip conditions L1126-1133
- **History:** ADR-130 fixed the component vocabulary and had clients render known kinds only because framework-hosted UX (CopilotKit-class) 'inverts the boundary via shared mutable agent-UI state' and untrusted text must never become active content — the same boundary-inversion failure as the Hermes exit, at the UI layer. Beta.1's instance-not-component path keeps every one of those rejections and adds pre-ship preconditions, so the earned position is extended under guard, not re-opened.

### S11.6 — Chat-transparency enumeration, poisoned-read/credential-reuse fixture families, and trusted-local-dogfood distinction not carried

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The containment shape that carries the safety load is verified intact — the regression review's adversarial sweep confirmed the read-API as sole read path, the request-envelope integrity fields, quarantine, taint, and the fail-closed egress family all held, and none of R1-R6 touch the agent boundary. Dropping the chat-transparency enumeration is charter-consistent: the Overreliance row attributes trust-incident defenses only to vigilance-independent mechanisms ('explanations do not prevent overreliance'), and beta.1 ships no first-party agent client for the enumeration to bind. But the drop is nowhere recorded, and one honesty nuance is weakened silently: ADR-130 stated that a local agent with its own file tools is in the trusted-local class regardless of transport (the credential-reuse fixture documented that a local bearer credential is readable by such an agent), whereas beta.1's s13 asserts agents are 'never granted' tools without restating that a BYO agent's own tools put it outside read-scoping — and beta.1's port-file token has the same readable-credential residual. That residual belongs in SECURITY.md's honest residual list, and the fixture families deserve a named re-entry point.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-130's per-agent read scoping was the lethal-trifecta/exfiltration mitigation, with the threat model stated honestly: 'read scoping is a policy boundary for tool-limited/cooperating agents; a local agent with its own file tools is in the trusted-local class regardless of transport', the first-rung all-vault CLI agent labeled 'trusted-local dogfood only, never a supported safe surface', and the cross-channel credential-reuse fixture documenting the residual. The transparency enumeration was carried from ADR-121's enqueue-only UI rule as chat ergonomics, not earned by a failure. Beta.1 keeps the containment mechanisms and the local-trusted framing (s13's scope flip condition) but does not restate the residual or carry the fixtures.
- **Action:** Add to design s13 (end of the agent-boundary paragraph) and s10's SECURITY.md spec: 'Not carried from ADR-130's body: the chat-transparency enumeration (plan/sources-read/assumptions/unknowns/pending-writes) — beta.1 ships no first-party agent client, and per the charter's overreliance row explanations are never counted as defenses; containment (read-API, envelope, quarantine, linter) is the defense of record. The trusted-local residual is restated: a local agent holding its own file/terminal tools is outside read-scoping regardless of transport and can read the daemon token, so it is named in SECURITY.md's residual list. The poisoned-read and cross-channel credential-reuse fixture families re-enter the CI corpus with the first shipped agent-transport ADR.'

### S11.7 — ADR-125's 'operations, never agents' naming rule not restated; engines/operations used interchangeably

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The substance of the rule is fully honored — s13 opens 'Memoria is not an agent, and beta.1 adds none' and reserves 'agent' exclusively for external clients — so no safety posture is lost. What is silently dropped is the naming discipline itself, which alpha earned twice: ADR-69 fixed the one-concept-two-names drift ('engine' vs 'app'), and the alpha.8 rename recorded the posture rationale verbatim ('zero-LLM deterministic work has no posture at all, so it is not an agent: it is an operation'). Beta.1 re-introduces mild two-name usage (engine/operation interchangeably) and gives the never-call-it-an-agent rule no durable home, which is exactly the zombie-reject pattern the docs-history report warns about. One recording sentence closes it.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-69 renamed engines to operations because the docs called one concept two names (the DDD ubiquitous-language anti-pattern) and 'engine' was not self-descriptive; the alpha.8 execution pass scrubbed 'agent' from the deterministic layer because posture, not capability, is what makes something an agent — the distinction that underwrote the whole no-autonomy line ADR-125 finalized. Beta.1 preserves the posture substance in s13 but not the naming rule; no documented failure is re-opened, only a recorded discipline left without a home.
- **Action:** Add one sentence to design s13 after the 'Memoria is not an agent' paragraph: 'Naming rule carried from ADR-69/125: Memoria's components are engines/operations — pinned, priced product code — and are never named or designed as agents; "agent" is reserved for external clients under this section's contract.'
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Keep the location (design s13, after the "Memoria is not an agent" paragraph) but replace the proposed sentence, which (a) calls all components "pinned, priced product code" — contradicting s13's own operation test, under which deterministic engines and supervisor components have no price — and (b) blesses "engines/operations" as an interchangeable pair, reproducing the one-concept-two-names anti-pattern ADR-69 exists to kill. Use instead: "Naming rule carried from ADR-69/125: the §2 worker components are *engines* (deterministic product code that writes to staging); the pinned, priced LLM calls this section admits are *operations*; one concept gets one name (the ADR-69 lesson), and neither is ever named or designed as an agent — 'agent' is reserved for external clients under this section's ADR-130 contract."

### S11.8 — memoria-policy-gate per-tool-call hook system dropped; superseded by single VaultWriter + request envelope

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This completes a demolition the alpha line itself decided (the plugin was 'dropped from the product, not deferred' under the standalone cut; A15's vault-template shipping it was a recorded lag), and the fail-closed function the hooks carried is preserved by construction, not lost: beta.1 has no external-adapter write path for a hook to guard — machine writes exist only through the daemon's VaultWriter and agent writes only through the envelope VaultWriter applies. The supersession is recorded: the docs-history B/A/R reject of per-lane write policies states 'Single-writer VaultWriter + credential-free workers + Guard deliver the guarantee structurally with zero per-role config; the old enforcement was advisory and failed open', design s11 converges on one-writer + staging, and s2 carries the load-bearing lesson explicitly ('Guard fails closed when its policy cannot load, and engine workers refuse to start unless Guard and the linter are registered — fail-closed only holds for a decision that is actually reached'). The regression sweep verified the single-writer spine and fail-closed egress intact.

- **Recorded:** docs-history B/A/R Reject L112 (agent-profile fleet / per-lane write policies) and Borrow L35 (Guard liveness + fail-closed contract, target beta1, folded per s14); design.md s11 L965-972 (one-writer convergence) and s2 L178-181 (fail-closed Guard liveness); from-reports-addendum s11.2 (re-home provenance)
- **History:** The hook system was earned by a live failure: ADR-27's shell hook 'never fired on live writes' (wrong tool-name match, consent-gated, fail-open), and ADR-28's in-process fail-closed plugin was the correction, with an adversarial test proving block-on-gate-failure. That failure mode — a gate that proceeds on its own failure — is addressed in beta.1 twice over: structurally (no per-call hook exists to fail; the only write paths are VaultWriter and the envelope) and explicitly (ADR-28's lesson restated as the s2 fail-closed liveness rule). Nothing the incident taught is re-opened.

### S11.9 — Scoped MCP demoted from primary surface to deferred/local-stdio; transport reshaped to plugin-daemon loopback HTTP + WebSocket push

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both halves of the delta are recorded in governing sections: s13 states 'Agent transports stay local/stdio for beta.1... remote/OAuth remains deferred', and s16's first bullet names the ADR obligation — the plugin+daemon host decision 'amends ADR-125 (standalone CLI + engine architecture) and ADR-130 (surfaces) and requires that ADR before implementation begins' — which is precisely the demotion of the A15 surface roster. The write-event push is likewise a recorded s16 decision (watcher misses are an honesty-contract violation). The invariant that mattered — the read-API as the sole read path with request-envelope integrity fields — is verified intact by the regression sweep, and A15 itself already held that MCP was 'one transport over engine/api', never the product surface, so no earned position is inverted.

- **Recorded:** design.md s13 L1017-1019 (transports local/stdio, remote/OAuth deferred); s16 L1152-1158 (ADR obligation amending ADR-130 surfaces) and L1192-1195 (write-event push)
- **History:** ADR-130 built the transports as 'pure marshalling skins' over one engine/api module and rejected MCP-as-product-surface ('MCP is one transport over engine/api; the CLI remains the no-daemon recovery surface'), with MCP behind an optional extra and a closed tool roster — the alpha position was that transports are fungible skins over the sole read path, earned against the wrapper-holding-logic gate failure. Beta.1 keeps that exact structure while swapping which skin is centered, and routes the surface change through the required amending ADR, so the reason alpha held its position is fully honored.
## 12. Security / OS confinement

3 gaps — leave 3 · record 0 · change 0

### S12.1 — OS-enforced egress (Linux CLONE_NEWNET netns) is Linux-only; seccomp/macOS sandbox-exec/Windows-Firewall flows cut

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The cut is explicitly recorded with rationale in the design body: §10's 'OS confinement: Linux network-namespace only' bullet names the three cut mechanisms and why ('two of them bought near-zero enforcement for real code and a 3-OS sandbox matrix'), mandates SECURITY.md state the per-OS truth, and §10's SECURITY.md bullet carries 'on macOS/Windows, no OS egress enforcement' as a named honest residual; §11 back-pressure item (6) records brokered egress + Linux netns as the enforceable form of the network allowlist, among the items that 'sharpen mechanisms alpha.15 already builds'. On macOS/Windows beta.1 equals — never regresses — the alpha line, which had zero OS-kernel enforcement on any platform at any point (grep of the full history finds no seccomp/namespace/firewall mechanism), and the regression review sweeps brokered fail-closed egress as present/strengthened. One editorial nit outside this gap's scope: §10's claim that netns is 'literally the charter's network namespace wording' does not match the current charter, which contains neither 'network namespace' nor 'allowlist' — the recording of the cut stands regardless.

- **Recorded:** Design §10 'OS confinement: Linux network-namespace only' bullet (0.1.0-beta.1-design.md L904–913) + SECURITY.md residual list (L955–961); design §11 back-pressure item (6) (L982–983); regression review 'Checked and intact' sweep (0.1.0-beta.1-alpha-regression-review.md L73–74).
- **History:** Alpha's application-level egress boundary was earned through repeated application-layer fail-open failures, never through OS enforcement: the alpha.1 shell hook never fired on live writes (ADR-27/28, history L306–310); alpha.9 recorded egress allow-by-default as a live P0 with the poisoned-paper injection threat, plus the 'merged ≠ deployed' gate and a second fail-open on plugin registration (history L1400); alpha.14 #1103 hardened allowlist matching fail-closed (L1964); alpha.15 ADR-125 made fail-closed an architecture invariant — 'a gate that proceeds on its own failure is not a gate' (L2202). Beta.1 addresses that recurring lesson more strongly than alpha ever did: engines hold no sockets structurally, Guard fails closed on policy-load failure with workers refusing to start, and on Linux the kernel netns enforces below the application layer where every alpha failure lived; the honest per-OS residual mirrors alpha's own ADR-46 correction of 'completely sandboxed' over-claiming (L669).

### S12.2 — Write-time exfiltration linter + unified canary spec/drill + per-OS keychain (vs alpha's structural no-exfil, diagnostic-plane self-test, bare loopback token)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Every facet of the delta is adjudicated in an authoritative record and all three mechanisms strengthen rather than drop invariants. The linter is recorded in the §11 convergence list ('the exfiltration linter as mechanized don't-amplify') and fully specified in §10 with one owner and write-time+export application; the regression review sweeps it as present/strengthened. The canary is an explicit §10 decision with rationale ('two incompatible canaries existed' → one spec owned by Security, weekly + post-migration drill, INC-canary incident response) serving the charter Trust row 'Canary checks'. The keychain is a §10 decision serving the charter Ops row 'Key handling', and its newness is governed by the recorded §13 BYOK/agent-boundary decision — the alpha line held no long-lived provider key to protect, so no precedent applies. The bullet's parenthetical instrumentation silence (evaluation protocol schedules no canary-drill acceptance test) is not a delta from alpha.15 — the drill's weekly + post-migration schedule and incident response are mandated in the governing design §10 itself, and the charter's evaluation scope owns retention measurement, not security ops.

- **Recorded:** Design §11 convergence list (0.1.0-beta.1-design.md L965–972, exfiltration linter); design §10 linter bullet (L914–922), keys/canary bullet (L948–954); design §13 BYOK/LLM-allocation record (L998–1058); charter Required Operations 'Key handling' row (0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md L65) and Required Trust 'Canary checks' row (L76); regression review sweep (0.1.0-beta.1-alpha-regression-review.md L73–74).
- **History:** ADR-105 (alpha.8) built the content-light diagnostic plane with a golden-corpus redaction self-test because logs were 'the first place vault-derived content could land' and 'a forgotten debug flag plus a routine git push exfiltrates unpublished research' (history L1286); alpha.11 made no-exfil structural via channel separation — agents hold no network or write authority (L1741); alpha.15 ADR-125/130 kept no-agent-tool-grants with the loopback bearer token and documented the residual 'any local bearer credential is readable by a trusted-local agent' (L2204).
