Beta.1 addresses each motivating concern by generalizing, not dropping: the linter operationalizes no-exfil as containment-at-write over all machine-writable content including extracted fulltext, the canary drill extends the ADR-105 self-test from the diagnostic plane to all artifacts/DB/logs/exports, and the keychain closes the bearer-token-era readable-credential residual for the new BYOK long-lived key alpha never held.

### S12.3 — Third-party-plugin interference revived as a named security corruption class (structurally absent in alpha.14/15 after Obsidian was dropped)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The revival is a recorded docs-history borrow, which counts as an authoritative record: the B/A/R Borrow table's 'Hostile-plugin defense' entry (target beta1) specifies exactly the §10 mechanism set — startup detection of known-hostile plugins/settings, registering machine-owned paths as formatter-excluded, auditing every plugin's data.json for secret fields before it enters backups — and design §10 implements it nearly verbatim with the human-span manifest gate named as structural backstop. The enabling delta (Obsidian back as required UI) is itself recorded as §11 back-pressure item (10), 'the host decision itself'. Even the no-alpha-precedent facets are covered: the data.json secret audit is inside the borrow entry's text, and the T3 key-leak coupling follows from the recorded §13 BYOK decision. Nothing is relitigated: the class returns only because the surface returns, and the defense is stronger than the alpha era's prohibit-or-detect-post-hoc posture.

- **Recorded:** Docs-history B/A/R Borrow table, 'Hostile-plugin defense' row (0.1.0-beta.1-docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md L44, target beta1); design §10 third-party-plugin bullet (0.1.0-beta.1-design.md L923–929); host pivot recorded as design §11 item (10) (L987–989).
- **History:** In the alpha.1–11 Obsidian/Hermes era the threat was real and handled by prohibition plus post-hoc detection: ADR-12 ruled obsidian-linter 'incompatible — do not install' because 'a deterministic tool still fails the architecture if it writes outside the Policy MCP / audit trail' (history L495); vault-hash-drift caught out-of-band edits only after the fact because Hermes hooks fail open (ADR-25/49, L495); ADR-74 (alpha.8) added the plugin-provenance lock against unprovable plugin artifacts (L1320). Alpha.14/15 dissolved the threat by removing Obsidian from the required product entirely (L2320). Beta.1 re-creates the surface via the host pivot and addresses the era's underlying failure (third-party writers bypass application gates; post-hoc-only detection) with proactive startup detection, formatter exclusion, the data.json secret audit, and the preventive human-span pre==post manifest gate with auto-rollback that the Obsidian era lacked.
## 13. Cost / snapshot / migration machinery

10 gaps — leave 6 · record 4 · change 0

### S13.1 — Cost becomes a control surface: BYOK price table, max_tokens ceilings, breaker, miss row

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The charter's Required Operations Scope Cost-control row and Success Claim 3 demand exactly this machinery ('fixed ceiling prices, monthly spend is visible, and large/cap-crossing work requires confirmation'), and design s9 specifies it as a full decision-with-rationale including the recorded reason for the single price table ('three components had diverged'). Design s11 back-pressure item 5 explicitly names the normative price table + max_tokens ceilings + confirm-over-threshold as a requirement alpha under-emphasized, and the miss-row revival is a recorded docs-history Borrow ('Ops & diagnostics integrity': unattributable spend becomes explicit miss rows). Alpha's telemetry-only posture rested on unvalidated thresholds, and beta.1 handles that concern by the charter's Calibration row: every numeric budget is a labeled pre-registered guess, with the $20 default grounded in the research evidence.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s9 (L845-869) + s11 item 5 (L981-982); 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Cost-control row (L64) + Success Claim 3; 0.1.0-beta.1-docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md Borrow row 'Ops & diagnostics integrity' (L62)
- **History:** Alpha never rejected a cost control surface; it simply never built one because 'no threshold in the prior corpus was ever validated' (ADR-129, history L2102) and the alpha.8 plane was export-only with a cost-misses writer but no aggregator (ADR-104/105/106, history L1392). Beta.1 addresses the unvalidated-threshold reason directly: budgets are pre-registered labeled guesses (charter Calibration row) and the miss-row finally gets its aggregator (breaker treats missing usage as over-budget evidence).

### S13.2 — Runner transport: OpenAI-compatible dual provider + pydantic-ai -> single Anthropic Message-Batches tier

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: medium

The substance of the swap is adjudicated by explicit decisions-with-rationale in the design body: s9 decides one pinned model tier for the whole beta ('a mid-beta tier change is a release marker, never silent') and the batch endpoint with 50% savings; s17 item 7 explicitly adjudicates the batch transport ('never batch' rejected); and s7 records the single-static-binary install with 'PyMuPDF's AGPL + Python contradicted it', a stack decision that plainly covers dropping the Python pydantic-ai runner. The function alpha's dual-pin apparatus bought - licensing every live call by a fixture/seeded-error verdict per (operation, model, mode) - is carried by s13's operation test (pinned prompt+model, fixture, arithmetic worst-case price) and s9's rule that any model or prompt pin change re-triggers fixture validation; the regression review's intact sweep verified 'per-operation model pins with test/live modes' present or strengthened.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s9 L855-861, s13 L1021-1031, s17 item 7 (L1265-1272), s7 L633-634; 0.1.0-beta.1-alpha-regression-review.md 'Checked and intact' sweep (L77)
- **History:** Alpha.14 PR-H built the dual local/gateway providers.yaml with per-operation runner.test/runner.live because 'no threshold in the prior corpus was ever validated' and non-sandbox use had to be licensed by the live model's seeded-error verdict per (operation, model, mode) (history L2102); ADR-125 pinned pydantic-ai as the sole typed runner for typed calls/structured output/retries within a Python stack (history L2096, L1940). Beta.1 keeps the licensing function (fixtures + re-validation on pin change) and removes the Python-stack premise with the recorded single-static-binary decision, so the motivating reason is honored, not re-opened.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Citations adjudicate only part of the delta: s17 item 7 records batch-transport acceptance with rationale, s9 L855-861 records one pinned tier + batch pricing. Nothing cited adjudicates the swap away from the OpenAI-compatible dual provider or the drop of pydantic-ai as the typed runner. s7 L633-634 is wrong (pdfium PDF extraction, not runner transport), and regression-review L77 only sweeps 'per-operation model pins with test/live modes' as intact. The gap entry itself says the transport swap was surfaced by verification.
- **Verifier notes:** Citations adjudicate only part of the delta: s17 item 7 records batch-transport acceptance with rationale, s9 L855-861 records one pinned tier + batch pricing. Nothing cited adjudicates the swap away from the OpenAI-compatible dual provider or the drop of pydantic-ai as the typed runner. s7 L633-634 is wrong (pdfium PDF extraction, not runner transport), and regression-review L77 only sweeps 'per-operation model pins with test/live modes' as intact. The gap entry itself says the transport swap was surfaced by verification.

### S13.3 — Relational cascade-rollback (ADR-127 2PC journal) -> git snapshots + VACUUM INTO + footprint-scoped reconciliation

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design s6 is an explicit decision-with-rationale: 'both, because they version different things' for git+VACUUM INTO, external git-dir to avoid collision with the user's vault repo, and 'Revert is DB-complete via reconciliation, not snapshots' because per-run DB snapshots 'would be write amplification in service of inverting ledgers the design defines as append-only'. Design s11 records convergence on 'one-writer + staging + run-scoped snapshots (the cross-store recoverability contract)', keeping ADR-127's pathspec commit hygiene, and the regression review's intact sweep verified 'cross-store recoverability / observable atomicity with paired rollback' held. Alpha's reason for the relational cascade - verdicts/records were relational and deliberately not file-recoverable - is dissolved by beta.1's two-class split, under which every derived table is re-derivable from post-revert files and checks re-earn via the local Checker.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s6 L448-452 and L501-510; s11 convergence list L965-970; 0.1.0-beta.1-alpha-regression-review.md intact sweep (L73-74)
- **History:** ADR-127 rejected git-as-sole-history because 'verdicts and the records graph are relational, high-cardinality, and deliberately not file-recoverable' and paid ADR-22's owned-durability cost with 2PC/fsync/recover (history L2128-2132). Beta.1 removes the premise: derived DB state is regenerable from vault files (s5 two-class split, checks fail closed to amber and re-earn), so a relational cascade has nothing left to protect that footprint reconciliation does not re-derive.

### S13.4 — ADR-127 recovery triad -> DERIVED vs OPERATIONAL taxonomy with revert carve-out and per-file conflict handling

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The taxonomy is an explicit, load-bearing recorded decision: s5 'Two DB classes, stated (the ruling idea in s0 depends on this split)' with the not-rebuildable ledgers preserved by VACUUM INTO plus vault-side exports, and s6 states the revert carve-out with rationale ('history appends, never erases'; 'cost rows never deleted'). The s18 resolutions strengthen rather than weaken the alpha triad: R1 makes verdicts DB-authoritative with fail-closed amber re-earn, and R3 restores content-addressed provider payloads as operational-ledger class. Alpha's core invariant - no human-authored datum in the accepted-loss class - is sharpened, since ledgers move from accepted-loss to backed-up-not-rebuilt and decide events are exported so no researcher judgment lives only in the DB.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s5 L429-444, s6 L505-510; s18 items 1 and 3 (L1282-1292)
- **History:** ADR-127's recovery classes existed so that files own authored meaning, provider records replay from blobs, and DB loss fails closed to unchecked, with 'No human-authored datum is ever in the accepted-loss class' (history L2132). Beta.1 addresses every leg: file authority holds, payloads replay returns via s18 R3, DB loss fails closed to amber (s5), and the formerly accepted-loss verdict/journal class is replaced by backed-up ledgers plus re-earnable checks.

### S13.5 — Write unit renamed operation -> run, with a fixed run-kind enum keying snapshot/revert/cost/Review/incidents

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The enumerated run is beta.1's own explicitly designed mechanism: s6 defines the run-kind enum inline with rationale for each elevation ('the monitor and snowball notes are vault writes, so they are runs like any other', 'rename for citekey correction'), s2 gives JobRunner run_id-minting, and the charter's Review row names the unit ('reversible by run'). The rename carries no lost invariant - alpha's per-operation journaling, idempotency, and rollback-unit semantics all map onto runs, and the gap report's own Appendix C classifies run-kind enums among below-altitude implementation detail. No alpha failure was ever attached to the 'operation' vocabulary.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s6 L454-458 and L482-488; s2 L138; 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Review row (L33)
- **History:** The 'operation' unit was alpha vocabulary from the manifest/runner era (per-operation pins, 'operation run <id>'), not a position earned by a documented failure; its operational substance (one commit per operation, journaled, revertible) is preserved and extended by the batch protocol. None found against enumeration; the docs-history memoriad job contract borrow (idempotency keys per job) is carried verbatim into s2.

### S13.6 — Anti-migration posture reversed: MigrationRunner named a beta.1 blocker

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This reversal is adjudicated in three authoritative places: design s11 item 9 ('the migration runner as a beta.1 blocker - beta is the first version whose data must survive later versions', booked as alpha.16 process scope), the charter's Upgrade-and-migration row ('Beta.1 data survives later versions through exercised, lossless migrations'), and s2's first-class MigrationRunner component. The docs-history Reject row 130 that killed migration machinery contains its own revisit trigger - 'revisit only when beta.1 creates a vault worth migrating' - and beta.1 is by definition that trigger firing, so the record and the reversal are consistent rather than contradictory.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s11 item 9 (L985-991) + s2 L147; 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Upgrade row (L61); 0.1.0-beta.1-docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md Reject row L130
- **History:** Alpha declined migration solely because no production vault existed: alpha.11 s20 'no migration, upgrade path, backwards-compatibility mode' (history L1727), alpha.12 'no migration target' (L1834), alpha.14 removed the schema-migration shim as 'dead machinery' with 'no production vault there is no migration target' (L1948). Beta.1 removes that premise - a real researcher's real corpus - which is exactly the condition the recorded rejection reserved for revival.

### S13.7 — Bare PRAGMA user_version -> structured migrations ledger table

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: overturned leave->record (citation failed audit) · confidence: medium

The ledger table is the concrete mechanism of the recorded migration-runner decision (s11 item 9 + charter Upgrade row) and is itself specified in the design body: s5's schema defines migrations(n, name, kind, applied_ts, git_pre_tag, db_snapshot, status) alongside meta.schema_version, and s6 step 1 reserves the VACUUM INTO snapshot for import/migration kinds. The charter bar 'exercised, lossless migrations' requires per-migration pre-tag/snapshot/status accounting that a bare integer cannot carry, so the delta is plainly covered by the broader recorded decision. ADR-125's rejection targeted ORM/migration frameworks, and a hand-rolled ledger table over stdlib DDL does not re-open it.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s5 L373 (schema) + s6 L461-462; covered by s11 item 9 (L985-987) and 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Upgrade row (L61)
- **History:** ADR-125's 'ORM + migration framework rejected: the integrity schema is the product; single-user scale needs .sql + user_version only' (history L2096) was an anti-dependency stance taken when no vault needed migrating, not a validated ceiling on migration bookkeeping. Beta.1 keeps the anti-framework substance (a plain SQLite table, no ORM) while adding the audit columns the charter's lossless-migration bar demands, so the motivating reason survives intact.
- **Action:** Record this delta in the design s11 divergence list; the claimed citation did not hold: Not adjudicated at the cited locations: s5 L373 is a bare schema line (the surrounding consolidation rationale covers anchors/links, not migrations), s6 L461-462 only mentions VACUUM INTO snapshots for migration kinds, s11 item 9 adjudicates the migration-runner posture reversal (item S13.6's delta) not the ledger-table-vs-PRAGMA-user_version mechanism, and charter L61 is an outcome bar silent on mechanism. No cited record carries a decision with rationale for replacing the bare user_version integer with a structured ledger; the gap entry marks this delta as verify-findings-surfaced.
- **Verifier notes:** Not adjudicated at the cited locations: s5 L373 is a bare schema line (the surrounding consolidation rationale covers anchors/links, not migrations), s6 L461-462 only mentions VACUUM INTO snapshots for migration kinds, s11 item 9 adjudicates the migration-runner posture reversal (item S13.6's delta) not the ledger-table-vs-PRAGMA-user_version mechanism, and charter L61 is an outcome bar silent on mechanism. No cited record carries a decision with rationale for replacing the bare user_version integer with a structured ledger; the gap entry marks this delta as verify-findings-surfaced.

### S13.8 — overrides.jsonl tiered DB-loss replay dropped; streaming-replication backup leg declined

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

The streaming-replication half is a recorded decision (s18 item 5: declined with rationale and a revisit trigger, grounded in the Litestream #1083 silent-failure evidence), but the overrides.jsonl tiered-replay drop has no record anywhere in the design, s18, or the docs-history tables - the gap report itself notes 'no dedicated record defense'. On the merits the drop is sound because ADR-127's invariant is honored structurally: restrictive/meaning-bearing dispositions now live in git-tracked frontmatter (superseded/reading) and so survive DB loss at the file layer without replay, entity/triage decide events are exported to vault CSVs, and permissive states re-earn by construction since mem rebuild fails closed to amber and re-verifies every checks verdict via the local Checker. The residual delta - decide events since the last backup/weekly export are an accepted-loss window where alpha's append-at-decision-time log had zero RPO - is small at N=1 scale but is exactly the kind of divergence the design's own name-every-divergence discipline says to record.

- **Recorded:** Partial: design s18 item 5 (L1297-1302) records the streaming-replication decline and inspector-pane backup status; the overrides.jsonl tiered-replay drop is nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-127 tiered the replay because 'the journal witness is gone, so the log cannot be trusted to unblock anything' and 'No human-authored datum is ever in the accepted-loss class' (history L2132, PR-B #1163). Beta.1 addresses both reasons by different mechanisms: unblocking states (check verdicts) re-earn via the fail-closed amber rebuild (s5 L407-411), and human dispositions live in the git-tracked vault rather than a sidecar log - only the between-export decide-event window weakens the second invariant slightly.
- **Action:** Add to design s11's divergence list (or s18): "ADR-127's git-tracked overrides.jsonl + tiered DB-loss replay is not carried: researcher dispositions live in git-tracked frontmatter (superseded/reading) and the exported decide-events CSV, so restrictive decisions survive DB loss at the file layer, and permissive states re-earn structurally - mem rebuild fails closed to amber and re-verifies every checks verdict via the local Checker. The 'restrictions reapply, permissions re-earn' invariant holds by construction; decide events since the last VACUUM INTO/weekly export are the accepted-loss window."

### S13.9 — DB-row hash chain + journal-head tamper anchor dropped; git commit chain resumes as tamper-evidence root

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: high

No authoritative record names the drop - the design never mentions the hash chain or journal-head, and s11/s18 are silent - but the delta is sound because the object the chain protected no longer exists: alpha.12 chained rows inside the DB only because the SQLite journal had become the record of authority, and beta.1 replaces that journal with the Memoria-owned git history (Mem-Run trailers), whose commit chain is itself the Merkle structure ADR-104 originally pointed at. The charter's Trust scope contains no tamper-evidence requirement, and the alpha line's own recorded position was that anchoring beyond git is 'theater' under single-researcher scope. Operational ledgers remain append-only evidence without a cryptographic root, which is a narrowing worth naming so it does not read as a silent loss.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent
- **History:** ADR-104 rejected in-file prev_hash chains because 'the vault is already a Git repo - commit history is a Merkle chain' and anchoring against a distinct adversary is 'theater' at single-researcher scope (history L1284); alpha.12 reversed inside the DB because the journal-integrity spike showed the now-authoritative SQLite journal's rows 'need an external git-tracked head anchor for tamper-evidence' (L1788), and ADR-127's journal-head 'narrows ADR-104's rejection' (L2130). Beta.1 removes the DB journal-of-record entirely, so the reason for the reversal is dissolved and the design lands back on ADR-104's original, still-valid posture.
- **Action:** Add to design s11's divergence list: "The alpha.12/ADR-127 DB-row hash chain + .memoria/journal-head anchor are not carried: the SQLite journal-of-record they protected no longer exists, and the Memoria-owned git history (Mem-Run trailers) is the tamper-evidence root - returning to ADR-104's git-is-the-Merkle-chain posture. Operational ledgers stay append-only evidence but carry no cryptographic root; heavier anchoring is theater at single-researcher scope (ADR-104's own framing)."

### S13.10 — Derived store relocated out of the synced vault to a per-device OS data dir

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The placement is an explicit decision-with-rationale in the design body: s5 opens with the DB at ~/.local/share/memoria/<vault-id>/memoria.db 'outside the synced tree, per-device, transactional, single-file backup via VACUUM INTO' (payloads in the same per-device dir), and the twin s6 relocation states the sync rationale in full ('no collision with the user's own vault repo and no .git churn in their file sync'). The alpha placement was affordable only under alpha.12's explicitly relaxed 'no multi-device sync (single machine)' constraint, whereas beta.1's plugin+daemon operates over the researcher's existing, possibly file-synced vault - putting a live WAL SQLite file inside such a tree is the corruption path the relocation avoids, while the charter's multi-device-writes exclusion still holds (one writing host).

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s5 L361-363 and L436-437; s6 L448-452 (sync-churn rationale for the paired relocation)
- **History:** Alpha.12 gave the DB an in-vault gitignored home (.memoria/state/) because 'the DB is authoritative working state, not a rebuildable index' needing a durable per-machine location (history L1778), and the whole boundary was made affordable by relaxing to 'no multi-device sync (single machine)' (L2310). Beta.1 honors the durable-per-machine-home reason exactly - it just moves the home to the XDG data dir (rhyming with ADR-105's diagnostics XDG plane, L1392) because the single-machine premise no longer bounds the vault's file-sync exposure.
## 14. Platform

5 gaps — leave 5 · record 0 · change 0

### S14.1 — Platform split re-introduced on a new axis (security-guarantee strength) after alpha.14/15 flattened the runtime-location split

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The umbrella delta has no normative content beyond its four facets, and every facet is individually adjudicated in the design body: the Linux-only kernel egress layer and the macOS/Windows sandbox cut are recorded with rationale and an honest-residual line in s10; the per-OS keychain in s10 and Windows code-signing in s16; the desktop-only plugin and mobile keep-test mode in s16 with recorded flip conditions; s11 items (6) and (10) record the netns and host decisions as deliberate beta.1 scope. The alpha-line flattening this superficially resembles removed a runtime-location prerequisite (Hermes WSL2-only, ending in 'one install command, no external runtime, no always-on process'); B1 imposes no OS prerequisite — one `mem` artifact installs and runs cross-platform (s16 'One artifact') — and splits only guarantee strength and adapter tier, so the reason alpha flattened its old OS dimension is not re-opened.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s10 L904-913 + L955-959 (Linux-only confinement, per-OS SECURITY.md residual), s10 L946-949 (keychain), s16 L1169-1171 (code-signing), s16 L1184-1191 + L1222-1232 (desktop-only plugin, mobile keep-test, flip conditions), s11 items (6) and (10)
- **History:** Alpha's only platform split was runtime-location: Hermes WSL2-only with Windows as the editing surface (ADR-26/55/64; history L565-579), whose documented costs were WSL2 as hard prerequisite, /mnt/c file-lock fights, the OneDrive hazard, and the networkingMode=mirrored bridge; alpha.14/15 removed it by dropping Hermes and shipping standalone installers (history L2022, L2190, L2302-2304). B1 preserves exactly the property that fix earned — single cross-platform artifact, no external runtime — so the motivating failure is addressed, not re-opened.

### S14.2 — Facet A: OS-enforced kernel egress (CLONE_NEWNET netns) is Linux-only; seccomp/macOS sandbox-exec/Windows-Firewall flows cut

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design s10 records the decision explicitly and with its reasoning: the three non-Linux OS-enforcement flows are cut because two of them 'bought near-zero enforcement for real code and a 3-OS sandbox matrix,' and SECURITY.md is required to state the per-OS truth plainly, with 'on macOS/Windows, no OS egress enforcement' carried in the honest-residual list. The charter's prompt-injection bar (untrusted text cannot control vault egress, req L74) is met OS-independently by brokered egress — engines hold no sockets at all and Guard is the sole network path — and the Linux netns is a strict addition on top of that. Alpha never had OS-kernel enforcement on any OS, so nothing alpha earned is lost; s11 item (6) further records brokered egress + Linux netns as the enforceable form of the allowlist.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s10 L904-913 ('OS confinement: Linux network-namespace only' with the cut and rationale) and L955-959 (SECURITY.md honest residuals); s11 back-pressure item (6)
- **History:** The alpha line's egress control was always application-level: the alpha.1 write-layer policy gate (ADR-22, permissions enforced per-profile at the write layer), alpha.9 egress-as-P0, alpha.11 channel-separation + allowed_network, alpha.14/15 no-agent-tool-grants — with no OS-kernel layer at any point in alpha.1-alpha.15 (gap report L146 twin bullet; history L1852 fail-closed provider allowlist as data-config over the manifest ceiling). There is no documented alpha failure behind cross-OS kernel enforcement to re-open; B1 keeps a strictly stronger application layer on every OS and adds kernel enforcement where it is cheap.

### S14.3 — Facet B: per-OS keychain for BYOK keys + code-signed Windows builds, both new in B1

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Both additions are recorded design decisions serving a charter bar. s10 specifies the per-OS keychain (Keychain / DPAPI / Secret Service, mode-0600 fallback with logged warning on Linux) and the invariant 'the key exists only in the keychain and Guard's memory,' directly implementing the charter Key-handling row (keys never enter vault content, backups, exports, or logs — req L65). s16 records Windows code-signing with its reasoning (SmartScreen reputation is per-identity, unsigned builds restart at zero every release) plus a recorded flip condition (package-manager-only channel if signing proves untenable). The delta is purely additive: alpha held no long-lived user key as a first-class secret, so no alpha invariant is displaced and nothing needs a divergence entry.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s10 L946-949 (keychain, key-residence invariant), s16 L1169-1171 (code-signing) + L1231-1232 (flip condition); requirements charter Key handling L65
- **History:** In the Hermes era, keys lived in per-profile .env files seeded by the installer ('Hermes reads per-profile .env only... The installer must seed shared keys into each profile .env', ADR-27 Finding 6, history L360), and model routing was a Hermes/OpenRouter deployment concern (history L593); by alpha.15 the sole credential was the loopback bearer token MEMORIA_HTTP_TOKEN. Alpha never had, and never rejected, a keychain; B1's BYOK (design s13) creates the first first-class user secret and the keychain is strictly stronger than the .env precedent. No failure re-opened.

### S14.4 — Facet C: Obsidian plugin is desktop-only and is the only researcher UI — the 'own ADR / next wave' work alpha.15's scope boundary punted

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The host decision and its desktop-only scope are adjudicated in s16, which records both the rationale (the plugin fronts the daemon; PDF extraction, embeddings, NLI, egress brokering, and the DB sit in a separate OS process for crash isolation, not Electron; the obsidian-git mobile-JS-fallback lesson) and the exact obligation the alpha.15 scope gate imposed: the decision 'amends ADR-125 and ADR-130 and requires that ADR before implementation begins,' with docs/reference/obsidian-plugins.md unchanged until it lands. s11 item (10) separately records the host decision as new beta.1 scope. The substance of the alpha demotion is preserved, not reverted: the engine remains the product (one `mem` artifact), the plugin is a client of the read-API, and every surface keeps a no-plugin floor except Ask, which s1 rules has no survival role — so this continues the alpha.12-15 arc under its own recorded terms.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s16 L1152-1158 (ADR obligation, named) and L1184-1191 (isDesktopOnly: true, catalog-clean); s11 back-pressure item (10); s1 L85-88 (no-plugin floors)
- **History:** Alpha.12 demoted Obsidian to an optional adapter on the principle 'the engine is the product... don't make Obsidian, Zotero, Hermes, or any adapter the architecture' (history L1814, ADR-122 era); alpha.14 dropped it as a required surface — 'product must run on vim/nano/file browser' (L1930, L2052); alpha.15 fenced plugin work behind 'its own ADR' and 'alpha.15 cannot close with Obsidian plugin implementation counted as release scope' (ADR-130, #1203/#1208, L2216). The motivating concern — an adapter owning state/policy/the write boundary and loss of the standalone floor — is addressed: B1 keeps the standalone engine with CLI floors and explicitly pays the required-ADR obligation before implementation.

### S14.5 — Facet D: mobile is keep-test mode by design — synced markdown + Bases catalog views, no daemon, no verdict-bearing views

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The mobile stance is recorded in s16 ('Mobile is keep-test mode by design: synced markdown, PDFs, Bases catalog views, mem-prov markers in source mode — no JS-fallback daemon heroics, the obsidian-git lesson') with an explicit recorded flip condition: if mobile capture/triage becomes a real daily-loop requirement, the move is thin-client-to-server (the Khoj archetype), a deployment decision, never a plugin heroic. The structural reason a daemon-less device renders only meaning-only views is itself recorded in s15 (meaning-only frontmatter keeps verdicts out of files, so native Bases structurally cannot carry check_status; anything verdict-bearing comes through the read-API). The write-side boundary is anchored in the charter's Deliberate Exclusion of concurrent multi-device writes (req L87), which is decisive under the calibration rules.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md s16 L1189-1191 + flip conditions L1224-1227; s15 L1093-1097 (forcing move); requirements charter Deliberate Exclusions L87 ('Concurrent multi-device writes')
- **History:** 'mobile' appears nowhere in the ~2400-line design history (grep over the full file: zero hits), confirming A15's zero design presence — there is no alpha 'mobile era' to revert to. The lineage B1 projects onto the device class is continued, not dropped: the alpha.12 keep-test (ADR-122 — markdown + portable bibliography survive the tool, history L2308) and the no-daemon CLI recovery surface (ADR-130, L2176); and the docs-history Reject table independently keeps mobile capture via network channels dead ('synced vault files the daemon ingests — never a network service'). The charter exclusion protects against the Obsidian-Sync last-write-wins data-loss risk; no failure re-opened.
## 15. Onboarding / seeding

5 gaps — leave 4 · record 1 · change 0

### S15.1 — Onboarding promoted from dormant alpha remnant to a centered beta.1 onboarding contract

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The reframe is adjudicated in exactly the authoritative place: design §11 records 'guided corpus seeding + time-to-first-Ask as the onboarding contract' as back-pressure item (2) and marks items (1)-(3) and (10) as new alpha.16 scope, and the charter's Install row (first value from a quickstart in under 30 minutes) plus Capture row make it a requirement with no Deliberate-Exclusion row against it. The alpha-line dormancy being reversed was alpha.11 reset collateral, never an earned position against onboarding. The paper adversarial review additionally keeps 'onboarding as retention mechanism' as a defended survivor, so the centering is consistent with the charter's retention-experiment framing.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md §11 L974-977 and L989 (back-pressure item (2), new alpha.16 scope); 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Install row L60 and Capture row L29; corroborated by 0.1.0-beta.1-paper-adversarial-review.md L101
- **History:** Onboarding peaked at alpha.10's clean-slate ADR-111/112/113 arc (history L1424, L1535-1583) and was dismantled at alpha.11's mass architecture reset, which seeded 'only test projects and captured sources created through the alpha.11 pipeline' (history L1763) — deletion as rebuild collateral, not a documented failure of onboarding. Beta.1's retention charter re-motivates centering it (paper-adversarial-review.md L101: Luger & Sellen 2016, Epstein et al. 2020, Brown et al. 2007), so no unaddressed failure is re-opened.

### S15.2 — Onboarding wizard: the deferred ADR-113 guided first-loop built as a linear, non-agent first-run sequence

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The wizard is the mechanism of the §11-recorded guided-seeding back-pressure decision, so the delta is plainly covered by a recorded broader decision, and §7 specifies it with in-body rationale ('This is what meets install → grounded answer ≤30 min'). ADR-113 was deferred on a sequencing precondition — the doc arc had to stabilize before an agent layer dramatized it — not on any failure of guided onboarding, and beta.1 sidesteps that precondition entirely: the wizard is a linear plugin flow with one confirm and no conversational agent, consistent with §13's 'Memoria is not an agent, and beta.1 adds none.' The docs-history 'never an enforced wizard' refusal governs compose stages (counter-outlines Borrow row) and the rejected 'mandatory ingest interview' is a per-source required conversation — the optional first-run seeding flow violates neither.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md §7 'Corpus seeding (onboarding wizard)' L684-689 (decision with rationale) under §11 item (2) L976-977/L989; consistency records: design §13 L1006, docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md L53 (compose-only wizard refusal) and L124 (mandatory-interview reject)
- **History:** ADR-113 (Co-PI-guided conversational onboarding) was recorded proposed/deferred because 'the ADR-112 doc arc is the script the agent layer would dramatize, so it must exist and stabilize first; building the agent layer against a moving doc flow would mean syncing two moving targets' (history L1546-1547) — a precondition, not an earned rejection. Beta.1 removes the agent from the first loop entirely, so the deferred hazard structurally cannot recur.

### S15.3 — Seeding relevance shifts from deterministic steering.md ranking to a priced LLM yes/no prefilter; paper-record vote-k Borrow not carried by the design

**RECORD — sound but unrecorded** · verification: confirmed (skeptic found no prior record) · confidence: medium

The prefilter is sound on the merits: it passes §13's operation test (pinned prompt + fixture, printable worst-case price, batchable), is optional, gates only digest spend ahead of a human confirm, and confers no verdict — preserving the proposer-never-authority line §13 keeps ('Neither side, ever: confers a verdict'). The alpha deterministic precedent was earned at a different pipeline stage — ranking external discovery candidates where abstracts/fulltext were unreliable — while the seeding wizard runs after $0 extraction+indexing, so the data-availability reason that kept model judgment out is satisfied rather than violated. What is missing is any record: no authoritative location adjudicates the deterministic-to-paid shift against the alpha precedent, and beta.1's own paper record Borrows a vote-k deterministic seed-selection algorithm for guided corpus seeding that the governing design does not carry or disposition — an unreconciled conflict between two beta.1 records.

- **Recorded:** nowhere - silent (design §13 L1033-1035 rosters the prefilter and applies the operation test, but neither §7, §11, nor §13 engages the alpha deterministic precedent or the paper-borrow-adapt-reject.md L17 vote-k Borrow the design omits)
- **History:** ADR-92 (alpha.15) accepted deterministic steering.md relevance for provider-discovered candidates because 'the cheap deterministic path clears the bar; ML deferred until data exists' and 'model embedding similarity remains out until candidate abstracts/full text are reliably present' (history L2162); ADR-129 required each tier to beat a declared cheap baseline (history L2152). Beta.1's prefilter operates on already-extracted fulltext with a printed price and a downstream human confirm, so the motivating precondition no longer applies — though no cheap-baseline comparison for the prefilter is recorded.
- **Action:** Add one recorded-divergence line to design §11 (or a sentence in §7): 'Seeding relevance runs as a priced, optional LLM yes/no prefilter under the §13 operation test, superseding alpha.15's deterministic steering.md relevance channel (ADR-92), which targeted fulltext-less external discovery candidates. The paper-record vote-k seed-selection Borrow (Su et al. 2022, paper-borrow-adapt-reject.md) is declined for beta.1 [or: adopted as a deterministic candidate-selection stage ahead of the prefilter], closing the conflict with the design of record.'
- **Verifier notes:** text correction: Replace "superseding alpha.15's deterministic steering.md relevance channel (ADR-92), which targeted fulltext-less external discovery candidates" with wording that does not claim supersession, e.g.: "Seeding relevance is a new, priced, optional LLM yes/no prefilter under the S13 operation test, gating only digest spend ahead of a human confirm. It does not reopen ADR-92's deterministic-relevance precedent: ADR-92 governed ranking fulltext-less external discovery candidates ("model embedding similarity remains out until candidate abstracts/full text are reliably present"), a stage beta.1 keeps deterministic (occurrence-counting, identifier-only, S7/S13), while the prefilter runs after $0 extraction+indexing, satisfying that precondition. The paper-record vote-k seed-selection Borrow (Su et al. 2022, paper-borrow-adapt-reject.md L17) is declined for beta.1 [or: adopted as the deterministic candidate-selection stage — and declared cheap baseline per ADR-129 — ahead of the prefilter], closing the conflict with the design of record." Keep the proposed location (one recorded-divergence line in design S11, or a sentence in S7).

### S15.4 — New measurable install → grounded answer ≤30 min contract (time-to-first-Ask)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The contract is not a silent delta — it is itself a charter requirement (Install row: 'clean-machine install reaches first value from a quickstart in under 30 minutes'), and the charter is the spec; the design records the enabling mechanism (§7: the first Ask is prompted before digests return, over indexed raw fulltext at $0) and §11 marks time-to-first-Ask as deliberate new alpha.16 scope, with §17 item 7 deferring to it. The bullet's noted silence — evaluation-protocol.md not scoring ≤30-min as a pre-registered metric — is structurally consistent, not a lost invariant: Install sits in Required Operations Scope, which the charter's scope map assigns to the design, while the protocol owns only the Required Evaluation Scope rows; an install-time acceptance bar is verified once at install and no success claim depends on it.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md Required Operations Scope Install row L60; 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md §7 L689, §11 item (2) L976-977, §17 L1271
- **History:** Alpha never bound install-to-first-answer time; ADR-111 reasoned 'done for real the knowledge loop takes months, so a one-sitting tutorial can't reproduce the payoff' and substituted a pre-seeded corpus for a time bound (history L1538). Beta.1 addresses that reasoning rather than re-opening it: the ≤30-min bound covers only mechanical first value (a $0 grounded Ask before any paid digest), while the payoff-density problem ADR-111 identified is still answered by re-adopting its pre-seeded sample corpus.

### S15.5 — Re-introduction of the retired alpha.10 half-built sample corpus (ADR-111 fixture)

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The re-introduction is an adjudicated Borrow in the docs-history borrow/adapt/reject record — which counts as a recorded decision — and the governing design carries it with every earned constraint intact: ~8 real citable sources, never generated ('a faked seed models the exact anti-pattern the product prevents'), deliberately half-built, idempotent load, clean removal by archive label, doubling as the end-to-end test fixture and demo. The alpha.11 retirement it reverses was reset collateral rather than a merits verdict, so re-introduction re-opens no documented failure, and beta.1 additionally fences the fixture from the genuine-use evaluation substrate the research evidence demands. The bullet's residual note — that this entry belongs in the gap report's 'Removed in A15, re-introduced in B1' appendix list — is report-side bookkeeping, not a missing design record.

- **Recorded:** 0.1.0-beta.1-docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md Borrow row 'Half-built sample corpus' L42 (target beta1; sourced to adr/111-two-mode-tutorial-spine.md, tutorials/sample-vault/README.md, reference/vocabulary-example.md) and Recommended action 8 L155; carried in 0.1.0-beta.1-design.md §7 L690-695
- **History:** ADR-111 built the mediterranean-diet sample vault because a one-sitting tutorial cannot reproduce a months-long knowledge loop, and required real-source authorship since 'learners imitate the form they are shown … a faked seed teaches fabrication of the exact thing the system prevents' (history L1537-1538); ADR-112 retained the seeded vault while superseding the tutorial spine (L1581); alpha.11 removed it only because the reset seeded 'only test projects and captured sources created through the alpha.11 pipeline' (L1763). Beta.1 preserves the earned rationale in full, so the reason for the alpha.10 position is honored and the alpha.11 removal reason no longer applies.
## 16. Reading / annotation

7 gaps — leave 7 · record 0 · change 0

### S16.1 — Zotero-first reading substrate reverts the alpha.14 Zotero cut

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17 item 1 explicitly records "Reading is Zotero-first" — primary read in Zotero's PDF reader, fulltext.md demoted to evidence substrate and kept as the full path for non-Zotero works — as a resolution "recorded so they are not re-litigated," and §16 records Zotero as an app reached over its read-only local API with no Obsidian-side Zotero plugin. The premise that motivated the alpha.14 cut (standalone CLI must not depend on a desktop reference manager) is itself deliberately reversed on the record: §11 item 10 names the host decision (Obsidian plugin + local daemon) as new beta.1 scope amending ADR-125, and §16 names the required ADR. The charter's null workflow is Zotero+Obsidian and the capture bar requires Zotero import, so Zotero-first reading serves the retention experiment directly. The two documented Zotero failure modes are avoided: the .bib auto-export second-source-of-truth is replaced by the read-only local API, and PDFs are copied into works/<citekey>/ so the corpus survives Zotero's death (design §7 L554–557; docs-history Reject "Zotero anti-patterns").

- **Recorded:** design §17 item 1 (L1241–1244); §11 item 10 (L987–989); §16 plugin-coexistence bullet (L1206–1211); docs-history Reject "Zotero anti-patterns" (L123)
- **History:** ADR-124 (history L2042, L2316) cut Zotero because "Alpha.14 makes Memoria a standalone CLI/engine. A required Zotero library or live Better BibTeX auto-export would violate that" — a premise, not a Zotero failure. Beta.1 reverses that premise on the record (§11 item 10, §16) and re-adopts alpha.11's read-only Local API discipline (history L1681); the genuinely earned Zotero lessons (stale .bib exports, deep-link PDF ownership dying with Zotero) are addressed by the local API and vault-owned PDF copies.

### S16.2 — Researcher-set `reading: skip|cite-only|read` frontmatter disposition key

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17 item 2 records the key explicitly: "researcher-set decisions (`reading`) are the only new frontmatter," in the same breath re-rejecting machine-owned stage frontmatter — so the boundary was adjudicated, not slipped. The verify-findings complaint that the key was unstated in §7 prose is resolved in the current design: §7 L705–708 states the key, its values, and its setting paths (designated Zotero tag/color or the work page), and the §3 frontmatter example carries it at L275. The key is human-set meaning-bearing intent (like `archived`), never machine state, so it does not reopen the forged-status/hash-churn failure that motivated meaning-only frontmatter.

- **Recorded:** design §17 item 2 (L1245–1248); §7 (L705–708); §3 frontmatter example (L274–275)
- **History:** Alpha held "no reading disposition" as a side effect of ADR-126's meaning-only frontmatter, earned by the documented check_status-in-frontmatter failure ("hand-edits forged status, and every consumer had to distrust the file it was reading," history L2086) and the repeatedly killed maturity/lifecycle ladders (docs-history Reject L109). Beta.1's key is researcher-set intent, not machine or lifecycle state, so the motivating failure does not apply; §17.2 confirms machine stage state stays DB-side.

### S16.3 — One-way append-only Zotero annotation sync inverts the alpha.11 sourcing refusal

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17 item 1 records the append-only annotation sync as part of the Zotero-first resolution folded into the body, and the mechanism is fully specified with its discipline in §7 L697–705 (one-way, keyed by Zotero annotation ID, dateAdded watermark, nothing flows back) and §5's append-only annotations table (L401–402), routed through the single-writer machine-write module. The alpha.11 refusal was premised on Memoria-owned PDF capture storing its own selectors; beta.1 removes that premise by making Zotero the primary reader, so annotation sync becomes the necessary conduit rather than a competing import path. The one-way pattern matches the settled community precedent (Notero/Better Notes/mdnotes) the gap report cites, and no write-back path exists to create the sync races the alpha line feared.

- **Recorded:** design §17 item 1 (L1241–1244); §7 (L697–705); §5 annotations table (L401–402)
- **History:** Alpha.11 §13 refused Zotero annotation import because "Memoria-owned PDF capture stores canonical quote/span/hash selectors itself" (history L1681) — a scoping decision under a Memoria-owned reading architecture, not a documented failure of annotation import. Alpha.14 then removed the whole Zotero surface on the standalone-CLI premise (ADR-124, history L1982). Beta.1 reverses both premises on the record (§17.1, §11 item 10), so the refusal's reason no longer applies.

### S16.4 — Exact-quote-only anchoring; W3C fuzzy re-anchoring deferred with a revive trigger

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The narrowing is an explicit decision-with-rationale in the design body: §7 L701–705 states the exact-quote bridge and that "fuzzy re-anchoring is Hypothesis-grade engineering, deferred until a measured orphan rate demands it," with the pre-registered revive trigger; §17 item 1 records the exact-quote anchor bridge as a resolution. The load-bearing half of the alpha position — never silently rebind or drop, failures surfaced as orphaned-anchor attention — is preserved intact via per-work orphan counting and annotations.status. Extractor-drift exposure is separately mitigated: ^pNNNN block IDs are assigned once at deterministic extraction with geometry in the anchors table keyed by text_sha256, rebuildable by re-running the same extraction.

- **Recorded:** design §7 (L701–705, explicit deferral with rationale and revive trigger); §17 item 1 (L1241–1244)
- **History:** ADR-129 bound the exact-then-fuzzy policy as "the Hypothes.is lesson": anchors are "re-anchored, never silently rebound or dropped" across extractor upgrades, with failures routed to orphaned-anchor attention (history L2140); ADR-126 relocated the excerpt to a W3C TextQuoteSelector (history L2076). The earned invariant is the never-silent posture, not the fuzzy algorithm; beta.1 keeps that invariant (visible orphans, pre-registered revive trigger) while deferring the fuzzy half until measured data justifies it.

### S16.5 — Per-work orphan counting as the honesty price of exact-quote anchoring

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

This is a new-in-B1 mechanism fully specified with rationale in the governing design: §7 L703–705 states misses are counted per work as orphans, "never silently dropped," §5's annotations table carries the status field (L401–402), and the evaluation protocol lists annotation orphan counts among the instrumented day-1 signals (eval protocol L55). It strengthens rather than weakens the alpha line — it is the charter's absence-rendered-as-absence honesty requirement applied to anchoring, and it is the pre-registered trigger for reviving fuzzy re-anchoring. Nothing about it re-opens alpha.11's fail-closed posture: the annotation row lands complete with an orphan status, never as partial state.

- **Recorded:** design §7 (L703–705); §5 annotations table (L401–402); evaluation-protocol §3 (L55)
- **History:** Alpha.11 expressed selector failure as a fail-closed job `failed` transition (no partial state), and ADR-129 routed anchor failures to orphaned-anchor attention (history L2140) — the visible-failure posture beta.1 continues as a counter. No documented alpha failure argues against visible orphan counting; it is the same never-silent discipline in a different rendering.

### S16.6 — Processing card / batch triage surface for new highlights

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

Design §17 item 1 records the processing card as part of the Zotero-first resolution, and §7 L708–720 specifies it with full rationale: one dismissible card per work batch, promote/link/drop/snooze worklist under §1's review discipline, machine pre-fill staying m-class with monotone taint, and zero-human-typed-character promotions flagged in Review — explicitly closing the laundering path. It is a recorded docs-history Borrow ("Batch worklists for high-cardinality decisions," one aggregate prompt, never N queue items — "forty cards train select-all-accept"), and the regression review's intact sweep confirms beta.1 kept act/ask/log routing, not an approval queue, so the surface does not re-open the removed pre-write approval-gate failure: it triages already-landed appends, it never gates writes.

- **Recorded:** design §17 item 1 (L1241–1244); §7 (L708–720); docs-history Borrow "Batch worklists for high-cardinality decisions" (L28); regression-review checked-and-intact sweep (L69)
- **History:** A15 had no triage surface because the presentation half of disposition telemetry died in doc-deletion packaging events, not on merits (docs-history headline L16, patterns L134); the related earned failure — the graduated pre-write approval gate and drip-fed queue items training select-all-accept — is documented in docs-history Reject L117 and Borrow L28, and beta.1's one-card batch-worklist shape is designed specifically to that lesson.

### S16.7 — Mandatory standalone `work interview` elicitation dropped; 2–3-question hook retained

**LEAVE — deliberate and recorded** · verification: confirmed (citation audited) · confidence: high

The drop is adjudicated in an authoritative record: the docs-history Reject entry "Mandatory ingest interview" keeps it dead with a full rationale — a required LLM conversation per source violates no-mandatory-agent/PI-direct access, inflates exactly the per-source burden the retention experiment measures, and duplicates annotations→notes — and the Adapt entry "Researcher takeaways as digest inputs" records the surviving replacement shape (direct affordance, no mandatory agent). Beta.1 honors the elicitation intent in substance through the annotation sync plus processing-card promotion path (§7) and the retained 2–3-question hook in the digest pipeline, so the subjective layer the interview served still has a channel. The charter's Capture bar ("no mandatory per-item decisions") independently forbids a mandatory per-source interview, making the drop charter-required, not merely defensible.

- **Recorded:** docs-history Reject "Mandatory ingest interview" (L124) and Adapt "Researcher takeaways as digest inputs" (L92); charter Capture bar (requirements L29); design §7 processing-card path (L708–720)
- **History:** Alpha.11 made the interview "the hinge … not an optional side chat" on the Karpathy-lineage belief that conversation turns capture into knowledge (history L1679), and alpha.14/15 carried `work interview` in the loop with digest failing on a required-but-missing interview (history L1984, L2188) — an aspiration, never a position earned by a documented failure. Beta.1 addresses the same aim at lower per-source cost via annotations→notes plus the in-pipeline hook, exactly the substitution the Reject entry names.
## Owner-position re-examination (2026-07-05)

One agent per contested position family (R-1 excluded: hard ruling; R-14/R-16/R-18 excluded: endorsements), each taking the owner position as a hypothesis, establishing the actual design history, and steelmanning both sides before a verdict; every verdict was then attacked by an opposite-side skeptic (evidence-only, no default refutation). All 12 verdicts survived their skeptics. Verdicts are recommendations: the open questions under each are the owner’s to close.

### R-2 — Hub is required (wiki<->ZK bridge)

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** Hub is the only knowledge concept that survived every alpha reset with a fresh re-derivation each time: Old Skeleton MOC -> ADR-50 rename keeping the ADR-19 threshold-alert mechanism (design-history L148-149), alpha.11's 25->12 collapse kept and reshaped it as "the merged Karpathy concept-page x ZK MOC: the machine keeps the topic synthesis current, the human owns the structure + argument" (L1637), and alpha.15's ADR-126 kept it among four types while deleting nine schemas (L2078). Alpha.11's three-node graph — digest (machine) / note (human) / hub (both) (L2284) — makes the owner's bridge framing literal architecture: hub was the one node both authors write, and digests were defined as "what hubs draw from" (L1635), so the digest->hub link was real, not retrofitted. Beta.1's own commissioned research reached verdict adopt on editorial hubs as the organizing layer (info-flow-research L612 "editorial at the hub layer"; L614, L625, L689 all adopt), yet design §17's seven resolutions never dispose of these verdicts, breaking §17's own "resolved... folded into the body — recorded so they are not re-litigated" contract; the design's only hub text is a rationale-free parenthetical (§7 L623). Docs-history Borrow #42 (line 42, target beta1) requires "a worked-example starter hub set marked example-not-default" in the sample corpus — an authoritative recorded borrow that cannot land in a no-hub design. And with the vocabulary substrate also dropped (S3.7) and no tags field (gap-report L44 correction), beta.1 has no salience/organizing layer at all — its generated navigation-only index.md projections (§3 L242-246) are precisely ADR-19's "generated list that looks curated but isn't" hazard with nothing answering it.

**For beta.1:** No charter row requires hubs and no Deliberate Exclusion covers them: beta.1 is "a retention experiment... not a feature milestone" (requirements L9-11), every Required Product Scope bar is met without a hub type, and the knowledge-format row demands OKF conformance parity, not type-roster parity (requirements L36). The same research the owner leans on size-gates the hub layer: structure notes became necessary only around 1,000-1,500 notes, and "beta.1 vaults will be small: hub suggestion, orphan detection, and heavy corpus mapping should activate progressively with vault size, not ship as day-one ceremony" (info-flow L685-687, verdict adopt); hubs "emerge bottom-up at a felt 'mental squeeze point'" and the tool must "not pre-generate a hub taxonomy at import time" (L619-622, adapt). The owner's direction "every digested work connects to a hub" is exactly the import-time taxonomy those adopted verdicts reject, at a corpus scale (~10 imports/week, design §7 L626) that will not reach the squeeze point inside the beta window. Every documented alpha failure around hubs is a failure of hub maintenance — membership rot ("every relevant new note requires a hub edit") and curated-looking generated lists (design-history L2078) — never of hub absence, and researcher-authored MOC-style notes remain writable as freehand files today. Finally, the alpha.15 hub form depends on the owned ID-backed controlled-vocabulary tag, a substrate beta.1 also dropped (S3.7); restoring that form drags in a dependency chain the charter never asks for.

**Decision:** The citation audit already established the drop is silent; the live question is RECORD vs CHANGE. Three findings push past RECORD. (1) Process debt inside the design itself: §17 claims all info-flow divergences "were resolved... and folded into the body," but three hub-layer adopt verdicts (L614/L625/L689) are unresolved — a §11 divergence line would leave §17's completeness claim false; only a resolution (adopt-in-some-form or reasoned reject) repairs it. (2) Corpus self-contradiction: docs-history Borrow #42 targets beta1 with a starter hub set for the sample corpus (itself justified by the cold-start abandonment window the retention experiment measures), which cannot ship in a no-hub design; either hub exists or that recorded borrow must be explicitly overturned. (3) The concept is separable from the machinery: the research's size-gating verdicts gate hub tooling (suggestion, staleness detectors, per-hub diagnostics), not the concept's existence, and the research-adopted candidates-section mechanism (L689: machine suggestions appended in a clearly-marked section the human promotes from; L627) answers the documented membership-rot failure without the controlled-vocab substrate — so a minimal hub (one enum value, one folder, one flow affordance) restores coherence at near-zero machinery cost. But the owner's full direction does not survive the same corpus test: mandating every digest connect to a hub contradicts the adopted bottom-up-emergence and no-import-time-taxonomy verdicts, and no charter bar or documented failure supports it. Verdict: partial — hub returns as a first-class, researcher-created editorial concept (upheld; entries flip to CHANGE), the digest->hub link returns as a candidates affordance rather than a hard flow terminus (R-5's mandate not upheld as stated), and hub tooling stays post-beta.1, size-gated, per the research beta.1 itself adopted.

**History:** The design history (scratch/design-history/memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md) shows: (a) continuous descent — Old Skeleton gated hubs/ (L90, L115, L132 with prescribed body sections at L224), moc in the original 16-type set (L268), renamed hub at ADR-50 keeping ADR-19's threshold-alert mechanism (L148-149); (b) agent-proposed hubs shipped at alpha.5 with hub writes explicitly forbidden to agents because "the annotation IS the curation that defines the type, and that is the human's" (L993) — the editorial-ownership rule beta.1's research independently re-derived; (c) alpha.11's clean-slate reset kept hub as one of three knowledge node-kinds — digest (machine) / note (human) / hub (both) — defining digest as "what hubs draw from" and hub as "the merged Karpathy concept-page x ZK MOC" and the project entry point (L1635, L1637, L2284): the strongest historical support for the owner's wiki<->ZK bridge framing; (d) alpha.15's ADR-126 kept hub among four types while deleting nine schemas, redesigning it around an owned ID-backed controlled-vocabulary tag to fix documented membership rot and ADR-19's "generated list that looks curated but isn't" hazard (L2078) — both failures of hub maintenance, not hub absence; (e) no documented failure of hub absence exists anywhere in the history, because absence never existed before beta.1. Corpus cross-checks: beta.1 design mentions hubs exactly once, the §7 L623 parenthetical (grep-verified); §17's seven resolutions omit the hub verdicts; docs-history line 42 carries the beta1-targeted starter-hub-set borrow and line 49 the hub-due/hub-staleness detectors; the regression review's "hub/tag graph recorded" sweep claim (L79) was already shown false by the audit.

**Entry amendments:**
- S2.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → CHANGE (hub sub-delta only) — Restore hubs/ to the §3 layout per the design change; the project multi-file split and per-work digest.md sub-deltas stand as recorded (docs-history Adapt #77/#78/#88/#97, Borrow #59) and need no further action.
- S3.2: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → CHANGE — Add hub to the §3 type enum as a researcher-created editorial concept with the machine-candidates contract, and add a §17 item resolving the info-flow hub-layer verdicts (adopt concept minimal-form, defer tooling size-gated) instead of the currently-proposed §11 divergence line.
- S10.2: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → CHANGE (concept half; navigation half stays continuity) — The concept-drop half is repaired by the S3.2 design change (which also lands docs-history Borrow #42's starter hub set); the navigation half remains continuity — no hub navigation surface ships in beta.1, matching every alpha release.

**Design change (if adopted):** In design §3: add hubs/ to the Memoria/ layout block (L196-218) and hub to the class enum (L266-267), with one paragraph after the frontmatter contract: "A hub is a researcher-created curated structure note (type: hub, human-class): a curated link list over works and notes with human-owned ordering and prose. Machine contribution is confined to a clearly-marked, run-attributed Candidates block appended by VaultWriter (mem-run marked, revertible; it never reorders or rewrites the curated body — human spans stay manifest-protected). Hubs are never machine-created and never pre-generated at import; hub-suggestion, staleness, and per-hub diagnostics are post-beta.1, activating progressively with vault size (info-flow L619/L687)." In §7 (L622-624): replace the parenthetical — after digest, new works snap to existing hubs by entity/embedding similarity and are appended to those hubs' Candidates blocks (info-flow L498-501/L627); creating a new hub stays a human act; mapping views remain post-beta.1 consumers. In §17: add item 8 recording the resolution: hub-layer adopt verdicts (organizing layer, editorial curation, candidates-promotion) adopted in this minimal form; the tooling verdicts deferred size-gated; "every digest connects to a hub" declined as import-time taxonomy the adopted research rejects. In the sample-corpus plan: docs-history Borrow #42's starter hub set ships as example hub files (example-not-default).

**Open questions (owner):** 1) Is digest->hub connection a hard invariant (R-5's flow terminus, "every digested work connects to a hub") or an affordance? The design's own adopted research (info-flow L619-622, L685-687) says affordance; making it mandatory means the owner overruling those adopted verdicts explicitly. 2) Does beta.1 hub membership need the controlled-vocabulary tag substrate (alpha.15's ADR-126 form), which couples this restoration to the R-13/S3.7 re-examination — or does the curated-list + machine-candidates form suffice for beta.1 scale? 3) Mixed-authorship hub files (a machine-appended Candidates block inside a human-class file) vs a paired report-class candidates projection: which fits beta.1's file-granular mem-* provenance model (absence-of-markers = human)? This interacts with R-3 (quarantine-on-change) and R-12 (only draft is freehand). 4) If the owner holds that retention itself depends on the organizing layer (not just design coherence), that is a charter under-scope claim — the charter currently has no organizing-layer row, and only the owner can amend the spec.

**Skeptic corrections:** 1) Finding (2) overstates: docs-history Borrow #42's "worked-example starter hub set marked example-not-default" CAN land in a no-hub design as freehand/scaffolded example notes — adjudication/S10.md's verifier notes (L23) already record that realization — so the borrow forces explicit disposition, not the hub type; the verdict should rest it on "must be disposed, and adopt-minimal also lands it," not "cannot ship." 2) Finding (1) under-cites the strongest evidence: the §17 breach is direct, not inferential — the information-flow design (the stance design §17 claims fully resolved) carries hubs/<topic>.md in its vault layout (L56), the editorial-hub law with human-approved cold-start hub stubs (L172), "hub candidate sections" in its machine-write law (L221), and hubs in its keep-test audit (L223), none disposed by §17's seven items; cite these. 3) The claim that the research "gates hub tooling, not the concept's existence" misreads info-flow L684-687 — its evidence is that structure notes themselves appeared at ~1,000-1,500 notes ("sub-1,000-note vaults need almost no structural tooling"), so a reasoned-reject §17 item was equally available; argue adopt-minimal as the better choice (owner prior + stance-design hub layer + four-reset history), not as the only repair. 4) Add the missed charter anchor for the mandate-declined half: requirements L29 Capture row ("no mandatory per-item decisions") makes a hard per-import digest→hub terminus a charter violation unless machine-created, which history L993, research L689, and info-flow-design L172 all forbid. 5) Open question 3 is already answered by design §4 L295-296 ("frontmatter file-default plus trailing block markers"): a mem-run-marked machine Candidates block inside a human-class hub file fits beta.1's existing provenance model — drop or narrow that open question.

### R-3 — Authorship-blind change reaction: quarantine then verify; graph-integrity verification

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The alpha line ran an unbroken, authorship-blind change-detection lineage from its first release: alpha.1's vault-hash-drift walked the audit log and flagged any file whose on-disk SHA-256 diverged — "a legitimate human edit in Obsidian surfaces here too, by design" (design-history L487); alpha.14's workspace scan recorded observed_external_edit events, demoted foreign-edited keep-set Concepts to unchecked (re-promoted only via mark-checked, a human act), and quarantined worker-owned paths (L1954); ADR-127 universalized it — every mutation, regardless of origin, non-consumable until a verification pass dispositions it, covering all tracked paths (L2122). The verification was indeed structural/graph integrity, never semantic: the shared suite was integrity-link-target-check, integrity-quote-anchor-check, evidence-resolves and citekey-resolution checks (L1657, L196), the history explicitly records structural checks as blind to crafted injection and unwarranted claims (L1725, L1735), and the borrow doc concedes "the mechanical slice (anchors resolve, links well-formed) is already quarantine-and-verify's job" (borrow/adapt/reject L118). Beta.1 is the first version with no out-of-band change witness at all: an agent or sync process editing human-class text is silently trusted as human, deletion of a researcher-set `superseded: true` silently re-admits a retracted work into Ask and past the export refusal (the fail-open direction, un-witnessed — design §4 L339-353), and the charter's hardest bar ("machines never overwrite or delete human-authored text; a violation stops the beta immediately," requirements L72) has neither enforcement nor detection for non-VaultWriter writers such as the researcher's own file-tooled agent. The detection infrastructure is already paid for: the manifest human_hash is "recomputable from the file alone" (design §4 L354-357) and every run's pre-tag commit-all materializes the out-of-band diff in plain git (§6 L460-462, L477-479).

**For beta.1:** Beta.1 did not drop quarantine-then-verify; it kept it where machines write and where machine verdicts are consumed: engine writes are staged then verified by the pre==post human-span manifest gate with auto-rollback (§6 steps 2-3), any edit under an `mc` marker fail-closes to amber and re-checks (§4 L325-338), rebuild demotes every verdict and re-earns it via the $0 local Checker, and export refuses on unresolved/superseded/unwarranted citations (§8 L828-836) — the regression sweep verified "quarantine-and-verify realized as staging + the human-span manifest gate" among 151 held invariants (regression review L62-68). The maximal reading — quarantine human-authored changes until verified — contradicts the alpha record itself: ADR-127's propagation kept PI-authored descendants live ("never auto-destroy human work," history L2126), the docs-history adapt row mandates "automated propagation may never demote/quarantine human-authored derived content — flag-and-route only" (borrow doc L85), and refuse-to-serve only ever guarded machine consumption under a stale checked hash (L2124), which beta.1's amber demotion reproduces fail-closed. The alpha scan's guarded objects largely do not exist in beta.1's substrate (no consumed references.bib, no overrides.jsonl, human notes not embedded — S05.md L36), prompts carry quotes/citekeys/sections only so foreign-edited notes structurally never reach a model (§8 L806-807), and the borrow doc records an explicit reject of foreign-commit policing as "detect-and-apologize" superseded by "VaultWriter+ledger+manifest (enforce, don't detect-and-apologize)" (L125). The charter requires none of this beyond what beta.1 has, and sync-conflict handling is a Deliberate Exclusion (requirements L87).

**Decision:** The decision splits on detection versus quarantine. (1) Detection is upheld: beta.1 has named residual holes with fail-open direction — no witness for out-of-band edits to human text, so the stop-the-beta human-text bar is undetectable for non-VaultWriter writers (exactly the "agent edits a human block = silently trusted as human" case), and no witness for removal of researcher-set restriction frontmatter (`superseded`), whose forging direction was adjudicated fail-safe (S04.md S4.4) but whose removal direction silently relaxes Ask exclusion and export refusal. Both were covered continuously from alpha.1 (vault-hash-drift) through alpha.15 (workspace scan / ADR-127) by authorship-blind hash detection, and beta.1's drop of the scan half is what S5.4's RECORD verdict papered over as merely unrecorded. The cost of restoration is near zero: the manifest hash is file-recomputable by design and the git pre-tag sweep already captures the out-of-band diff. (2) Verification-as-graph-integrity is upheld: the owner's characterization matches the alpha structural suite exactly, and beta.1 currently runs those checks only at export and Ask, so link/anchor/citekey rot between consumption points has no home; folding it into §5's periodic reconciliation pass is a small doctrine-consistent extension (flags, never blocks). (3) Quarantine/refuse-to-serve for human or foreign edits is rejected: the alpha line was authorship-blind in detection but deliberately authorship-asymmetric in reaction — human-authored content was flag-and-route only, never withheld (history L2126; borrow doc L85) — and refuse-to-serve guarded only stale machine verdicts at machine consumption, which beta.1's marker+hash+checks fail-closed amber plus the export gate reproduce. Restoring universal withhold-until-verified would overrule a documented alpha lesson with no documented failure justifying it. Also decisive: ADR-127 was a designed belt for ADR-128's no-write-gate epistemics ("errors become detectable, attributable, and reversible instead of gated at creation," L2122) — so what beta.1 must preserve is that property; without the detection sweep, foreign changes to non-machine-block content are not detectable at all, breaking the property the alpha mechanism existed to deliver. Hence partial: S5.4 becomes CHANGE (detection sweep + graph-integrity verify, flag-and-route; non-restored halves recorded), S4.1's absence-of-markers rule stands as a detection/classification rule — the owner's own scope note concedes it "may stand" as detection — with its trust consequence mitigated by the new witness rather than by changing the rule.

**History:** All in scratch/design-history/memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md unless noted. (1) L487, L495: alpha.1 `vault-hash-drift` (CRITICAL detector) compared last recorded after_hash to on-disk SHA-256 — authorship-blind by design ("a legitimate human edit in Obsidian surfaces here too"); the detective backstop to imperfect prevention. (2) L1655/L1657: alpha.11 trace-integrity scan quarantined untraced/foreign commits; the structural detection suite was graph-integrity checks (integrity-link-target-check, integrity-quote-anchor-check, evidence/claim-quote, citekey sweeps; L196 frontmatter-link detector "checks every links: wikilink resolves"). (3) L1725/L1735: structural checks were explicitly blind to crafted injection and well-formed-but-unwarranted claims — alpha verification was never semantic; the semantic residual got a human checkpoint, not the suite. This confirms the owner's graph-integrity characterization. (4) L1954: alpha.14 workspace scan — observed_external_edit journal events; keep-set foreign edit imported as PI edit and demoted to unchecked (human re-promotion via mark-checked); worker-owned paths/references.bib quarantined, never re-consumed. (5) L2122/L2124/L2126: ADR-127 universal invariant (all origins, all tracked paths incl. overrides.jsonl); consumption guard = refuse+enqueue on hash mismatch vs the recorded checked hash (synchronous demote-on-read rejected); two-tier demotion kept PI-authored descendants live — the alpha reaction was authorship-ASYMMETRIC even though detection was blind. (6) Borrow/adapt/reject doc L85: adapt row "automated propagation may never demote/quarantine human-authored derived content — flag-and-route only." (7) Same doc L118: "the mechanical slice (anchors resolve, links well-formed) is already quarantine-and-verify's job." (8) Same doc L125: recorded REJECT of git-as-enforcement foreign-commit quarantine ("enforce, don't detect-and-apologize") — the philosophy under which beta.1 dropped scan-based detection, but enforcement cannot cover writers outside VaultWriter, where detection is the only option. (9) Negative finding: no documented alpha-era incident of a foreign edit causing harm — ADR-127 was a designed belt for ADR-128's epistemics (S05.md L39 concurs), so the obligation on beta.1 is the detectable/attributable/reversible property, not the mechanism form. (10) Beta.1 counter-evidence: design §6 L463-480 (staging + manifest gate + pathspec-limited commits), §4 L325-338 (fail-closed amber), §8 L828-836 (export refusal), §5 L414-427 (human notes not embedded; reconciliation pass is existence-level only, not hash-level); regression review L62-68 verified the family held.

**Entry amendments:**
- S5.4: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → CHANGE — partial restore (detection + graph-integrity verification, flag-and-route; refuse-to-serve and human-content quarantine deliberately not restored, recorded) — Extend §5's periodic reconciliation pass into an integrity sweep that detects any out-of-band change (manifest human_hash recompute + diff against the last run commit) and runs graph-integrity verification (links/anchors/citekeys resolve) on changed files, routing findings to Review as flags — and add the §18-style record of what stays dropped.
- S4.1: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — unchanged — Absence-of-mem-* stands as the classification/detection rule (the owner's scope note concedes this); its trust-asymmetry consequence — foreign edits inheriting human trust invisibly — is mitigated by the S5.4 detection sweep rather than by changing the rule.
