**Design change (if adopted):** In design §5, extend the periodic-reconciliation paragraph (L418-427) into an integrity sweep with two added duties: (a) foreign-change detection — recompute each manifest path's human_hash against the manifest of record and diff the vault against the last run's commit (the pre-tag sweep already materializes out-of-band changes); any out-of-band change to a Memoria/ file, author unknown by construction, surfaces as an observed-external-edit Review item at notice loudness, with changes to researcher-set restriction keys (`superseded`, `local-only`) named explicitly because their removal direction fails open; machine-block edits already demote to amber via marker/current-hash/checks disagreement (§4) and need no new mechanism; (b) graph-integrity verification — on changed files at detection time and across the bundle once per sweep, verify wikilinks resolve, block-ID anchors exist, and citekey references resolve in `works`; findings flag into Review, never block (the export gate remains the only refusal point). Feed the sweep's result into the inspector pane's existing "integrity verdict" line (§1 L100). Then add one §18-style recorded decision (merging the S5.4 RECORD text the machine adjudication drafted): beta.1 deliberately does not restore read-path refuse-to-serve or quarantine of human-authored/foreign content — flag-and-route only, per the alpha propagation lesson (ADR-127 two-tier demotion; docs-history authorship-asymmetry row) — and the alpha scan's objects (a hand-consumed references.bib, overrides.jsonl, human notes in the retrieval substrate) do not exist in beta.1.

**Open questions (owner):** 1. The scope caveat already recorded in the rulings file: whether R-3 also constrains the NLI Checker's role on machine-generated digests (semantic verification) — owner-only. 2. Whether "quarantine" is meant as withhold-from-service even for human-authored changes: the corpus (ADR-127 kept PI-authored descendants live; borrow-doc L85 mandates flag-and-route for human-authored content) shows the alpha line itself never withheld human content — only the owner can overrule that documented lesson, and this verdict assumes he does not. 3. Charter interplay: foreign-edit detection partially covers sync-mangled files, brushing the "Concurrent multi-device writes" Deliberate Exclusion (requirements L87) — is detect-and-report in scope while conflict *handling* stays excluded? If the owner intends full foreign-edit coverage as a trust requirement, the charter under-scopes (no Trust row demands an out-of-band change witness) and needs a one-row amendment. 4. R-8 interplay: absence-of-markers=human was rationalized by zero-migration; if the vault is Memoria-born (R-8), S4.1's recorded rationale needs re-derivation even though the rule itself survives (humans still edit markerlessly in stock Obsidian).

**Skeptic corrections:** Three fixes, none verdict-changing. (1) Re-ground reasoning point (3): history L2126 and borrow-doc L85 are propagation-tier evidence (PI-authored *descendants* stay live); the alpha direct-edit reaction was authorship-blind non-consumability (L1954 "direct edit to a checked keep-set Concept is marked unchecked/non-consumable"; L2122 "regardless of origin"). The rejection of restored quarantine should instead rest on beta.1's fail-closed consumption points, citing design L770-771 (verbatim quote asserted byte-substring of the anchored block, fail ⇒ drop + re-index — the beta.1 analog of ADR-127's refuse+enqueue for the retrieval substrate) and L757-758 (incremental re-chunk diffed by sha256 on every capture commit), which the argument_against never cited and which close the strongest owner-side counter (that the chunk substrate lacks alpha's consumption guard). (2) Add missed evidence for the S5.4 CHANGE: design §10 L923-929 claims "the human-span manifest gate remains the structural backstop" for third-party-plugin between-run rewrites, but §6 step 3 compares human_hash only pre/post around Memoria's own writes — the design leans on a backstop that does not cover the claimed class; the design_change should also amend that §10 sentence so the new sweep is named as the actual backstop, not just feed the inspector line. (3) Tighten open question 2's wording: alpha never withheld human content from human-facing service, but it did withhold directly-edited items from machine consumption until the scan dispositioned them — beta.1 reproduces that guard at its consumption points, so the question is narrower than stated.

### R-4+R-9 — Catalog records/entities are SQLite; bibliography.bib is the survival artifact, never local-only

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The alpha line's mature doctrine was "files own meaning, the DB owns records" (ADR-124/126, gap report S2 row, L31), and record.md is a machine record dressed as a markdown file — kin to the machine-materialized-state pattern beta.1 itself calls "a standing reject with three documented generations of decay" (design §5 L418-421). Everything genuinely relational in the catalog — entities, mentions, citation edges, annotations — already lives DB-side in beta.1's own schema (§5 L397-404; §7 L615-631; §17.5), which validates the owner's "relational by nature" intuition. The charter's Survival claim names the .bib's form as the survival floor ("plain markdown plus standard bibliography files", charter L22-23), so a reading where the catalog's survivor IS the bibliography file is charter-compatible; and for Zotero-sourced works the researcher's Zotero library independently preserves full fidelity, making per-work CSL-JSON copies look redundant. R-9's operational demand is genuinely unmet in the text: no design sentence exempts bibliography.bib from local-only, while beta.1 does make the *other*, same-named artifact — the per-export references.bib — local-only by inheritance from draft.md (§8 L840-841), so an unrecorded guarantee invites exactly the conflation the owner fears. One recorded sentence closes it.

**For beta.1:** The .bib alone cannot carry re-import fidelity, on alpha's own record: "references.bib is portable but lossy relative to the catalog DB; this is accepted for alpha.12 simplicity" (history L1802), and the Zotero re-import key rides csl_json.custom.zotero_key (design §7 L557-558), which has no standard BibTeX home — a nonstandard field is dropped by precisely the standard tools Success Claim 4 is about. DB-authoritative catalog + exported survivor is the shape whose failure alpha documented: the catalog-recovery spike FAILED ("Periodic export loses Memoria-owned catalog changes made after the last export", L1802), forcing same-commit bibliography atomicity as a patch; beta.1 removes that failure structurally because each record is itself a keep-test file, so catalog survival no longer depends on export freshness or backup horizon. Every reason ADR-122/124 gave for SQLite — worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates, projections (L1896, L2042) — stays DB-side in beta.1 (§5), so the delta re-opens no earned position; and non-Zotero works (DOI/arXiv, BibTeX-file, repo — required Capture inputs, charter L29) have no Zotero fallback, so their fidelity and the researcher's metadata corrections need a file home or die with the DB, violating §5's own rule that no researcher judgment lives only in the DB (L441-443). R-1 strengthens, not weakens, this: a stable work_id decoupled from citekey must survive DB loss to keep identity stable, and record.md is the only file-side carrier available. Alpha itself already denormalized a citation survival copy into keep-set files after the cross-store spike FAIL ("the embedded Citation is the survival copy", L1776); full CSL-JSON expands that earned position rather than reversing it.

**Decision:** Both briefing tests resolve against the position's core. (1) Can the .bib alone carry re-import fidelity? No — the lossiness finding is the alpha line's own accepted record (history L1802), CSL-JSON is the native ≥95%-fidelity format from the Zotero API (design §7 L554-556), and the idempotent-upsert key (custom.zotero_key) has no durable BibTeX representation; making the .bib the catalog's source also reintroduces the rejected BBT-.bib-as-interface shape ("a second source of truth with built-in staleness", docs-history Reject #123). (2) Does R-1 change the equation? Yes, in beta.1's favor: a stable work_id must survive total DB loss or rebuild severs identity, links, and anchors — the file-side record is the natural carrier, so R-1 makes record.md more load-bearing, not less. (3) The relational half of R-4 is not a delta at all: beta.1 keeps entities, mentions, edges, and all operational state DB-side (§5, §7 L615-631, §17.5, docs-history L111); a per-work CSL-JSON document is a document, stored as a JSON blob even in the works row (§5 L374) — materializing it in a fenced block changes nothing relational. (4) The authority direction matters only on conflict, and file-wins is what the charter's Rebuild row ("derived state is regenerable from canonical files", L63) and §5's two-DB-class split presuppose; DB-wins re-creates the alpha.12 spike failure class. (5) R-9's actionable content is upheld: today nothing makes bibliography.bib local-only (it is a non-markdown file at the bundle root, outside local-only/, with no frontmatter to flag, and local-only is prompt-egress-only per §3 L280/§10 L942-944 — never a sync or survival exclusion), but the guarantee is recorded nowhere, and the per-export references.bib IS local-only by inheritance (§8 L840-841), so the distinguishing sentence in S2.5's RECORD action (verifier-corrected wording, which already cites R-9 verbatim) is the right and sufficient fix. Net: no governed entry flips to CHANGE; the owner position lands as one recorded design sentence (R-9) plus confirmation that beta.1 already embodies R-4's relational claim.

**History:** Design history (memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md): L1800 — alpha.12 keep-test flip: the *relational catalog graph* was judged working state failing the survival test and moved to SQLite, while the source concept file survived; L1802 — references.bib flipped to SQLite-first rendering AND became same-commit atomic because the catalog-recovery spike FAILED ("Periodic export loses Memoria-owned catalog changes made after the last export"), with the .bib explicitly accepted as "portable but lossy relative to the catalog DB … for alpha.12 simplicity" — the single most decisive artifact against .bib-as-sole-survivor; L1776 — the cross-store spike FAIL forced denormalizing a compact citation survival copy INTO keep-set files ("source_id is the live handle; the embedded Citation is the survival copy") — i.e., the alpha line itself established file-side catalog survival copies, which beta.1's full-CSL-JSON record.md expands; L1896 — ADR-122 rejected promoting SQLite to canonical Concept store as "opaque to Obsidian/Git" and kept the DB behind the checked-Concept boundary; L2042 — ADR-124 rejected a frontmatter-only catalog because alpha.14 needed durable worker state, provider payload provenance, full-text gates, and projections in SQLite — all of which remain DB-side in beta.1 (§5 L359-444). Entities: alpha.14 removed markdown entity Concepts and docs-history L111 records the sprawl reject — beta.1 continues it (§7 L615-631). The alpha "local-only" (ADR-63) was a deployment-topology homonym, so R-9's egress-exemption demand has no alpha precedent to honor — it is a new, previously silent constraint.

**Entry amendments:**
- S2.2: LEAVE → LEAVE — Uphold the machine adjudication: record.md-as-fidelity-carrier stands on alpha's own lossiness record (history L1802) and the file-side survival needs of the zotero_key and (post-R-1) work_id; note in the final report that R-4's authority inversion was tested and rejected on that evidence.
- S7.1: LEAVE → LEAVE — Uphold: the delta is a re-scoping, not a reversal — every ADR-122/124 reason for SQLite stays DB-side (§5), and only fidelity plus the re-import key move to the keep-test file; R-4's direction would re-open the documented alpha.12 catalog-recovery failure.
- S2.5: RECORD → RECORD — Keep RECORD with the verifier-corrected text — this is the upheld fragment of the owner position: it states bibliography.bib is a keep-test survival artifact never subject to any local-only mechanism (R-9 verbatim) and distinguishes it from the per-export references.bib, which is local-only by inheritance (§8 L840-841).
- S7.6: RECORD → RECORD — Keep RECORD: the entities half already embodies R-4's relational claim (docs-history L111, §7 L615-631, §17.5); the unrecorded catalog/-tree-drop half still needs the §11 divergence sentence the machine adjudication directed.

**Design change (if adopted):** Adopt S2.5's verifier-corrected recording into design §3, directly under the layout block (or as a §11 converges clause): "references.bib continues as Memoria/bibliography.bib — a rename only: still the generated, complete keep-test bibliography takeout. The alpha.12 same-commit atomicity rule's earned reason (catalog changes lost after the last export) no longer applies: catalog records are themselves keep-test files, so the .bib is regenerable and its freshness is not survival-critical. bibliography.bib is a keep-test survival artifact and is never subject to any local-only mechanism — frontmatter flag, local-only/ residence, or marked ancestor (owner ruling R-9). The per-project export/references.bib (cited works only, emitted at export time, local-only inherited from draft.md) is a second, export-scoped artifact serving the charter's Compose bar, not a replacement." No other design change: R-4's relational claim is already beta.1's recorded position, and its authority inversion is rejected.

**Open questions (owner):** (1) Charter reading: does the owner hold that Success Claim 4's "standard bibliography files" was meant to name the .bib as the catalog's ONLY intended survivor (which would make record.md over-scope), or as a floor? The corpus supports the floor reading (Rebuild row L63 requires regenerability from canonical files), but only the owner can say what the charter intended — if the former, the charter itself should be amended rather than the design argued around it. (2) If R-1's stable work_id lands, should it ride record.md (frontmatter or the CSL fence) so identity survives total DB loss? The analysis says it must live file-side somewhere; the exact home is the owner's call. (3) Was R-9's "never local-only" meant to cover only Memoria/bibliography.bib, or also the per-export references.bib — which beta.1 deliberately makes local-only by inheritance from draft.md (§8 L840-841)? If the latter, that is a real CHANGE to §8, not just a recording.

**Skeptic corrections:** Three supporting-argument fixes, none changing the verdict or amendments: (1) Soften "DB-authoritative catalog + exported survivor is the shape whose failure alpha documented" — history L1802's documented FAIL was the periodic-export variant only; same-commit atomicity was the earned fix and the fixed shape was stable alpha.12→15 (gap report §2 L30 records the keep-test as HOLDING), so R-4 inherits the fix rather than re-opening the failure; rest the rejection on the independent legs (lossiness accepted-on-record, zotero_key's lack of a durable BibTeX home, non-Zotero fidelity, R-1). (2) Drop or reword the Reject #123 analogy ("making the .bib the catalog's source reintroduces the rejected BBT-.bib-as-interface shape") — docs-history L123 rejects the BBT auto-export .bib (Zotero-owned, staleness/sync races), a mechanism that does not map to a Memoria-generated .bib. (3) Weaken "record.md is the only file-side carrier available" for a stable work_id to "the natural file-side carrier" — fulltext.md/digest.md frontmatter are also file-side homes; the substantive point (R-4's direction deletes the natural home) holds. Additionally, the final report should note that the alpha.12 keep-test doctrine ("everything else is free to be SQLite", history alpha.12 theme) is permissive, not mandatory — the strongest owner-side text — and therefore does not forbid beta.1's file-canonical records; stating this preempts the best remaining counter.

### R-5+R-10 — The basic flow: work -> catalog -> extract -> digest(=wiki) -> hub, 1:1 work:digest

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The flow's terminus is Memoria's founding premise, and beta.1 amputates it: the genesis is Karpathy's LLM-wiki — an agent that "compiles raw sources into a persistent, interlinked markdown wiki ... instead of retrieving from scratch each query" (history L23) — and beta.1's Ask over raw fulltext chunks with "digests are enrichment, not the search surface" (design §11 L977-978) is precisely retrieve-from-scratch, with digest.md restored as isolated, uninterlinked pages. The alpha line consistently defined digest as "the reading unit, and what hubs draw from" (history L1635) and made the digest→hub compounding step "core — the Co-PI differentiator, not deferrable" (L1679); hub survived every consolidation including alpha.15's nine-schema cut, each time with a re-derived mechanism fixing its documented failures (ADR-50 L148-149; hub_handoff.py shipped at alpha.5, L993; owned checked vocab-tag at ADR-126, L2078), and "compounding-wiki value" was one of two carried-forward bets the alpha.12 release gate instrumented (L1810). Beta.1's own commissioned info-flow research returned verdict adopt on "structure notes/hub pages as the organizing layer" (info-flow L614-615), adopt on machine tags resolving to hub pages (L624-627), and adapt on Karpathy digest+hub maintenance (L664-667) — and the design ships none of it, with the only design-body trace a parenthetical ("hubs and mapping views are post-beta.1 consumers", §7 L623) that the S2.3 adjudication itself found is not an adjudication. Beta.1's corpus-organizing terminus is therefore effectively nothing: navigation-only index.md projections (§3 L242-246), human wikilinks in notes/, and a DB-side backlink table (§5 L380) — a retention experiment on a system whose central differentiating bet is structurally absent.

**For beta.1:** The charter is the spec and it contains the flow beta.1 built: the Capture row requires "catalog, full text, and optional digest" — digest explicitly optional — and no required row names a hub, topic layer, or organizing terminus; the beta is "a retention experiment ... not a feature milestone" (requirements L9-10, L29). The alpha line's own final canonical minimum loop ended at digest, not hub — "work add → work enrich → work interview → work digest" (gap report L118) — a hub navigation surface never shipped in any alpha (gap report L124), and the ADR-30 audit found the tag-suggestion layer the ADR called "the system's value" was never built (history L1368), so hub-as-flow-terminus is lineage and aspiration, not exercised, failure-earned machinery. The documented hub failures run the other way: hand-curated membership "rots (every relevant new note requires a hub edit)" and generated lists "look curated but aren't" (ADR-126/ADR-19, history L2078), and beta.1's own adopted research says hubs are sparse, emerge bottom-up at ~1,000-1,500-note squeeze points, creation "stays a human act," and "do not pre-generate a hub taxonomy at import time" (info-flow L619-627) — all of which contradicts "every digested work connects to a hub" as an ingest stage. Opt-in digest is charter-conformant and flow-compatible: the wizard's single "Digest N works: est. $X" batch confirm keeps digest one flow action with no per-item decisions, and `indexed` as the $0 payoff state is what dissolved the alpha failure where one dead precondition blocked a work (S9.3). Restoring the terminus also drags in substrate beta.1 deliberately dropped (hub type — R-2; vocabulary — R-13), which are separately owned re-examinations.

**Decision:** Three questions decide this. (1) Does beta.1 have any corpus-organizing terminus? No — verified against the design: the lifecycle ends at `digested` (§7 L514-522), the only hub mention is a deferral parenthetical (L623), index projections are "navigation-only and meaning-only" (§3 L246), reports/ are never indexed, and the DB links table is a mechanical backlink graph; digests are explicitly "enrichment, not the search surface" (§11). The owner's core factual claim verifies. (2) Is that defect a silent one? Partly no longer — S2.3 already establishes the hub drop is unrecorded and proposes the §18 record — but the flow-terminus question is more than a recording gap: beta.1's own research adopted hub pages as the organizing layer and the design silently declined the adopt verdict (the gap report names this conflict at L39), and the beta will test a product whose carried value bet (compounding wiki, history L1810) cannot compound. That earns a concrete, minimal design change, not just a record. (3) Is the owner's full direction right? Not in its strong form: "every digested work connects to a hub" as an ingest stage is contradicted by the corpus the owner's own rules make decisive — the membership-rot failure record, the sparse/bottom-up/human-created hub evidence, and beta.1's standing-queue abandonment arithmetic (§7 L625-628) — and the alpha.15 solution (hub owns a checked tag; membership is a query, never a per-work hub edit) is the earned shape any restoration must take, which depends on R-2 (hub type) and R-13 (vocabulary substrate), separately owned. Meanwhile work→catalog→extract→digest exists 1:1 (owner concedes via R-10), and digest opt-in is compatible with digest as a structural stage because the charter itself makes digest optional, the confirm is batch-level not per-item, and no downstream stage hard-depends on it. Verdict: partial — uphold the missing-terminus finding and convert S2.3's flow half to CHANGE with the minimal interlinking mechanism buildable on existing substrate (edges table, machine-class digest.md, plain wikilinks), while binding hub pages themselves to R-2 and rejecting the per-work-connection stage and any change to digest opt-in.

**History:** The flow the owner names existed and evolved across the alpha line. Genesis: Karpathy LLM-wiki × Razlogova — compile into a persistent interlinked wiki, not retrieve-from-scratch (design-history L23); Zettelkasten/Memex principles recorded from alpha.1: "a claim with no `links:` ... cannot compound" (L225), "a claim note with no incoming links ... may as well not exist" (L278). Alpha.11 materialized the full chain: ingest spine "capture → conversation → digest+hub compounding → notes" as operation Concepts, with compile-source-digest implementing the compounding step ("compile the per-source digest, then compound hub updates"), labeled "core — the Co-PI differentiator, not deferrable" (L1679); digest defined 1:1 per source as "the reading unit, and what hubs draw from" (L1635); hub as "the merged Karpathy concept-page × ZK MOC" (L1637). Hub machinery that actually shipped: ADR-19 tier-2 hub-threshold Mapper handoff (hub_handoff.py, alpha.5, L993). Alpha.15's four-type cut deleted nine schemas but kept hub, giving it one owned checked controlled-vocab tag precisely to fix documented membership rot ("every relevant new note requires a hub edit") and ADR-19's "generated list that looks curated but isn't" hazard (L2074-2078) — i.e., the earned lesson is mechanical membership via tags, never per-work hub edits. Countervailing findings: the alpha.15 canonical minimum loop ended at digest, no hub step (gap report L118); no hub navigation surface ever shipped (gap report L124); the ADR-30 tag-suggestion layer was never built (L1368); "compounding-wiki value" was a carried bet, instrumented but never validated (L1810). Beta.1-side: design §7 L514-522 lifecycle ends at digested; §7 L623 sole hub mention (deferral parenthetical); §11 L977-978 demotes digests to "enrichment, not the search surface"; info-flow research verdicts adopt/adapt hubs as the organizing layer with sparse bottom-up human creation and no import-time taxonomy (L612-627, L664-667) plus co-citation counting primitives "emitting ranked lists per hub/cluster" (L324); the charter Capture row makes digest optional and no charter row names an organizing layer.

**Entry amendments:**
- S2.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → CHANGE — needs design change (scoped to the hub-drop/flow-terminus sub-delta; the project-split and digest-restore sub-deltas stay recorded borrows) — Keep the proposed §18 item-7 record, and additionally amend design §7 to decide the flow's terminus: a deterministic, capped, machine-maintained Related-works interlinking section on digest.md (per the design_change field), replacing the L623 parenthetical with an explicit recorded decision that binds hub pages themselves to the R-2 re-examination.
- S9.5: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — deliberate and recorded (unchanged) — The lifecycle state machine is not the defect — connection to the corpus is a graph property, not a pipeline status (per the alpha line's own 'standing is a property, not a location' lesson), so no connected status is added and the entry stands.

**Design change (if adopted):** In design.md §7: (1) in the work-lifecycle paragraph (L514-522), add one sentence after the digested state: "Digestion is not the flow's end: a digested work is joined to the corpus in the vault, not only in the DB (see Corpus connection below)." (2) After the DigestEngine block (after L682), add a short "Corpus connection (the flow's terminus)" paragraph: when a digest run completes (and regenerated on work-page attention thereafter), VaultWriter appends a deterministic machine section to digest.md — "Related works (generated)" — the top-k neighbors by shared outgoing references / co-citation counting over the existing edges table (§5), rendered as plain wikilinks with visible arithmetic per line ("shares 12 references"), cap-stamped, k a logged shadow knob; never LLM-generated, never exhaustive (the info-flow record rejects auto-lists that rot), machine-class like the rest of digest.md. This makes digests an interlinked wiki layer using only existing substrate (edges table, VaultWriter, keep-test-survivable wikilinks) and is the substrate hub pages draw from. (3) Replace the §7 L623 parenthetical with: "hub pages and mapping views as the human-curated organizing layer are under owner re-examination (R-2); if restored they return in the earned alpha.15 shape — sparse, created by the researcher at machine-detected squeeze points (suggest when ≥N works/notes cluster on shared references or key terms), membership mechanical, never a per-work edit obligation, no import-time taxonomy." (4) Land S2.3's §18 item-7 record as already proposed.

**Open questions (owner):** 1. Charter scope: no charter row requires an organizing layer, and Deliberate Exclusions do not exclude one — the charter is silent, not decisive. If the owner intends "connected to a hub" as core basic-flow scope (R-5's ruling sentence), the charter needs an owner amendment (a row under Required Product Scope, or an extension of the Knowledge-format row); only the owner can decide whether the retention experiment must test the compounding-wiki bet or deliberately tests capture/ask/compose parity alone. 2. Shape of the restored connection, if R-2 restores hubs: the literal direction "every digested work connects to a hub" (R-2/R-5) is incompatible with the corpus evidence the owner's own rules make decisive (membership-rot failure record, sparse bottom-up hubs, standing-queue abandonment arithmetic); does the owner accept the alpha.15 mechanical-membership shape (hub owns a tag/query; connection is derived, not written per work) as satisfying the ruling? 3. Terminus attachment for undigested works: with digest opt-in (charter Capture row), a work that is never digested has no digest.md to carry the Related-works section — should the terminus also attach to record.md or the indexed state so undigested works still join the corpus, or is connection acceptable as a digest-stage benefit only?

**Skeptic corrections:** Two non-flipping fixes: (1) argument_for overstates that beta.1's Ask "is precisely retrieve-from-scratch" — beta.1 does compile persistent per-work digests (opt-in DigestEngine, §7 L648-682); the verified defect is that digests are uninterlinked across works and never enter the search surface (§11 L977-978), i.e., compiled-but-inert, not uncompiled. Soften that clause so the amendment does not rest on a contestable genesis framing. (2) The design_change should cite its own in-design precedent to preempt the ADR-19 "generated list that looks curated but isn't" objection: §7's snowball already lands a capped machine digest note with transparent occurrence counting and cap stamps (L727-739), and info-flow L627 explicitly endorses a "machine-maintained candidates section — not exhaustive auto-lists that rot" — naming both makes the Related-works section demonstrably the researched acceptable shape rather than new machinery. Optionally, open question 3 can note that R-10 itself locates the missing link at digest→hub, so attaching the terminus to digest.md (not record.md/indexed) already matches the owner's own clarification.

### R-6 — Every md file is an OKF Concept with per-type frontmatter AND body-section schema

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The owner is right that beta.1's contract surface is thinner than its own evidence base demands. (1) The class enum re-mixes layers ADR-126 deliberately separated: evidence/gaps/export/report/incident/conflict — machine projections and operational artifacts alpha.11 retired as "projections or worker state, not durable Concepts" (design-history L1629) and ADR-126 refused to make types ("a thing on a different layer is not a knowledge type," L2074) — sit as enum-peers of note/work/project, and no beta.1 record adjudicates that re-mixing (the gap report itself flags it, gap-report L38). (2) The per-class contract now lives only in scattered prose plus VaultWriter product code — the "contract scattered across hand-synced places" shape ADR-119 documented as having *already drifted* once (design-history L1439). (3) Two docs-history borrows the corpus targeted at beta1 are not visibly folded into the design: "One schema, three enforcement points" (borrow L39) and MASSW "fixed headings in digest.md (Key idea / Method / Outcome)" (borrow L97) — the design defines the digest JSON kinds (§7 L652-654) but never the rendered digest.md body. (4) Human-class files that machine consumers must parse are contract-free: the §8 export gate refuses on "a mapped project claim with no mc anchor and no gap marker" (L833-835), yet nothing defines how a claim is delimited in project.md — a consumer specified against an undefined contract. Conformance-by-construction covers machine files; it says nothing about the files whose structure other mechanisms consume.

**For beta.1:** Restoring per-type schema files with strict validation re-opens the one documented failure in this cluster: the type roster "grew by accretion... each with folder homes, lifecycle fields, and per-type rules. The multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion" (ADR-126, design-history L2074, L2284-2286) — beta.1's answer (no schema surface to accrete into; VaultWriter serializes from typed fields; DigestEngine output schema-checked before staging, design §7 L659) addresses that failure structurally. The strict reject-undeclared validator was alpha.15-only and principle-driven, not failure-earned (S04.md L21), and its drop is recorded with rationale and a revisit trigger (§18(6) L1303-1312). Body-section *validation* has no alpha precedent to restore: bodies were template-prescribed only, and "the schemas, not the templates, are what validation runs against" (design-history L231). The OKF grounding is historically inverted: OKF mandates permissive consumption and prose-typed links — "the inverse of Memoria's thesis"; the alpha line's strictness was Memoria's own, adopted "at the boundary, never internally" (L2296-2298) — so "real OKF concepts" cannot ground strict per-type validation, and beta.1's strict-producer/permissive-consumer posture is exactly the alpha.11 OKF stance. The charter's Knowledge-format bar (requirements L36) requires typed frontmatter and OKF v0.1 bundle conformance, both met; validating human-class bodies would collide with "flags never block" (§3 L256-258) and the Trust row's machines-never-touch-human-text (requirements L72).

**Decision:** The decisive split is between contract-as-artifact and contract-as-validation. What the alpha line's per-type schemas demonstrably earned was catching drift between multiple encodings of one contract (form vs schema vs template, ADR-119; ADR-71's bypass argument) and enforcing invariants on human/agent-authored typed Concepts (the born-current thesis, claim required-fields). Neither failure has a substrate in beta.1: there are no forms or templates as second encodings, and there are no human-authored typed Concepts — claims/theses are alpha.16 scope with the argument graph, and human notes are deliberately freeform under zero-migration. Machine writes are covered by construction plus explicit pre-staging schema checks. So restoring schema files + strict validation would be machinery without a consumer, against a recorded accretion failure — that half of R-6 fails on the merits. But the owner's narrower formulation — "each file class should have a defined frontmatter + body-sections contract" — is currently unmet as a *stated* contract: the per-class shapes exist (record.md's fenced CSL-JSON, fulltext's ^pNNNN anchors, evidence.md's idempotent anchored blocks, gaps.md's denominator-first shape) but are scattered, the digest.md rendered body is never defined despite a beta1-targeted borrow demanding fixed headings, the enum's layer-mixing is unadjudicated, and the export gate consumes project.md structure ("mapped claims") that no contract defines. The minimal change is a normative per-class contract table — defined contracts, enforcement by construction, no schema files, no validator — which satisfies the defensible core of R-6 while preserving beta.1's earned structural answer to accretion. S4.2 stands (strictness was never the OKF-grounded part of the position); S4.3's RECORD stands and folds naturally into the same table.

**History:** Per-type schemas ran continuously from the pre-alpha.1 Old Skeleton: `.memoria/schemas/` was "THE single schema source" (design-history L104), 18 types at alpha.1 (L111), each schema declaring required/optional field maps, kinds, enums, literal pins — frontmatter only, with unknown extra fields ALLOWED ("the schema constrains, it does not enumerate," L158). Closure to reject-undeclared arrived only at alpha.15 PR-AC #1197 (L2090), completing ADR-119's principle, not answering an incident. Body sections were never schema-validated in any era: alpha.1 prescribed section bodies via templates with real epistemic rationale (note-body-structure, L222-225) but "Templates are scaffolding — the schemas, not the templates, are what validation runs against" (L231). What the schema layer demonstrably earned: ADR-71 — free-text capture leaked instructional text, no per-type required-field enforcement, unconstrained vocabularies; one schema driving form + Linter so layers can't diverge (L763-765); ADR-119 — the contract scattered across four hand-synced places had already drifted (source form added `summary`, dropped `links`, L1439); the born-current thesis that "validates clean" because enum-membership checking can't see history (L1073); alpha.14 #1157 universality because consumers "have no guaranteed field to read" otherwise (L1922). The counter-failure: type accretion — 25→12 at alpha.11 (operational types retired as "projections or worker state, not durable Concepts," L1629), 12+→4 at alpha.15 ("the multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion," ADR-126, L2074, L2284-2286). OKF: adopted boundary-only; permissive consumption and prose-typed links are "the inverse of Memoria's thesis"; "Memoria is deliberately ahead of OKF" (L1297, L2296-2298). Beta.1 corpus: borrow "One schema, three enforcement points" Target beta1 (borrow-adapt-reject L39) and MASSW "fixed headings in digest.md" Target beta1 (L97) — neither visible in the design body (no forms/Guard-validation mechanism; digest.md rendered layout undefined, only JSON kinds at design §7 L652-654); PICO/FINER-as-project.md-sections is Target alpha16 (L78).

**Entry amendments:**
- S3.1: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → CHANGE — needs design change (severity: low-medium) — Add a normative per-class contract table to design §3 (frontmatter keys + body-section shape + enforcement point per class value), define digest.md's rendered heading layout in §7 per the beta1-targeted MASSW borrow, and record the enum's knowledge-class vs projection/operational-class split so the ADR-126 layer distinction and its re-mixing are adjudicated — no per-type schema files, no strict validator.
- S4.2: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — deliberate and recorded — Stands: the strict-reject validator was alpha.15-only and principle-driven, its decline is recorded with a revisit trigger in §18(6), and the owner's own OKF grounding argues permissive consumption — strict-producer-by-construction plus permissive consumer is the alpha line's recorded OKF posture.
- S4.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — sound but unrecorded — Stands with the verifier's corrected text; the recording naturally lives beside or inside the new §3 per-class contract table so the field-set change reads as part of a defined contract rather than a bare divergence note.

**Design change (if adopted):** In design §3, immediately after the frontmatter YAML block (~L284): add a normative per-class contract table covering all 13 class-enum values — for each: required/optional frontmatter keys, body-section shape (work/record.md: work keys + fenced full CSL-JSON block; fulltext: linearized paragraphs each carrying `^pNNNN`; digest: fixed rendered headings Key idea / Method / Outcome / Limitations serialized from the §7 JSON with per-claim anchors; note: stamped type + optional anchor link, body human-free; evidence: one anchored block per pinned item, idempotent by `ev-` id; gaps: denominator-first regenerated report; project: question + outline sections with claim-bearing outline entries citing evidence spans (the structure the §8 export gate's mapped-claim refusal parses); draft/ruled-out: scaffold-stamped type, body human-free, draft local-only by default; export/report/incident/conflict: machine shapes as already specified in §3/§6/§8) — and the enforcement point per class: machine classes conformant by construction (VaultWriter serializes from typed fields, §18(6)); human classes stamped at scaffold, bodies never validated (flags never block). Present the enum in the table as two groups — knowledge classes (work, fulltext, digest, note, project, draft, ruled-out) and projection/operational classes (evidence, gaps, export, report, incident, conflict) — with one sentence recording that this is the ADR-126 layer distinction carried as grouping, not as per-type rule machinery. In §7 (DigestEngine), one sentence: digest.md renders the JSON under the fixed headings above so section-scoped reading and any future section-scoped FTS survive as plain markdown. No schema files, no validator, no change to §18(6).

**Open questions (owner):** 1) Does the owner accept contract-as-stated-artifact with enforcement-by-construction (the §3 table) as satisfying R-6, or does R-6 require a machine-checkable schema artifact plus a validation pass? The latter re-opens the ADR-126 accretion surface and exceeds the charter's Knowledge-format bar — if the owner wants it anyway, that is a claim that the charter under-scopes the knowledge format and needs an explicit charter amendment, not a design edit. 2) Should human-class bodies (project.md, notes) ever be validated rather than merely scaffolded? That collides with "flags never block," zero-migration, and the Trust row, and it is really R-12's question (only draft.md freehand) — the owner should resolve it there, with R-8 (Memoria-born vault) as a dependency since it removes the zero-migration constraint. 3) The export gate's "mapped project claim" refusal needs a defined claim-delimitation contract in project.md to be implementable — should that contract land in the §3 table (as proposed) or in §8's export-gate spec, and does the owner want it this side of the alpha.16 argument-graph work it foreshadows?

**Skeptic corrections:** Two evidence-weight corrections, neither disposition-changing. (1) Argument_for point (3) should drop or demote the "One schema, three enforcement points" borrow (borrow-adapt-reject L39) as an unfolded-beta1-borrow: its operative content is a per-type schema driving a capture form plus Guard validation as authority, "Strict, not liberal: unknown fixed-set values reject" — the exact posture design §18(6) explicitly declined on 2026-07-04 (post-dating the borrow's 2026-07-03 target assignment), and its substrate (capture forms, templates as second encodings) is absent from beta.1, as the verdict's own reasoning section concedes. Citing it beside the MASSW borrow overstates the owner's side; only the MASSW L97 borrow is compatible with the verdict's own "no schema files, no validator" remedy and should carry that point alone. (2) Argument_for point (1) over-reaches with design-history L1629: alpha.11 retired alert/flag/gap/queue/worker-card/worklist-item as DB-side "projections or worker state, not durable Concepts," but beta.1 deliberately materializes evidence.md/gaps.md as vault files under its file-vs-DB split (design L220-222) — the opposite of alpha.11's projections-stay-DB-side stance — so they are not the same objects re-mixed; the enum-grouping recommendation should rest on ADR-126's layer test (design-history L2074, "a thing on a different layer (a source record) is not a knowledge type") and the gap report's own flag (gap-report L38) alone. All other citations audited accurate: §18(6) at L1303-1312, flags-never-block at design L256-258, charter Knowledge-format L36 and Human-text L72, ADR-119 drift at design-history L1439, accretion at L2284-2286, OKF inversion at L2296-2298, and the three amendments' entry mappings match S03.md/S04.md.

### R-7+R-11+R-20 — Argument graph is core (claim substrate, JSON-Canvas graphs, writing+coding modules)

**Verdict: REJECT** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The owner's value-chain claim is conceded by the corpus itself: the docs-history dossier calls the alpha.16 writing module "largely pre-designed" and its own borrow rows say "a project can have zero missing notes and still be intellectually bankrupt" — retrieval-coverage gaps cannot see argumentative bankruptcy (docs-history L19, L51). The retention literature the beta.1 research collected shows output-anchored synthesis is what retained researchers (Heptabase's sustained PhD adoption, info-flow-research L1052-1055) while pure networked-notes promises churned (Roam, L1056-1059), so a beta.1 reduced to draft.md + an export gate risks losing the payoff claim to ChatGPT's fluent drafting for a reason knowable in advance. The claim substrate genuinely is the graph's prerequisite — ADR-126 made claim/question a mode precisely because "field-derived typing could not tell a plain thought from a claim missing its evidence" (design-history L2074-2076) — and dropping mode, typed links, paper_plan, deliverable targets, frame-paper, and --ready-only (gap-report L41, L43) strips every production-side substrate at once, betting the whole differentiator on grounding alone. The alpha line carried this machinery continuously from ADR-52 (alpha.1) through ADR-77/78/79 (alpha.5) to the alpha.15 typed project concept, and code/ sat beside drafts/ and exports/ in the alpha.5 project skeleton (design-history L957) — this is a 14-release investment, not a speculative feature.

**For beta.1:** The charter is a retention experiment, not a feature milestone (requirements L9-11), and its production bar is explicit: Compose = "gather evidence, show gaps, produce a markdown draft, and export markdown plus BibTeX" (L32); Payoff = one compose moment beating a same-day ChatGPT counterfactual ending in a portable exported draft (L18-19) — beta.1 meets all of it, with the export gate strengthened to refuse on superseded/retracted works and unwarranted mapped claims (design §8 L827-843, §18 R2). The argument graph never earned its keep through use: no production vault ever existed in the entire alpha line (design-history L1916; S8.1 history), and its own earned safety rule defeats it in beta.1's measurement window — the alpha.5 maturity floor (≥5 addressed relations incl. ≥1 contradicts, below which all structural signals display below-threshold, and "impact ranking is weakest precisely when orientation is most needed," design-history L969-975) guarantees the graph is structurally mute in a cold-start vault while billing PI authoring cost the Parity claim cannot afford (warrant authoring was already ruled "the single biggest labor sink for the least deterministic payoff"). The charter pre-registers exactly the detection the owner's hypothesis needs: synthesis-shaped Asks instrumented separately to attribute payoff failure to evidence granularity vs grounding (L54), relegation clusters tracked ahead of abandonment (L54), and a missed engagement number maps to "targeted redesign, never kill" (L53) — so if the production end is the binding constraint, the experiment proves it cheaply and routes to the pre-designed alpha.16 module (docs-history action 10). The saturation face is separately charter-barred (Aggregate evidence scores, L85), the coding module is charter-barred (Deep code intelligence, L86 — beta.1's inert-but-surviving code files meet that row's own bar), and JSON Canvas as the rendering contradicts the alpha.15 evidence-based rejection of ADR-103 ("spatial-at-scale refuted; tabular/faceted is the validated default," design-history L2182, L2233) plus two info-flow verdicts saying don't build a canvas for beta.1 (L289, L1054).

**Decision:** Three considerations decide it. (1) The deferral is compatible with the retention experiment because the experiment is designed to adjudicate the owner's own hypothesis: the charter's leading-indicator and attribution rows (requirements L53-54) make "payoff fails because the production end is missing" a measurable, pre-registered outcome with "targeted redesign, never kill" as the response — building the argument graph first would spend the friction budget (info-flow: abandonment clusters at month three around elaborate workflows) on machinery that is never-user-validated and, by its own maturity-floor rule, structurally muted during the cold-start weeks beta.1 measures. (2) The history shows the graph was earned by design reasoning, never by use: built at alpha.5 (structural_impact.py), rebuilt at alpha.11 (analyze-project-argument, render-project-argument-canvas), absorbed at alpha.15 (typed project, paper_plan, deliverable targets) — and at every step the record itself warns the signals are worthless below graph maturity, which a fresh beta.1 vault cannot reach quickly. Deferral-with-a-named-home (docs-history action 10 seeds alpha.16 with the full dossier, standing rejects included) honors the 14-release investment better than shipping it into a cold vault. (3) Each sub-position independently hits a decisive record: saturation/ordinal scoring collides with the Aggregate-evidence-scores exclusion; the coding module collides with the Deep-code-intelligence exclusion and the ADR-34 rejection (alpha.5) plus alpha.11's explicit code scope-out; JSON-Canvas-as-rendering collides with the alpha.15 ADR-103 rejection grounded in refuted spatial-at-scale evidence — the only admissible canvas form is a generated snapshot projection (never the edge store, pinned layout, docs-history adapt row 100), which is an alpha.16 rendering decision. The claim substrate (R-10) travels with its consumer by the owner's own framing, so it stands or falls with R-7 — and R-7 falls for beta.1 scope. The machine adjudications' dispositions (LEAVE for the recorded deferrals, RECORD for the two silent substrate drops with return-with-consumer language) are exactly right.

**History:** (a) alpha.5 built the Project gate: ADR-77/78/79 accepted 2026-06-16, structural_impact.py (~800 lines), gap taxonomy, and the hard-coded maturity threshold — "the gate's trust switch... not a knob to tune"; below ≥5 addressed relations incl. ≥1 supports AND ≥1 contradicts, confidence displays below-threshold; cold-start uses scope-overlap because "impact ranking is weakest precisely when orientation is most needed"; warrant authoring deliberately left off as "the single biggest labor sink... for the least deterministic payoff" (design-history L945-990). The same release created projects/_template/{code,drafts,exports} (L957) and REJECTED ADR-34 code-artifact autopilot ("declined, not parked," L987). (b) alpha.11 re-derived the graph as operations — analyze-project-argument, render-project-argument-canvas (L1685) — and explicitly scoped out code-note/coding artifacts (L1655 region, §7.1/§15). (c) alpha.15 absorbed ADR-77/78/79 into the typed project concept: paper_plan, thesis-as-role, deliverable targets outline/section/figure/code as "artifacts, not Concepts" (L2080); native gap engine with {0,1,2} ordinal scoring and the saturation block, checked-only, advisory never gating (L2160 region); --ready-only export under ADR-130 (L2184). (d) Canvas: alpha.7 shipped propose-class JSON Canvas emitters as scratch proposals only — the engine "deliberately does not emit Canvas" as truth (L1158); ADR-103 proposed canvas as projection-never-edge-store (L1311); alpha.15 REJECTED it: "spatial-at-scale refuted; tabular/faceted is the validated default; small-graph view must beat a tabular baseline" (L2182, L2233). (e) No production vault ever existed anywhere in the alpha line (L1916; alpha.14 §0 cutover rule), so none of this machinery was ever exercised by a real researcher — the argument graph was earned by design reasoning, not incident or usage. (f) The deferral is recorded with a named home: docs-history borrow rows L50-58 all Target alpha16, headline L19 "the alpha.16 writing module is largely pre-designed," action 10 (L157) seeds it with the dossier including standing rejects (projected argument canvas engine, L129; agent-executed code loops, L113); info-flow-research L289 and L1054 both rule out building a canvas/whiteboard for beta.1, allowing a generated .canvas snapshot later.

**Entry amendments:**
- S3.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — sound but unrecorded (unchanged) — Keep the prescribed §11 divergence entry stating the claim/question mode and claim-context substrate return with their alpha.16 argument-graph consumer; per the owner's own R-10 the substrate belongs to R-7's scope and falls with it for beta.1.
- S3.4: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — deliberate and recorded (unchanged) — The argument-graph project concept, deliverable targets, frame-paper, and --ready-only are the recorded alpha.16 writing-module deferral (docs-history L50-57, action 10); the charter's Compose bar requires gather/gaps/draft/export, not an argument graph, and the saturation face is charter-barred.
- S3.6: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — sound but unrecorded (unchanged) — Keep the prescribed §11 entry: typed-link consumers are alpha.16 scope and the representation question (including a possible generated-.canvas rendering) reopens with them; supersession, the one live relation, is carried by superseded-by.
- S6.16: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — deliberate and recorded (unchanged) — Ordinal scoring plus a saturation band is an aggregate evidence score, directly covered by the charter's Deliberate Exclusion (requirements L85) and the Calibration row (L50); beta.1 ships no phase-confidence meter rather than a weakened one.
- S8.1: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — deliberate and recorded (unchanged) — Retrieval-coverage gaps with printed denominators meet the charter's show-gaps bar; the argument-graph machinery's honesty core (never present machine confidence on sparse evidence) survives as the empty-contrasts refusal and denominator discipline in design §8.

**Open questions (owner):** (1) Charter scope is the owner's call: R-7's "the alpha.16 deferral is overruled" is an argument that the charter under-scopes the Payoff claim — if the owner genuinely believes retention fails without the production end, the honest move is a dated charter amendment expanding the Compose/Payoff bars (a bigger, longer beta), not a design-body change; the corpus evidence (cold-start maturity floor, friction budget, pre-registered attribution of payoff failures) argues the current sequencing is the cheaper test of his own hypothesis, but only he can re-scope the experiment. (2) Alpha.16 commitment: the deferral's soundness rests on alpha.16 actually executing docs-history action 10's dossier — the owner should confirm the writing/coding module is a committed next release with the dossier as starting spec, otherwise "deferred" degrades into the silent-delete pattern the docs-history warns about. (3) R-11's admissible remainder: when the graph returns at alpha.16, a generated JSON Canvas *snapshot* (projection only, never the authoritative edge store, layout positions pinned, gated on the feasibility spike — docs-history adapt row 100, info-flow L289) is compatible with the record; canvas-as-workspace/engine remains refuted (ADR-103 rejection; reject row 129). Whether alpha.16 graphs render as .canvas snapshots vs the validated tabular/faceted default is an owner rendering decision for that release, under those constraints. (4) Optional record hygiene, owner's preference: the production-end deferral (argument graph + writing module → alpha.16) is recorded in the docs-history file but not named in design §11's own divergence list — a one-line §11 addition would give the governing document single-file visibility of the largest re-sequencing in the gap corpus, at zero mechanism cost.

**Skeptic corrections:** Two precision fixes, neither verdict-affecting: (1) "the maturity floor guarantees the graph is structurally mute in a cold-start vault" overstates — alpha.5's own design ships a deterministic cold-start regime (scope-overlap triage, design-history L975) precisely because "impact ranking is weakest when orientation is most needed," so below the floor the gate degrades to honest low-confidence orientation rather than muteness; the accurate claim is that the structural payoff (impact ranking, saturation — L969-971: saturation_state forced "unknown" in cold-start) is inoperative during the measurement window's opening weeks while typed-link authoring bills the Parity budget. (2) "The charter pre-registers exactly the detection the owner's hypothesis needs" is generous: L54's pre-registered attribution axis is "evidence granularity vs grounding" (confirmed verbatim in design §8), which does not name a missing-production-end cause; the owner-hypothesis detection actually rests on L53 (qualitative researcher judgment primary; missed engagement → "targeted redesign, never kill") and L54's relegation-cluster tracking, which the verdict also cites — so the leg holds, but on those rows. Minor: the maturity floor is ≥5 addressed relations incl ≥1 supports AND ≥1 contradicts (L969), not only ≥1 contradicts. The open questions (charter re-scope is an owner amendment, alpha.16 commitment is load-bearing, .canvas snapshot admissible at alpha.16, one-line §11 record) are correct and should stand.

### R-8 — Memoria is a new vault, never added into an existing one

**Verdict: UPHOLD** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The nesting premise is unresearched and thin in beta.1's own terms: it appears only as assertion (design §3 L191-192, L253-262), with zero grounding in the 1059-line info-flow research (its sole "existing vault" hit, L258, is about license partitioning) and no docs-history borrow, while the design elsewhere concedes pre-existing notes buy nothing — §5 L414-416 refuses to embed them ("embedding the user's whole personal vault buys no beta.1 feature"), they are not indexed, not manifested, and not consumed by any flow, so nesting's entire functional payoff is human wikilink convenience. The recorded parity rationale (§1 L47-50, "the researcher already lives in Obsidian; zero app-switching") argues for Obsidian-as-host versus a standalone app, not for co-residency in the researcher's pre-existing vault — the nesting decision borrows that argument's glow without its own. Meanwhile nesting bills real machinery and hazard: the sibling-root collision policy (S02.md action + verifier fix exist only to patch it), the zero-migration-dependent justification of the human-detection rule (§3 L261-262), and — unexamined in the design — §6's snapshot substrate (`--work-tree=<vault>`, commit-all pre-tags, incident path `git reset --hard pre/r_…`, L448-476) which mechanically sweeps the researcher's entire foreign corpus into Memoria's git and puts it inside a whole-tree hard-reset failure path, touching the charter's immediate-stop human-text bar (requirements L72). The whole alpha line was Memoria-born ("alpha.14 is a standalone workspace, not an Obsidian vault adapter," history L1936; repo-is-the-install-unit, L567), and the owner's position system (R-3 quarantine-then-verify, R-12 only-draft-freehand) is only coherent over a tree wholly under Memoria's regime — nesting is precisely what forced beta.1 to narrow alpha's quarantine posture to trusted-by-default (gap report §5). Finally, beta.1 is a retention experiment on exactly one researcher — the owner — and no charter row requires co-residency; a retention experiment whose only subject rejects the deployment topology measures topology friction, not product value.

**For beta.1:** Obsidian wikilinks, backlinks, graph, and search do not cross vault boundaries, so a Memoria-born vault permanently severs the researcher's years of existing notes from works/, fulltext anchors, and projects — URI links are the only bridge and they carry no backlinks or hover; when composition wants the researcher's own prior thinking, the only remedy is manual copy-in, i.e. the migration cost zero-migration eliminated, deferred and paid by hand (this is the merits case S02.md L9 relied on to keep the entry). The charter frames beta.1 against the null workflow "Zotero + Obsidian + ad-hoc ChatGPT" (requirements L9-11), and the abandonment tracker scores "fallback to null tools" (L49): a second vault inserts a window-switch between the researcher's daily driver and Memoria, a classic abandonment channel that in-situ nesting eliminates. The blast-radius and collision costs of nesting do not force a new vault — the minimal remedies are footprint-scoped restore in §6 and the already-drafted install-time collision rule (S02.md verifier notes) — so beta.1's shape is repairable in place. And the alpha precedent's earned reason for whole-tree ownership (golden-copy repair, folders.yaml single source) was dissolved by the alpha line itself at alpha.15 (golden_restore removed, "package reinstall is the restore path"), so history supplies identity, not a binding mechanism; per the ground rules, "alpha was standalone" is not itself an argument.

**Decision:** Three considerations decide it. (1) The charter is genuinely neutral: no Required-Scope row needs co-residency (Parity rows measure action speed — writing a note in a Memoria-born vault is plain Obsidian at identical speed; Reading/Ask/Compose/Survival are vault-topology-independent; the Knowledge-format row names "the Memoria/ tree," satisfiable in either topology), so this is a choice between two charter-compatible shapes, which makes the decision quality of each side the test. (2) On decision quality the sides are asymmetric: nesting is a one-line unresearched premise whose only in-design payoff (human wikilinks to pre-existing notes) supports no charter bar, while it generates dedicated machinery (collision policy, zero-migration rationale chains) and an unexamined safety hazard (§6 whole-foreign-vault commit-all + `git reset --hard` incident path over notes Memoria does not govern); Memoria-born deletes that machinery — under the project's own minimal-machinery rule it is the smaller design — restores coherence with the rest of the owner's position system (R-3, R-12) and with the alpha-line identity whose integrity regime (universal frontmatter, quarantine-until-verified) presupposed a wholly-governed tree. (3) The wikilink-severance counterargument, the strongest against, bills only researcher convenience — and the researcher is the owner, who has priced and rejected it; the machine adjudication's claim that a Memoria-born vault "undercuts note-writing-parity and retention claims" (S02.md L9) overstates the charter, since parity is action speed, not corpus co-location, and retention is validly measured on whichever topology actually ships. The host-decision complex is still ADR-pending ("a proposal, not product truth," §16 L1152-1158), so reversing the nesting premise now is cheap. Uphold — scoped to the nesting sub-delta of S2.1 only; the shell removals and engine-private-state relocation in the same entry are independently reasoned continuations of the alpha.12→15 trajectory and stand.

**History:** The alpha line was Memoria-born end to end, and nesting has no precedent in either direction. Origins: "The repo is the install unit" (ADR-26), scaffold→populate→golden-copy install flow (ADR-55) — history L567, L619; the vault was Memoria's own git repo (ADR-104 reasoning "the vault is already a Git repo," L1284). Alpha.14 states the identity outright: "--workspace not --vault because 'alpha.14 is a standalone workspace, not an Obsidian vault adapter'" (L1936); alpha.15 fenced editor adapters behind their own future ADR (L2216). The gap report confirms "nesting Memoria as a subfolder has no alpha-line precedent (the workspace *was* the install from the Old Skeleton through A15)" (gap report L30). However, the whole-tree-ownership machinery reason was dissolved by the alpha line itself: alpha.15 removed golden_restore.py (PR #1206; "package reinstall is the restore path," ADR-125 — per S02.md L12), so what survives from history is the standalone identity and its integrity regime (universal frontmatter alpha.14 PR #1157; ADR-127 quarantine-until-verified of foreign edits, gap report §5), not an install-machinery obligation. Beta.1's regression review never tested the standalone-workspace identity as an invariant (no nesting adjudication anywhere in it), the info-flow research contains no nesting discussion, and the zero-migration premise exists only in design §3 — an unresearched clean-slate insertion of exactly the class the owner's addendum flags (owner-rulings L110-112). S02.md's own history verdict agrees no earned failure blocks either topology ("Nesting beside foreign notes has no alpha precedent in either direction — no earned failure is re-opened," L12); what it did not weigh is that beta.1's §6 substrate (design L448-476: work-tree=<vault>, commit-all pre-tags, reset --hard incident path) silently extends Memoria's failure machinery over a corpus it does not govern — a hazard only the nesting topology creates at that scale.

**Entry amendments:**
- S2.1: RECORD — sound but unrecorded (record folders.yaml retirement + Memoria/-collision policy; R-8 noted as under re-examination) → CHANGE — scoped to the nesting sub-delta: design §3 rewritten to a Memoria-born vault per R-8; the catalog/spaces/journal shell removals and the engine-private-state relocation to the per-device data dir stand as adjudicated; the folders.yaml-retirement recording sentence is kept (topology-independent); the two-sibling-roots collision policy is superseded by an init-time rule (refuse a non-empty target; reconnect a directory whose Memoria/index.md carries okf_version "0.1", never re-mint) — Replace the zero-migration/nesting premise in design §3 with the Memoria-created-vault model and record the divergence in §11, leaving the entry's other sub-deltas and their recordings intact.

**Design change (if adopted):** Minimal change, all in design.md: (1) §3 layout block L191-192 — replace "<vault>/ # the user's existing vault, untouched" and the "<existing notes> # zero migration, zero markers required" line with "<vault>/ # a Memoria-created vault (minted by mem init / the onboarding wizard); Memoria is never installed into a pre-existing vault". (2) §3 L253-258 — delete "pre-existing notes outside it stay untouched by design (zero-migration)"; keep the bundle boundary as Memoria/ (charter Knowledge-format row verbatim) and keep the freehand-file convergence sentence (researcher freehand files inside the bundle still converge via one-tap proposals). (3) §3 L260-262 — keep "Absence of all mem-* markers = human" but re-derive it: it is the freehand-note detection rule (researcher-authored files need no ceremony), no longer justified by zero-migration. (4) §16 acquisition/§7 seeding — the quickstart creates the vault; install refuses a pre-existing non-empty vault directory; a directory whose bundle-root index.md carries okf_version "0.1" is recognized as an existing Memoria vault and reconnected, never re-minted (this replaces S02.md's proposed collision-policy recording). (5) §11 — add a recorded divergence: "The clean-slate draft's nesting/zero-migration premise (Memoria/ beside existing notes) is overruled per owner ruling R-8: the vault is Memoria-born, restoring the alpha-line standalone-workspace identity ('not an Obsidian vault adapter') in Obsidian-vault form; the two-sibling-roots question and the migration-shaped rationale chains dissolve with it." No change to §6 mechanics is required by R-8 itself (the work-tree becomes a Memoria-governed vault), but see open questions.

**Open questions (owner):** 1) Bundle-root placement: keep <vault>/Memoria/ as the bundle folder inside the Memoria-born vault (satisfies the charter Knowledge-format row verbatim) or promote the vault root to bundle root (cleaner, but needs a one-word charter amendment)? 2) What regime governs researcher-created files outside the bundle in the Memoria vault — free zone, or fully governed (interacts with R-12 and R-3, which are only enforceable under full governance)? 3) Is there a sanctioned one-way import path for selected notes from the researcher's old personal vault, or is the old vault pure archive? 4) Adjacent §6 defect surfaced by this pass, owner attention warranted regardless of R-8: the incident path `git reset --hard pre/r_…` (design L475) resets the entire work-tree, so a human edit typed anywhere in the vault during a failed run is destroyed — the charter's immediate-stop class (requirements L72); a footprint-scoped restore would honor the bar. The Memoria-born vault shrinks this blast radius but does not remove it.

**Skeptic corrections:** Three non-verdict-changing fixes. (1) Reasoning point (3)'s claim that the owner "has priced and rejected" the wikilink-severance cost over-reads owner-rulings L114-120: R-8's text is bare assertion and engages none of the severance merits, so the uphold must rest on its independent legs (parity-as-action-speed; charter neutrality), which it also states — drop or soften the "priced" clause. (2) "Nesting is precisely what forced beta.1 to narrow alpha's quarantine posture to trusted-by-default (gap report §5)" mis-attributes: gap report L63 records the narrowing without attributing it to nesting, and the corpus states the dependency in the enabling direction (design §3 L261-262; gap report L48: the marker-absence rule "is the basis of zero-migration"); the forcing inference is sound (quarantining an unmarked foreign corpus at vault scale is untenable) but should be labeled as the re-examination's inference, not a gap-report finding. (3) Additive: cite docs-history reject row L130 ("No production vault has ever existed... revisit only when beta.1 creates a vault worth migrating") in the proposed §11 divergence recording — it is corpus language consistent with the Memoria-created-vault model and strengthens the amendment.

### R-12 — The only human/freehand file is the draft

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** Read as structured-vs-freehand (the only coherent reading — the owner's own R-10/R-16 make notes the human ZK layer), R-12 is essentially the alpha.15 end-state, not a new demand: alpha.15 made every knowledge file a typed Concept with a per-type schema under closed validation (design-history L2074, L2086, L2090), while the project's deliverables — the draft class — were explicitly "artifacts, not Concepts" (L2080); i.e., "only the draft is freehand" was the shipped model. The structure was earned: alpha.1's note-body contracts carried recorded rationale ("a claim with no links has not made it into the knowledge graph... it cannot compound"; "a source note without a Critique is storage, not synthesis" — L222-225), and freeform human creation had a documented failure record — ADR-71 (L763): no required-field enforcement, controlled vocab as free text, instructional leakage, fixed by schema-driven forms; ADR-119 (L1439): the hand-synced contract had already drifted. The docs-history pass itself targets "One schema, three enforcement points" (schema drives capture form, validation, templates/views) at beta1 (borrow/adapt/reject L39), and beta.1 realizes none of it for human files — an unadjudicated miss against a recorded borrow. Most concretely, beta.1's own export readiness gate consumes structure a freehand project.md cannot supply: it refuses on "a mapped project claim with no mc/Checker-verified anchor and no explicit gap-analysis missing-evidence marker" (design §8 L833-836, §18(2) L1287-1289; regression-review R2 L40), yet the design nowhere defines how a claim is mapped or a gap marker written — the gate is unimplementable against an uncontracted file.

**For beta.1:** The charter — the spec — deliberately admits freehand human files twice: the parity success claim requires "note-writing is no slower than plain Obsidian" (requirements L15-16), and the Knowledge-format bar scopes required typed frontmatter to "every Memoria-created file" (L36); mandatory schema-conformant notes attack the primary retention claim head-on. The docs-history record cuts the same way: "Fleeting capture — keep zero-friction capture — it is where the ChatGPT null workflow wins" is a beta1-targeted Adapt (L91), and the rows that give project.md real body structure (thesis as project.md section L77, versioned research question as body sections L78) are targeted alpha16, with their consumer. In beta.1 human notes have no machine consumer at all — "only works.fulltext (plus opt-in digest chunks) is embedded; notes and projects are hashed for the manifest but not embedded" (design §5 L414-416) — and the argument graph, note modes, hubs, and vocabulary are all deferred/dropped, so per-type note contracts would be exactly the "mechanism without a named consumer decays into decoration" pattern the same corpus warns of (B/A/R L136). The per-type-schema machinery also carries its own documented failure: the 12+ type zoo where "the multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion" (L2074), and capture friction that "pushes work into ad-hoc notes" (L1344-1345). Finally the freehand posture is partially recorded, not silent: §3 L254-262 (one-tap frontmatter proposals, flags never block) and §18(6) L1303-1312 adjudicate it as a deliberate OKF-permissive trade, and project.md/ruled-out.md/draft.md already carry stamped typed frontmatter at creation (§3 L234-237) — beta.1 concedes the frontmatter half of the Concept contract everywhere except raw freehand notes.

**Decision:** Three considerations decide it. (1) The one place R-12 names a live defect rather than a preference is project.md: beta.1 itself re-adopted the alpha export gate (§18(2)) whose refusal predicate — mapped claim, verified anchor, explicit gap marker — presupposes a structure contract the design never defines for the freehand file it reads. That is an internal inconsistency inside chartered required scope (Compose + Citation-honesty bars), so the project.md slice of R-12 is upheld on beta.1's own terms, independent of the argument-graph deferral; the fix is the design's own accepted no-schema pattern for body structure, digest.md's fixed headings (B/A/R L97, target beta1). (2) The notes/ slice fails against the charter: "note-writing no slower than plain Obsidian" plus the Memoria-created-only frontmatter scoping make freehand notes a chartered decision, not sloppiness, and with notes un-indexed and every structure consumer deferred, a beta.1 note schema is structure without a consumer. The owner's own R-10 concedes the substrate question belongs to R-7's argument-graph scope — so the note-Concept contract rides with the R-7 re-examination, not with R-12. (3) ruled-out.md and draft.md are already where R-12's defensible reading puts them: typed frontmatter stamped at creation, human body; ruled-out.md's recorded borrow (L59) defines it as a rationale log with no machine consumer, so a schema adds nothing. What remains genuinely owed is a recorded decision: the human-class freehand roster is currently legible only through §18(6)'s validator-strictness lens, and the unrealized beta1-targeted "one schema, three enforcement points" borrow (L39) is adjudicated nowhere — under the project's own name-every-divergence discipline that silence gets closed with a record, including the revive path (contracts return with the alpha.16 writing module, or earlier if R-7 is upheld). No S8 adjudication entry (discovery/gap analysis) is touched by R-12.

**History:** (a) Alpha.15's shipped file model matches R-12 almost verbatim: four Concept types each with a per-type YAML schema validated in product code, closed validation rejecting undeclared fields, universal meaning-only frontmatter (ULID id/type/title/tags/typed links/aliases) — design-history L2074, L2086, L2090 — while project deliverable targets (outline/section/figure/code, the draft class) were "artifacts, not Concepts" (L2080). The freehand-only-draft roster is the alpha.15 state, not an invention. (b) Structure on human notes was earned by recorded reasoning, not incident: note-body contracts (L222-225: claim without links "cannot compound"; source without critique is "storage, not synthesis"); ADR-71 structured capture (L763: free-text creation gave no required-field enforcement, vocab drift, instructional leakage); ADR-119 (L1439: the contract re-encoded in four places had already drifted). (c) The counter-record is equally earned: the type zoo "grew by accretion... the multiplicity itself caused drift and confusion" (L2074); fleeting capture friction "pushes work into ad-hoc notes" and "capture should not steal focus" (L1344-1345); ADR-128's theatre finding against blocking gates (L2110-2112). (d) The docs-history B/A/R file splits the question by release: "One schema, three enforcement points" is a beta1-targeted borrow beta.1 never realized (L39), zero-friction fleeting capture is a beta1-targeted adapt (L91), digest.md fixed-headings-no-schema is a beta1-targeted adapt (L97), while thesis-as-project.md-section and the versioned research question as body sections are alpha16-targeted (L77-78). (e) Beta.1 state: notes/projects un-embedded (§5 L414-416); scaffolded human files type-stamped (§3 L234-237); freehand notes converge via proposals (§3 L254-262, §18(6) L1303-1312); export gate consumes undefined project.md claim mapping (§8 L833-836, §18(2), regression-review L40). All paths: /home/eranr/memoria-vault/scratch/design-history/memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md, /home/eranr/memoria-vault/scratch/releases/0.1.0-beta.1/{0.1.0-beta.1-design.md, 0.1.0-beta.1-requirements.md, 0.1.0-beta.1-alpha-regression-review.md, 0.1.0-beta.1-docs-history-borrow-adapt-reject.md}.

**Entry amendments:**
- S3.1: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → CHANGE — narrow (severity: low-medium), scoped to the R-12 slice only — Define the project.md Concept contract that design §8's export gate already consumes (fixed body headings plus the claim-mapping and accepted-gap marker syntax the mapped-claim refusal parses), and add a recorded decision naming the human-class freehand roster as a deliberate file-model choice — notes freehand for the charter parity bar, per-type human-file contracts returning with the argument-graph module — closing the silence around the unrealized beta1-targeted 'one schema, three enforcement points' borrow; the enum-vs-schema and validator halves stay LEAVE pending the R-6 re-examination.
- S3.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD (unchanged) — The note claim/question substrate is the notes-half of R-12 but the owner's own R-10 assigns it to R-7's argument-graph scope, so its disposition rides with the R-7 re-examination; the existing RECORD action (name the drop in §11 with the alpha.16 revive path) already implements what R-12 can independently demand.
- S2.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded (hub silence) → RECORD (unchanged) — R-12's ruled-out.md/draft.md aspect is rejected: both already carry stamped typed frontmatter with a deliberately human body (§3 L234-237), ruled-out.md's recorded borrow defines it as an unconsumed rationale log, and the entry's RECORD disposition (owned by the R-2 hub re-examination) is untouched by R-12.
- S8.1-S8.4: leave 3 / record 1 → unchanged — No amendment — the gap-report S8 entries adjudicate discovery/gap analysis; R-12's '§8' reference is design.md §8 Compose, whose defect is carried under the S3.1 amendment above.

**Design change (if adopted):** Two minimal edits. (1) design.md §8 Compose (at L818, the project.md sentence): replace "project.md (human: question + outline citing evidence/spans)" with a defined Concept contract — project.md is machine-scaffolded at project creation (type: project stamped, body human) with fixed headings (e.g. Question / Outline / Claims / Accepted gaps), where a claim is a list line under Claims carrying [[citekey#^anchor]] or [@citekey] citations, and an accepted gap is an explicit marker line (the gaps.md-ledger form per the docs-history tri-disposition adapt is an acceptable alternative home); state that the export readiness gate's mapped-claim refusal (§8/§18(2)) parses exactly this contract. This is the digest.md fixed-headings pattern (structure that survives as plain markdown — no schema files, no validator, no blocking), so it does not reopen §18(6). (2) design.md §18 add recorded decision (7) — "Human-class file model": name the roster (notes/ freehand by design under the charter's note-writing-parity bar, converging via one-tap proposals; project.md/ruled-out.md/draft.md type-stamped scaffolds with human bodies; draft.md the only fully uncontracted file); record that per-type Concept contracts for human files — including the docs-history "one schema, three enforcement points" borrow and the note claim substrate — are deferred to the alpha.16 writing module and return earlier if the R-7 re-examination pulls the argument graph into beta.1. Echo one sentence in the §11 divergence list.
