**Open questions (owner):** 1) Conformance mode: does the owner intend blocking schema validation on human-authored files at write time, or is proposal-based convergence acceptable? Blocking conformance for notes/ contradicts the charter's "note-writing no slower than plain Obsidian" parity bar and the flags-never-block rule — if intended, that is a charter amendment (the owner arguing the charter under-scopes), not a design fix. 2) Does the note-Concept contract ride with R-7's disposition (per R-10's own scoping), or does the owner want a beta.1 note schema even with no beta.1 consumer (notes un-indexed, graph deferred)? 3) Is the stamped-type + freehand-body form acceptable for ruled-out.md, or does R-12 require body sections there too? 4) For the project.md contract: fixed headings + citation-bearing claim lines (the minimal gate-serving slice proposed here), or the fuller alpha16-targeted shape (thesis section, versioned research question) pulled forward?

**Skeptic corrections:** Three fixes, none verdict-flipping. (1) Missing engagement with owner R-8: the notes-slice rejection leans on §3 L254-262's freehand-convergence proposals as the recorded posture, but R-8 (owner-rulings L114-120) explicitly governs "freehand-file convergence proposals" and demands their re-derivation if the vault is Memoria-born — the §18(7) recorded decision should either cite R-8's pending re-examination or drop the proposals-mechanism leg and rest solely on charter L15-16/L36 plus the no-consumer state (§5 L414-416), which hold independently of zero-migration. (2) The argument_for's "adjudicated nowhere" for the beta1-targeted "one schema, three enforcement points" borrow (B/A/R L39) is overstated: §18(6) (design L1303-1312) adjudicates its validation-strictness third by declining the strict-reject validator; only the capture-form and templates/views thirds are unadjudicated — the reasoning section concedes this ("legible only through §18(6)'s validator-strictness lens") but the argument_for should match. (3) The S3.1 amendment homes the project.md-contract CHANGE under an entry whose gap statement is the enum/per-type-schema-files delta; the defect is a §8 Compose contract gap (gate consumes undefined structure), so it should be carried as a new §8-scoped finding or the S3.1 amendment should state it extends the entry's scope — procedural cleanliness only, the design change itself is correct and minimal.

### R-13 — Discovery must have topics

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The owner is factually right that beta.1 has zero topical substrate: no `tags` field, no vocabulary.md, no facets, no topic edges — grep-verified in the adjudication (S03.md L69-72), and even the recording of the drop was silent. Three real jobs contract with it: (a) topical enumeration/browse ("show me everything I have about X") has no surface — Ask returns ranked top-k evidence with a per-work cap (design §8 L766-767), not a shelf, and Bases has no topic field to view by; (b) topic-level gap analysis ("my catalog is thin in area X I never asked about") has no substrate — beta.1 content gaps are per-question df-0 facets (§8 L782-787), which cannot see an unasked area, and the gap-matrix/charting machinery that would serve it lives only in the unfolded if-design lens (L180, enrichment-only tier; L140, closed charting vocabulary); (c) beyond-catalog lookup for X with zero seed works is structurally impossible — snowball only radiates from held works (§7 L727-739), so for topics outside the citation neighborhood the owner's sentence "the system cannot help the user find information about X" is literally true. The alpha line carried topical classification continuously from the Old Skeleton (gap report §3, S3.7 entry L44), alpha.14 wired topics into retrieval query expansion, gap coverage counting, and discovery candidate generation (design-history L1992, L2004-2006), and the if-design itself needs OpenAlex topic/concept clustering for its cold-start hub bootstrap (if-design L172) — evidence that a topics tier keeps acquiring consumers whenever the system grows an organizing layer.

**For beta.1:** For the beta.1 charter's actual bars, the topics substrate is not load-bearing, and its earned alpha rationale is mooted rather than re-opened. (1) In-catalog "find about X": the vocabulary discipline's documented failure was facet-string drift making facet queries silently incomplete ("receptivity-detection vs opportune-moments… the PI infers thin coverage when coverage is adequate", design-history L218) — a failure mode of literal facet queries, which beta.1 has none of; its query surface is FTS5 BM25 ∪ vector retrieval (design §8 L766-767), where dense embeddings handle exactly the synonymy axis the controlled vocabulary existed to control, and the printed denominator + zero-survivors searched-set banner (§8 L782-792) directly answer the "PI infers thin coverage" harm. (2) The shipped alpha value was thinner than the position implies: ADR-30's embedding+zero-shot tag layer — "the system's value" — was never built; classify diverged to a deterministic OpenAlex-topic mapping (design-history L1368), no production vault ever existed, and the alpha.14 topic-edge wave was a weeks-old additive build earned by no documented failure (S09.md L12, S08.md L21). (3) Beyond-catalog: the topic/concept discovery leg was re-derived as out on evidence (VOSviewer/CiteSpace field-scale mapping non-transferable to a single-researcher corpus, verdict avoid, info-flow-research L321-323) while the kept citation leg is positively grounded (Hirt 2023; BibliZap 75%→91-97%, L268), and the charter's amended exclusion deliberately admits only bounded citation-graph discovery — "recommender feeds remain out" (requirements L84). (4) The alpha line itself assigned topical *navigation* to hubs, not facets ("topical navigation is built by hubs", ADR-04's surviving half, design-history L272) — so the browse gap is R-2's question, not R-13's. (5) Any alpha-style restoration collides with standing doctrine: machine-materialized frontmatter facets are a reject with three documented generations of decay (design §5 L418-427, §17(2), docs-history reject L110). (6) The charter's leading-indicators row (requirements L54) already instruments the exact failure the owner predicts — failed/empty Asks feeding relegation clusters — so the beta measures the claim instead of pre-deciding it, and OpenAlex topic payloads survive verbatim in the content-addressed payloads store (§5 L386-387) for a zero-refetch revival.

**Decision:** Decisive considerations. First, decompose the owner's "find information about X" into its three legs and test each against the corpus: retrieval (served — FTS+vector natively covers the synonym-drift failure that earned the controlled vocabulary, with stronger honesty machinery than alpha's facet queries ever had); topical navigation (a real hole, but the alpha line's own doctrine located that function in hubs, which is R-2's re-examination, not a faceting substrate); external discovery (the topic leg was rejected on named evidence in the info-flow pass and is excluded by a dated charter amendment — upholding it here would be re-scoping the charter, which only the owner can do). Second, the ground-rule test — does the drop re-open a documented failure or contradict a charter bar? — comes back negative on both: the facet-drift failure has no query surface to bite (mooted, not ignored), and the Ask/Compose bars are met by corpus retrieval with denominators. Third, the owner's prior does earn something concrete: the machine adjudication left the revival substrate incidental (payloads happen to contain topics) and trigger-less; a position this strongly held by the owner, aimed at a genuinely unserved future capability, should be converted into a pre-registered, falsifiable revive trigger keyed to the charter's own instrumentation — the same treatment S9.14 got for Semantic Scholar. That is a recording strengthening, not an architecture change, so all three dispositions stand: S3.7 RECORD (text strengthened), S9.1 RECORD (as verifier-corrected, plus one cross-reference), S8.2 LEAVE (charter-covered). The owner's endorsements themselves support this shape: R-14 endorses dropping steering.md (the topical steering lever) and R-15's enrichment stage 2 ("maximum metadata… to help the user discover new knowledge") is the natural owner of a topics tier — as enrichment data, exactly the if-design's enrichment-only (unverified) tier, never a curated frontmatter vocabulary.

**History:** (1) alpha.1 (design-history L215-218): `system/vocabulary.md` SSOT with three facets (research_area ~27 curated terms, methodology, claim topics); the earned rationale is facet-value drift producing silently incomplete facet queries — "produces no error… the PI infers thin coverage when coverage is adequate"; research_area was seeded mechanically from OpenAlex topics by classify.py to remove drift at intake; MeSH/ACM CCS deliberately kept OUT of the queryable facet ("for browsing, not querying"). (2) ADR-54 (L244): classify automated because a human gate on high-volume verifiable metadata "is a guaranteed rubber stamp." (3) ADR-04's surviving half (L272): topics live in frontmatter facets, never folders — and topical navigation is built by hubs, not facets. (4) Audit finding (L1368): ADR-30's embedding+zero-shot tag-suggestion layer — the part the ADR calls "the system's value" — was never built; shipped classify was a deterministic OpenAlex-topic mapping (classify.py:118-154). (5) alpha.14 (L1978, L1992, L2004-2006): topics/concepts/keywords/MeSH/SDG imported as graph edges; qmd graph-neighborhood docs carried topic rollups; query expansion over citations/topics/facets was retrieval baseline; gap analysis counted tags/topics/research_area terms as coverage evidence; graph edges fed discovery candidates — all an additive late build, earned by no documented failure or incident. (6) alpha.15 (L2078): hub owns exactly one ID-backed controlled-vocabulary tag (the vocabulary's navigation consumer is the hub); ADR-93 (L2164): tag candidates emitted as unchecked cards, never written. (7) No production vault ever existed in the alpha line (S08.md L12), so no usage incident backs the topical substrate either way. Net: what research_area + vocabulary.md actually powered was facet queries/dashboards, retrieval query expansion, topic-coverage gap counting, and topic-edge discovery candidates — the first is mooted (no facet surface), the second is displaced by dense retrieval, the third and fourth are deferred with named homes (alpha.16 charting/gap-matrix cluster; citation-graph discovery kept on stronger evidence).

**Entry amendments:**
- S3.7: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — with strengthened recording text (pre-registered revive trigger added) — Keep the RECORD disposition but extend the adjudicated §11/§18 recording text so the topics-tier revival is a pre-registered, evaluation-keyed decision (trigger + doctrine bounds + zero-refetch substrate) rather than an incidental possibility.
- S9.1: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — unchanged (one cross-reference sentence added) — Keep the verifier-corrected recording text and add one sentence noting the raw OpenAlex topic/concept/keyword data survives verbatim in the content-addressed payloads store, so the alpha.14 edge wave can be re-materialized at $0 if the S3.7 revive trigger fires.
- S8.2: LEAVE — deliberate and recorded → LEAVE — unchanged — No change: the topic/concept discovery leg is excluded by the dated charter amendment (requirements L84) and re-derived as out on named evidence (info-flow-research L321-323), while the kept citation leg is positively grounded — re-admitting it is a charter-scope question for the owner, not an adjudication change.

**Design change (if adopted):** Extend the S3.7 recording (design.md §11 divergence list or an §18-style recorded decision — the same location the S3.7 action already targets) with a pre-registered revive trigger: "Dropped from alpha.15: the controlled-vocabulary/faceting substrate (system/vocabulary.md, research_area/methodology facets, vocab and classify). Beta.1 retrieval is FTS+vector and discovery is citation-graph-bounded (§17(4)); no facet query surface exists, and machine-materialized frontmatter facets remain a standing reject (§5, §17(2)). OpenAlex topic/concept payloads are preserved verbatim in the content-addressed payloads store (§5), so revival needs no re-fetch. Revive trigger (pre-registered): if beta instrumentation shows topic-shaped Asks failing (failed/empty Asks in the charter's relegation-cluster leading indicator) or snowball recall measurably insufficient for topic-scoped needs, the recorded revive path is the information-flow design's enrichment-only (unverified) topics tier — DB-side, never frontmatter facets, only human-certified stubs ever feeding query drafting — the first post-beta discovery-side expansion alongside the S9.14 Semantic Scholar entry." No other design.md change; no architecture change.

**Open questions (owner):** 1. Charter scope (owner-only): should "find information about X beyond the catalog with zero seed works" — topic-scoped external lookup, impossible under citation-graph-bounded discovery — enter beta.1 scope? That requires amending the Deliberate Exclusion a second time against its stated reason ("corpus-only answers keep gap claims honest"; recommender feeds out). If the owner believes the charter under-scopes discovery here, that is a charter ruling, not an adjudication outcome. 2. Cross-position dependency: if the R-2/R-5 re-examinations restore hubs to beta.1, the alpha.15 hub form carries one ID-backed controlled-vocabulary tag per hub and the if-design's cold-start bootstrap proposes hub stubs from OpenAlex topic/concept clustering (if-design L172) — does the owner intend R-13's substance to be satisfied through the hub layer (the alpha line's own home for topical navigation), making a separate faceting substrate unnecessary even post-beta? 3. Ownership: should the enrichment-only topics tier be adjudicated under R-15's stage-2 enrichment re-examination ("maximum metadata obtainable, to help the user discover new knowledge") rather than as a discovery precondition — i.e., topics as enrichment data with charting consumers, never a curated vocabulary?

**Skeptic corrections:** 1. Citation precision (argument_against item 3 and the S8.2 amendment rationale): info-flow-research L321-323's avoid verdict is stage-labeled "Corpus mapping / gap analysis," not Discovery, and rejects field-scale cluster-map *visualization* (VOSviewer/CiteSpace) while its note explicitly keeps the counting primitives — co-citation, bibliographic coupling, keyword co-occurrence — as transferable "list-generating queries." Saying the topic/concept discovery leg was "re-derived as out on evidence" at L321-323 overstates the research; the decisive grounds for S8.2 LEAVE are requirements L84 (dated charter amendment) + design §7 L722-739 and §17(4), and any recorded text should cite L321-323 only against cluster-map machinery so it cannot later be read as rejecting the counting-primitive queries the research endorses (which the proposed enrichment-only revive path would serve). 2. Missed corroborating record: docs-history borrow/adapt/reject L82 ("Per-project topic hints," Adapt, target alpha15/16 — "topic list + one-line description in the project body/DB, not frontmatter") is an authoritative adapt row the re-examination never cites; it independently confirms the verdict's bounds (topics DB-side, never frontmatter, deferred past beta.1) and is worth one cross-reference in the strengthened S3.7 recording text. 3. Wording nit in design_change: "the first post-beta discovery-side expansion alongside the S9.14 Semantic Scholar entry" collides with S9.14's recorded "the first post-beta enrichment expansion"; keep the tracks explicitly distinct or drop the ordinal so the design does not record two competing "firsts."

### R-15 — Enrichment has two stages: cite-minimum and discovery-maximum

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The two-stage frame is historically real, not invented: from day one ADR-30's Tier-1 merge did both jobs simultaneously — registry-grade record completion AND discovery-signal maximization (S2 supplying intents/tldr/SPECTER, references as a DOI-deduped cross-provider union; history L518) — and the 867-entry spike rejected single-source precisely to maximize obtainable metadata (L521). Alpha.14 then built the stage-2 apparatus out explicitly: topics/concepts/keywords/MeSH/SDG/authorships/Crossref-relation edges imported because "the graph feeds retrieval query expansion and gap analysis" (L1978), with real consumers — gap analysis counting topic/keyword edge terms (L2004) and graph edges feeding discovery candidate generation (L2006) — and ADR-129 promoted S2 to conditional default-on for exactly the discovery signal class (L2142). Beta.1's s7 enrichment paragraph, by contrast, states only a stage-1 purpose ("fills empty fields only — the JabRef rule", L589-592); no sentence anywhere in the design names a discovery-serving goal for enrichment, so the stage-2 contractions (S6.4 roster, S9.1 graph scope, S9.14 S2 drop) were each decided silently against no stated requirement — the machine adjudication itself found all three unrecorded or half-recorded. The frame also has predictive force: it is the correct lens under which R-13 (topics) and R-17 (S2) are not isolated nits but instances of one unstated question — what does stage 2 require?

**For beta.1:** Tested against the three governed entries, "beta.1 collapses both stages into stage 1" is factually overstated, and two of the three entries are vindicated by the frame itself. (a) S6.3: the JabRef rule is a stage-1 merge policy, and its premises moved — Zotero plus citation.doi.org now author the record (s7 L529-541, L554-559), and the spike's each-provider-incomplete premise is weakened by 2026 measurement (Culbert et al. 2025: OpenAlex reference coverage matches WoS/Scopus; info-flow-research L184, JabRef-merge adopt verdict L214-215); crucially the full OpenAlex response — topics, concepts, counts, the stage-2 raw material — is preserved verbatim and replayable in the payloads store (s7 L593-599), so nothing obtainable is discarded, only not-yet-distilled. (b) S9.2: the alpha gate is the thing that conflated the stages — three live providers including Unpaywall as a precondition for a work becoming cite-able (gap report L107) — whereas land-then-resolve delivers stage 1 unconditionally and leaves enrichment non-blocking, exactly the separation R-15 demands; Unpaywall's OA data now runs inside OpenAlex post-Walden (info-flow L184), and the charter's one-initiating-action capture bar independently forbids the gate. (c) S9.11: attention-only refresh governs stage-1 record fields; the discovery-feeding signals do get scheduled background acquisition — the idle capped cited-by backfill (s7 L600-603), the scheduled citation monitor (L740-744), and the weekly retraction audit — and alpha never decided a cadence at all (S09.md L110: a standing open question, not a shipped mechanism). Beta.1 also already has a stage-2-lite with charter license: bounded snowball + monitor discovery (s7 L722-744; charter L84 amended exclusion).

**Decision:** The decisive test is whether the frame, taken as true, flips any governed entry from RECORD to CHANGE — i.e. whether each delta is a stage-2 collapse or a stage-1 policy the frame actually endorses. S9.2 fails the test outright: gating citation-eligibility on enrichment providers is stage conflation, and removing it is the two-stage architecture; the owner's own frame says stage 1 is "the bare minimum needed to cite," which land-then-resolve delivers without waiting on stage 2. S9.11 fails because the freshness that matters to discovery (new citers, retractions) is already on scheduled background channels, while record-field background refresh is counter-indicated by the Mendeley postmortem and freshness-at-moment-of-use practice (info-flow L184) — the rule is per-stage, not a blanket staleness posture. S6.3 is the closest call, but the merge rule governs only who authors the citation record; the "maximum obtainable" metadata from the one admitted provider is fetched and kept verbatim in payloads, so the stage-2 deficit is in distillation and consumption scope (no topic edges, no facets, no S2) — and those contractions are the S9.1/S6.4/S9.14 entries, governed by R-13 and R-17 re-examinations, not these three. What survives of R-15 is real but narrower than CHANGE: beta.1 nowhere states that enrichment has a discovery-serving second stage, which is why every stage-2 contraction went unrecorded — the frame should be written into the design as the governing statement, and the three entries' already-mandated RECORD texts should use the stage vocabulary so the distinction does not get lost again. That is a recording-plus-framing fix, not a mechanism change, hence partial.

**History:** (1) ADR-30/alpha.1 (history L515-527): enrichment was born two-purpose — Tier-1 resolve/merge is per-field best-source-wins for record fields AND carries discovery signals (S2 intents/tldr/embedding; references = DOI-deduped union); single-source rejected on the 867-entry spike (reference counts 151/129/146 across S2/OpenAlex/Crossref; ORCID in OpenAlex, ~0 in S2). (2) Alpha.14 (L1974-1978): full text became a hard digest precondition — the reason the Unpaywall retry loop existed (L1976) — and the graph import expanded to topics/concepts/keywords/mesh/SDG/authorships/relations because "the graph feeds retrieval query expansion and gap analysis". (3) Alpha.14 consumers (L2002-2006): gap analysis counted topic/keyword edge terms; graph edges fed discovery candidate generation without qmd rediscovery — stage 2 had named consumers. (4) ADR-129/alpha.15 (L2138-2142): merge hardened (provider_coverage=full|partial|degraded, conflict raises attention, never silent overwrite); S2 promoted conditional default-on-when-keyed for TLDRs/SPECTER/citation-intents — "proposers, never authorities". (5) Refresh cadence: never a decided alpha mechanism — a standing open question across alpha.13-15 (S09.md L110 verifier notes, omnibus 09bf018f), so no earned position backs background TTL refresh. (6) Info-flow research L184 (2026 evidence): OpenAlex two-source spine with Crossref fill-in is best practice; Unpaywall runs inside OpenAlex post-Walden; Culbert et al. 2025 shows OpenAlex reference coverage matches WoS/Scopus; JabRef empty-field merge is the proven mechanism (Mendeley postmortem against background auto-refresh; freshness scoped to moment of use). The stage-2 side: L268/L321-324 — field-scale topic mapping verdict "avoid" for a single-researcher corpus, but counting primitives transfer as list-generating queries.

**Entry amendments:**
- S6.3: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — recording text amended with the two-stage frame — Keep RECORD; amend the proposed s11/s18 recording to state that the JabRef rule is stage-1 (cite-minimum) merge policy under registry/Zotero record authority, that the stage-2 raw material (full OpenAlex payload incl. topics/concepts/counts) is preserved verbatim in the payloads store for future distillation, and that stage-2 distillation scope is governed by the s7 two-stage statement (see design_change), not by this merge rule.
- S9.2: RECORD — sound but unrecorded (verifier: half-adjudicated) → RECORD — recording text amended with the two-stage frame — Keep RECORD; amend the recording to state that land-then-resolve implements the stage separation (stage-1 citing never waits on stage-2/acquisition fetches — the alpha gate conflated them), and that Unpaywall's OA-location data now ships inside OpenAlex post-Walden (info-flow-research L184), so the drop is roster consolidation plus the recorded Zotero-handoff decision, not a stage-2 capability loss.
- S9.11: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — recording text amended with the two-stage frame — Keep RECORD with the verifier's corrected text; add one sentence naming the per-stage freshness split — stage-1 record fields refresh on attention with as-of stamps, stage-2 discovery signals get scheduled/idle background acquisition (capped cited-by backfill, citation monitor) and retraction its weekly audit — so 'no background auto-refresh' is a stage-1 rule, not a system-wide staleness posture.

**Design change (if adopted):** Add a short governing statement to design.md s7, immediately before the "Enrichment (corpus-scoped, $0)" paragraph (L589): "Enrichment has two goals, staged. Stage 1 — cite-minimum: the registry-authored record plus Zotero fidelity gives every landed work a complete, cite-able record; land-then-resolve means stage 1 never waits on stage 2. Stage 2 — discovery: metadata that helps the researcher find knowledge inside and outside the catalog. Beta.1 ships stage 2 deliberately citation-graph-only (reference edges, capped cited-by, snowball + monitor); the verbatim payloads store retains each provider's full response so later stage-2 distillation (topic facets, additional providers) needs no re-fetch. Stage-2 expansions are named, not silent: Semantic Scholar revives per its recorded trigger (s11 divergence note), and topic/facet distillation follows the R-13 resolution." Plus the three amended RECORD texts above (s11 divergence list / s18-style entries, as each adjudication already specifies).

**Open questions (owner):** (1) Does the charter under-scope stage 2? No charter row requires discovery quality or recall — the amended exclusion (requirements L84) merely permits bounded citation-graph discovery. If discovery-maximum is a beta.1 requirement rather than a post-beta expansion, the charter needs a Discovery row, and that decision — not these three entries — is where R-13 (topics) and R-17 (S2) land. (2) Does "maximum metadata obtainable" mean store-maximum (the payloads store already achieves this for the admitted providers) or distill-and-consume-maximum (which requires naming beta.1 consumers, against the corpus's own warning that a mechanism without a named consumer decays into decoration)? (3) Should stage-2 expansions ship in beta.1 or wait on the recorded revive triggers (discovery recall / reading triage measurably suffering)? Only the owner can weigh that against the retention-experiment framing.

**Skeptic corrections:** (1) Entry-set swap not far enough: R-15 explicitly governs "provider-roster narrowing" (S6.4), but the re-exam adjudicated S9.11 (which R-15 never names) and handed S6.4 to "R-13 and R-17." R-17 covers only the S2 leg; S6.4's verifier-confirmed unadjudicated leg — the cross-provider DOI-deduped reference-union drop (adjudication S06.md S6.4 verifier notes: "No cited location adjudicates that leg"; gap report L73) — involves Crossref references and is neither topics (R-13) nor S2 (R-17). Under R-15's own frame it is stage-2 raw material (edge recall feeds snowball's occurrence-count ranking, design s7 L729-733). Add a fourth amendment: amend S6.4's already-mandated RECORD text with the stage vocabulary plus the Culbert et al. 2025 single-source evidence (info-flow L184 and the "single enrichment backbone" adopt verdict) — otherwise the distinction the re-exam warns about is lost on exactly the entry with the confirmed recording hole. (2) Design-change text error: "the verbatim payloads store retains each provider's full response so later stage-2 distillation (topic facets, additional providers) needs no re-fetch" is false for additional providers — S2/scite signals (TLDR, SPECTER, intents) were never fetched and are not in payloads; scope the no-re-fetch claim to already-admitted providers' stored responses. (3) The proposed stage-2 goal sentence ("metadata that helps the researcher find knowledge inside and outside the catalog") writes an uncharted goal into s7 while the re-exam's own open question (1) leaves charter scope undecided; word it descriptively — "beta.1 ships stage 2 as bounded citation-graph discovery per the amended exclusion (requirements L84)" — and cite the corpus's own avoid verdict on additional enrichment providers (info-flow "Do not add PubMed/Europe PMC, Dimensions, or OpenCitations," stage Discovery, verdict avoid), which is affirmative evidence against reading "discovery-maximum" as a beta.1 requirement.

### R-17 — Semantic Scholar belongs in the provider roster

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The only empirical spike ever run on the researcher's real library (ADR-30, alpha.1, 867 entries) is pro-S2 evidence: reference lists were 151/129/146 across S2/OpenAlex/Crossref — each provider incomplete — and S2 uniquely supplied intents/TLDRs/embeddings in the shipped co-primary merge validated live at the G10 gate (history L518-527). Beta.1's own evidence base repeatedly reaches adopt/adapt verdicts that S2 would satisfy: the abstract fallback chain names S2 as tier 3 (info-flow-research L240, verdict adopt), the discovery section names OpenAlex and S2 as "the two allowlisted discovery providers" with S2's Recommendations API as a hosted implementation of the evidence-backed seed±negative-list pattern (L852-855, verdict adopt; Scholar Inbox retention data L813-814), and the S2-specific row is adapt, not avoid (L204-207). For the R-15 stage-2 goal (maximum metadata to power discovery), S2 has two concrete beta.1 consumers: free TLDR lines on snowball-digest candidates and the citation monitor (reading triage at $0, attacking exactly the per-item friction the retention experiment measures) and a fuller reference set raising snowball recall. Finally, beta.1 silently reversed an explicit alpha.15 ADR-129 promotion (history L2142): S2/SPECTER/TLDR/scite have zero hits in the governing design, the deferral lives only in a non-authoritative lens doc (S9.14, adjudication/S09.md L134-136) — exactly the silent-divergence failure the name-every-divergence discipline exists to prevent.

**For beta.1:** The charter is the spec and no row requires any S2 signal; the one S2 capability with real product pull — recommendations — is explicitly excluded ("open-ended search and recommender feeds remain out," requirements L84), and §7's bounded discovery is deliberately "visible arithmetic, never a black-box recommender — that is the echo-chamber counter" (design L730-731, on Horbach et al. echo-chamber evidence, research L832-835). Two of S2's four unique offers have no beta.1 consumer at all: SPECTER contradicts the charter's hash-pinned installer-bundled local-model trust row (requirements L78; design L751-756) and the offline row, and the research rejects SPECTER-class ML at personal-corpus scale (L409); citation-intent candidates fed alpha's corpus-wide tension engine, which beta.1 deliberately keeps dead (S6.2; NLI-only within the retrieved set, design §8) — and intent labels are documented noisy (research L328, L779-780). The reference-union premise has weakened: Culbert et al. 2025 shows post-Walden OpenAlex reference coverage competitive with WoS/Scopus (L184, L288), and residual incompleteness is disclosed via index-relative cap-stamped wording rather than merged away. Operationally S2 is now a degradable tertiary: 1 RPS keys, free-email key requests refused since Aug 2024 — the beta.1 researcher is on gmail and likely cannot get a key at all — keys pruned after 60 days idle, Springer abstracts withheld, the unauthenticated pool globally throttled (L206). And the ADR-129 promotion beta.1 reverses was never earned by a documented failure or measured benefit — its recorded rationale is one posture line ("proposers, never authorities," history L2142), while the alpha line actually carried S2 deferred through alpha.12-14 (history L1864, L1892).

**Decision:** The verdict turns on what S2 would actually power in beta.1, consumer by consumer. (1) Recommendations: charter-excluded (requirements L84) and structurally counter to §7's transparent-arithmetic discovery — out unless the owner amends the charter. (2) SPECTER embeddings: no consumer; the vec store is built from a hash-pinned, installer-bundled local model as a charter trust requirement (L78) that API-served vectors cannot satisfy, and search must work offline. (3) Citation intent: its alpha consumer (Tier-0 contradiction candidates feeding the tension engine) does not exist in beta.1 — the contradiction pipeline is deliberately local-NLI-within-retrieved-set only, and the docs-bar keeps the full engine dead. (4) That leaves TLDR triage lines on discovery/monitor notes and extra reference edges for snowball recall — both real, both unproven for this researcher, and both exactly what the recorded revive trigger tests ("discovery recall or reading triage measurably suffers without TLDRs/recommendations," info-flow-design L110). For an unproven, key-gated provider — where the beta.1 subject's gmail address likely cannot obtain a key at all under the Aug-2024 policy (research L206) — deferred-with-a-falsifiable-trigger is the correct beta.1 disposition, on the same evidence-shaped grounds that kept PubMed/Dimensions/OpenCitations out (research L261-263). The owner's API-quality prior is therefore right about the API and wrong about the roster: the API's value class survives, but as the named first-in-line post-beta expansion, and that status must live in the authoritative design, not a lens doc. Two aspects of the position are upheld: (a) the deferral must be durably recorded with priority and the trigger must be decidable from beta.1 event data (small §7 logging addition), and (b) the reference-incompleteness leg (S6.4's unadjudicated single-source delta) needs a recorded escalation ladder whose first rung is a DOI-deduped union across the two providers already allowlisted — Crossref deposited references have been open via the free REST API since 2022 (research L197) — so ADR-30's lesson gets a zero-new-egress response path before any S2 revival. Roster membership itself is rejected; all three entries stay RECORD with amended recording text.

**History:** (1) alpha.1 ADR-30: S2+OpenAlex co-primary with Crossref, per-field best-source-wins with provenance; intents/tldr/embedding sourced from S2; references a DOI-deduped union — earned by two red-team rounds plus the 867-entry spike (reference counts 151/129/146 for one paper; ORCID in OpenAlex, ~0 in S2); single-source (S2-only) explicitly rejected on the spike; shipped and validated live at the G10 gate (design-history L515-527). (2) alpha.12 CLI-first reset: docs updated so enrichment "calls Crossref, OpenAlex, and Unpaywall" with Semantic Scholar/PubMed marked deferred (L1892); the alpha.13-era deferred-work list likewise carries "Semantic Scholar, PubMed, arXiv…" (L1864). (3) alpha.13 design §0 names S2 among six enrichment providers (L2262, L2314) but implementation stayed deferred. (4) alpha.15 ADR-129: S2 promoted to conditional default-on-when-keyed (reference union, citation intents as free Tier-0 contradiction candidates, TLDRs, SPECTER; never promotion-required), scite.ai optional opt-in; recorded why is the posture line "Like every provider and judge: proposers, never authorities" (L2142) — a capability expansion, not a position earned by documented failure or measured benefit. (5) Beta.1 evidence base: S2 is now operationally a "degradable tertiary" — 1 RPS keys, free-email key requests refused since Aug 2024, 60-day key pruning, Springer abstracts withheld (info-flow-research L184, L204-207); scite API ≈12x the entire monthly budget and proprietary → link-out forever (L209-211, info-flow-design L276, L288); Culbert et al. 2025 shows OpenAlex reference coverage now competitive, weakening the 2023-era union premise (L184, L288); yet the research adopts S2 in the abstract fallback chain (L240) and as the second discovery provider via its Recommendations API (L852-855) — resolved the other way by design §17 #4 and the charter's amended discovery exclusion. (6) The deferral-with-revive-trigger exists only in the lens doc (info-flow-design L110, L266): the governing design has zero hits for Semantic Scholar/scite/SPECTER/TLDR, confirming S9.14's silence finding.

**Entry amendments:**
- S6.4: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — with amended recording text — Extend the entry's s11 recording of the single-source reference-edge leg with a recorded escalation ladder: if snowball recall measurably suffers, the first response is a DOI-deduped reference union across the two providers already allowlisted (Crossref deposited references are open via the free REST API since 2022 — zero new egress surface), and only after that a Semantic Scholar revival — so ADR-30's each-provider-incomplete lesson has a named response path, not only honest cap-stamped labeling.
- S9.9: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — unchanged — R-17 does not disturb this entry: none of its providers is Semantic Scholar, and each narrowing (arXiv-via-DataCite, SWH/NCBI deferral, ORCID/ROR/ISBN silence) stands or falls on the entry's own existing recording action, which already covers the verifier's gaps.
- S9.14: RECORD — sound but unrecorded → RECORD — with amended recording text — Adopt the verifier's split-provider recording (S2 deferred as the first named post-beta enrichment expansion with the revive trigger; scite.ai rejected permanently — link-out only, ~12x-budget evidence) and add one sentence instrumenting the trigger: log per-candidate summary/abstract availability on discovery-digest and citation-monitor notes so 'discovery recall or reading triage measurably suffers without TLDRs' is decidable from beta.1 event data rather than impression.

**Design change (if adopted):** Three minimal edits. (1) design.md §10, deferred-named-entries line (L902-903): add `api.semanticscholar.org` alongside arxiv.org/europepmc.org, Software Heritage, NCBI. (2) design.md §11: add the divergence bullet in the S9.14 verifier's corrected wording — "Semantic Scholar (alpha.15 ADR-129: conditional default-on-when-keyed — reference union, citation-intent contradiction candidates, TLDRs, SPECTER) is deferred, not shipped — beta.1 enrichment is OpenAlex plus Crossref (retraction + title fallback). Revive as a named allowlist entry with its own audit — the first post-beta enrichment expansion — if discovery recall or reading triage measurably suffers without TLDRs/recommendations; if the shortfall is reference recall specifically, the first response is a DOI-deduped union across the already-allowlisted OpenAlex+Crossref (zero new egress) before any new provider. scite.ai (ADR-129: optional opt-in) is rejected, not deferred — link-out only, no revive trigger, on cost evidence (~12x budget)." (3) design.md §7, Discovery (snowball digest note, ~L732-737): one sentence — each candidate line records whether a one-line summary/abstract was available (present | absent-in-source | not-yet-fetched) and the run's PRISMA-S event line carries the count, making the S2 revive trigger decidable from logged data.

**Open questions (owner):** (1) Key feasibility, decisive for any revival: can the owner actually obtain and sustain an S2 API key (free-email key requests refused since Aug 2024; the beta.1 researcher's address is gmail; keys idle 60 days are pruned)? An institutional key materially weakens the operational counter-argument and could lower the revive threshold. (2) Charter scope: does the owner consider a seed-list-driven, capped, provenance-stamped recommendation digest (S2 Recommendations API with researcher-controlled positive/negative lists — the pattern the info-flow research adopted at L805-820 and L852-855 with Scholar Inbox retention evidence) an excluded 'recommender feed' or admissible bounded discovery? Beta.1 resolved it as excluded on echo-chamber evidence; only the owner can amend the charter if it under-scopes stage-2 discovery here. (3) If R-15's two-stage enrichment is ruled into beta.1 scope itself (not post-beta), which single S2 consumer justifies the roster slot first — TLDR triage lines or the reference union — given that the union has a zero-new-egress alternative on the existing roster?

**Skeptic corrections:** (1) Overweighted operational counter: research L207 — the note on the very adapt entry the verdict cites (L204-207) — already prescribes a keyless path (opportunistic unauthenticated /paper/batch, mandatory backoff, degrade-to-absent), so "the gmail researcher likely cannot obtain a key at all" is not itself a roster barrier and open question (1) should note that keyless degraded use is the research's contemplated mode; the verdict should rest, as its consumer analysis already does, on the requirement-driven allowlist ground alone. (2) Undisposed fifth consumer: the reasoning never resolves the adopted abstract fallback chain naming S2 as tier 3 (research L240-242; carried at info-flow-design L114) that its own argument_for raised — the §11 divergence bullet should name the abstract-tier loss (degrades to OpenAlex→Crossref→local-PDF with absence-as-absence; Springer abstracts withheld from S2 regardless, L206) under the same revive trigger. (3) Missed strengthening evidence: gap report L73 shows alpha.15's shipped providers.yaml carried S2 as deferred — ADR-129 was never realized live — so beta.1 reverses only a paper promotion and is continuous with the last shipped roster state; worth adding to the §11 recording text. (4) Citation nits: research L328 is an adapt verdict proposing a reading-triage consumer for intents (guided-reading queue), not merely noisiness evidence — cite it as a proposed consumer beta.1 also lacks; L832-835's avoid condemns graph-similarity-only as the *sole* channel, so "never a black-box recommender" should be attributed to design L730-731's recorded stance plus charter L84, not to the Horbach evidence directly; history L1892 sits in the alpha.13 section (L1838+), not alpha.12.

### R-19 — Did beta.1 lose the 2PL/ACID design?

**Verdict: PARTIAL** · survived opposite-side skeptic

**For the position:** The alpha line built a hard-won transactional discipline over two releases and beta.1's s6 does not visibly restate all of it. Alpha.12's cross-store materialization protocol was forced by a FAILED crash-replay spike ("hashes alone are insufficient" — history L1790), and alpha.15 ADR-127 paid ADR-22's owned-durability debt in full: 2PC journal states pending->materialized with the commit SHA recorded after git commit, write-ahead fsync ordering, one workspace-scoped write lock, crash-at-any-boundary recovery via `workspace recover`, WAL + synchronous=FULL (history L2128). Beta.1 s6 (L446-510) defines rollback only for the verify-mismatch path and revert; nothing in the design (grep: crash/recover across all 1353 lines) says what happens when the daemon dies between apply and commit — partially applied machine blocks sit uncommitted with no manifest rows and no named recovery step. Worse, the one rollback s6 does define is `git reset --hard pre/r_...` (L475), a whole-worktree reset that would destroy human keystrokes made anywhere in the vault during the run — a blast radius alpha's per-output journal-cascade rollback unit (history L1796) never had, and a direct contradiction of s6's own "Atomicity protects the safety property (no human text altered)" (L486-487).

**For beta.1:** The premise as stated is unconfirmed: no 2PL (two-phase locking) design ever existed — greps for 2PL/two-phase-lock/ACID over the 557KB history return zero hits (the only "two-phase" is a rsync deploy, L855); concurrency was always serialization (alpha.5 per-citekey board-serialized writes, L525; alpha.15's single workspace write lock, L2128), and beta.1 keeps a stronger structural form: one JobRunner, VaultWriter as sole machine writer, engines staging-only, per-file locks + quiesce + stale-base skip-and-requeue (s2 L138-168, s6 L460-471) — which additionally protects concurrent human typing, something alpha's lock never addressed. The 2PC's motivating premise is dissolved by a recorded decision: ADR-127 needed cross-store atomic pairing because the DB was authoritative and "deliberately not file-recoverable" (L2130); beta.1's two-class split (s5 L429-444) makes every derived table re-derivable from post-revert files with fail-closed amber re-earn, so reconciliation replaces replay ("Revert is DB-complete via reconciliation, not snapshots", s6 L501-510, with the write-amplification rationale stated). ACID-at-the-DB survives (WAL, transactional, s5 L361-363; delete-then-insert in one transaction so "a crash leaves the old index intact", s8 L757-758), pathspec commit hygiene survives (s6 L477-480), the durable-envelope/idempotency function survives (s2 L170-176), and the dedicated regression review swept "cross-store recoverability / observable atomicity with paired rollback" and "request-envelope integrity fields" as present or strengthened (regression-review L74, L77). S13.3/S13.4 adjudicated exactly this delta LEAVE with citation-audited high confidence.

**Decision:** Decisive considerations. (1) Premise: the owner's "2PL/ACID" names something the corpus never contained as locking theory; what the alpha line actually earned — via a failed spike (L1790) and ADR-127 (L2128) — was cross-store 2PC with crash recovery, plus DB-level ACID. So the question properly becomes: does beta.1's run protocol cover the 2PC contract's function? (2) Mostly yes, by premise-dissolution, not by omission: cross-store atomic pairing existed to protect an authoritative, not-file-recoverable DB; beta.1's two-class split (derived = regenerable fail-closed, ledgers = append-only observational, exported) removes the object of protection, and this is recorded with rationale in s6 L501-510 and s5 L429-444, independently confirmed by the citation-audited S13.3/S13.4 adjudications and the regression review's intact sweep (L74). Serialization, DB transactions, pathspec commit hygiene, idempotent durable jobs, and the fail-closed read barrier all survive at named locations. The already-booked RECORD actions on S13.8 (tiered replay drop) and S13.9 (hash-chain/journal-head drop) correctly absorb the tamper-evidence and replay halves of the owner's concern. (3) Two legs are genuinely not covered and are upheld: (a) ADR-127's crash-at-any-boundary recovery has no beta.1 analog — s6's protocol handles verify-mismatch and revert but is silent on daemon death mid-run; detection exists (stale heartbeat, s2 L174-176) but the response is unstated; (b) the only defined rollback is whole-tree `git reset --hard`, which can clobber concurrent human edits in non-footprint files — a regression versus alpha's per-output rollback unit and versus s6's own safety property (L486). Both are fixable with existing machinery (pre-tag, per-file dry-run classes, conflict diversion, reconciliation, idempotency keys, incidents) in a few sentences, so the amendment is narrow: S13.3 flips to CHANGE scoped to those two legs; the replacement architecture itself stands.

**History:** (a) No 2PL/ACID vocabulary exists anywhere in the design history: greps for "2PL", "two-phase lock", "ACID" over memoria-design-history-alpha.1-to-alpha.15.md return zero hits; the sole "two-phase" match is a two-phase rsync deploy (L855, unrelated). (b) Concurrency was serialization, never a lock protocol: alpha.5 ADR-30 "find-or-create is idempotent only under serialized writes", board-dispatched per-citekey lock (L525); alpha.15 "one workspace-scoped write lock per operation" (L2128). (c) The real transactional design: alpha.12 SQLite state boundary (L1766-1796) — write-boundary constraints "inside the same worker transaction" (L1784); durable request envelope with idempotency_key UNIQUE (L1786); hash-chained append-only journal (L1788); cross-store materialization "Transactions: SQLite first, file promotion second" with durable payload bytes, forced by the FAILED crash-replay spike "hashes alone are insufficient" (L1790); recover_pending_materializations crash replay (L1792); consumable_outputs read barrier (L1794). (d) alpha.15 ADR-127 (L2122-2132): "Cross-store recoverability (observable atomicity): 2PC with journal states pending->materialized (materializing commit SHA recorded after git commit), write-ahead fsync ordering, one workspace-scoped write lock per operation, crash-at-any-boundary recovery via workspace recover; connections pinned WAL + synchronous=FULL" (L2128); pathspec-only commits, never git add -A, git-as-sole-history rejected because verdicts/records are "deliberately not file-recoverable" (L2130); recovery classes, DB loss fails closed, "No human-authored datum is ever in the accepted-loss class" (L2132); the arc summary: the DB gives "records, queues, and verdicts a transactional home markdown cannot provide" (L2310). (e) The rollback unit in alpha was per-output (journal cascade over derivations, L1796; gap report L154), never a whole-worktree reset.

**Entry amendments:**
- S13.3: leave → change — Uphold the git+VACUUM-INTO+reconciliation replacement but require s6 to close ADR-127's two uncovered legs: an explicit interrupted-run (crash-mid-batch) recovery rule, and footprint-limited rollback in place of whole-tree git reset --hard.
- S13.4: leave → leave — Stands — the DERIVED/OPERATIONAL taxonomy is recorded with rationale (s5 L429-444, s6 L505-510) and sharpens ADR-127's no-human-datum-accepted-loss invariant.
- S13.8: record → record — Stands — the existing action text (tiered replay honored structurally: restrictions in git-tracked frontmatter, permissions re-earn via fail-closed amber) answers the replay half of R-19.
- S13.9: record → record — Stands — the existing action text (DB journal-of-record gone, git commit chain is the tamper root per ADR-104's original posture) answers the tamper-evidence half of R-19.
- S13.1: leave → leave — Stands — not transactional machinery; unaffected by R-19.
- S13.2: record → record — Stands — runner transport; unaffected by R-19.
- S13.5: leave → leave — Stands — operation->run rename preserves the journaled, idempotent, revertible write-unit substance R-19 cares about.
- S13.6: leave → leave — Stands — migration posture; unaffected by R-19.
- S13.7: record → record — Stands — migrations ledger; unaffected by R-19.
- S13.10: leave → leave — Stands — per-device DB relocation preserves the durable-per-machine-home reason and protects WAL SQLite from file-sync corruption.
- design s6: batch protocol as written (whole-tree reset --hard on verify-mismatch; no interrupted-run path) → footprint-limited rollback + explicit interrupted-run recovery rule — Amend s6 per design_change; no architectural change, two additions reusing existing machinery.

**Design change (if adopted):** Two additions to design.md s6, both reusing machinery the design already has. (1) Footprint-limited rollback (edit step 3, L475): on manifest mismatch, restore pre/r_... state only for the run-footprint paths (git checkout pre/r_... -- &lt;footprint&gt; semantics), never a whole-worktree reset --hard; a footprint file carrying a later human edit diverts the restored content to &lt;name&gt;.conflict.md + incident, exactly as revert does (s6 L493-495). This preserves the incident semantics while honoring L486's "no human text altered" for concurrent edits outside the footprint. (2) Interrupted-run recovery (add after the partial-success rule, ~L489): on daemon start, any run left status=running with a stale heartbeat (s2 L174-176) and no run commit is recovered as a run: its footprint files are restored to the pre/r_... base per rule (1), its jobs are requeued by idempotency key, a footprint-scoped DB reconciliation is enqueued (same pass as revert, s6 L501-505), and incident INC-r_...-interrupted is logged. This is beta.1's answer to ADR-127's crash-at-any-boundary obligation (history L2128) — one named path, no 2PC reinstated, no per-run DB snapshots added.

**Open questions (owner):** (1) Whether the operational-ledger loss window (decide/cost/guard events since the last VACUUM INTO / weekly export) with no cryptographic root over ledgers is acceptable at N=1 scale — the S13.8/S13.9 record-actions assume yes; only the owner can endorse or escalate that to a design change. (2) Whether interrupted-run recovery should also be a user-facing command (a mem-recover / inspector-pane surface, ADR-127's workspace-recover shape) or remain automatic-on-daemon-start only. (3) Whether the owner intends "2PL/ACID" to demand anything beyond crash recovery and rollback precision — e.g. reinstating durable pre-apply payload storage so a crash after a paid LLM call never re-bills (alpha.12's materialization_payloads bought this; beta.1 retries re-pay at batch prices) — that is a cost/durability tradeoff the design currently leaves implicit.

**Skeptic corrections:** Three refinements, none refuting: (1) The argument_for's claim that "nothing in the design says what happens when the daemon dies between apply and commit" should cite and dispose of design L66-69 — "Work survives restarts... never half-write (all machine writes are staged, §6)" — which a grep for "restarts" surfaces; it covers only queue persistence and pre-apply staging, and its unbacked "never half-write" assertion actually strengthens the CHANGE (the design claims a property s6 does not deliver on daemon death mid-apply). Add the concrete failure mode the re-examination missed: s6 L479's next-run pre-tag commit-all sweeps half-applied machine blocks into a commit with no Mem-Run trailer, making them unrevertible-by-run. (2) Anchor both upheld legs in the charter rather than alpha comparison, per the ADRs-are-reference ground rule: leg (b) violates Trust L72 ("Machines never overwrite or delete human-authored text; a violation stops the beta immediately"); leg (a) violates Review L33 ("reversible by run") and Operations Failure-handling L66 (failures must name the data state). This makes the S13.3 CHANGE stand without any appeal to ADR-127. (3) Open question 3 overstates re-billing: s18 R3 / s5 L434-436 already give a content-addressed payloads store making enrichment merges replayable; narrow the question to digest-class LLM outputs, which alone lack durable pre-apply payloads.
